rOR  ALUMNI  OF  NICHOLS  JUNIOR  COLLEGE

1939  -  1943

World  War  II  wrote  finis  to  the  opening  chapter  of  the  history  of  Nichols
Junior  College.  The  twelve  years  from  1931  to  1943  were  years  of  pioneering  and  de¬
velopment.  They  were  the  years  when  growth  in  terms  of  numbers  of  students,  of
expanding  physical  plant  and  of  improved  facilities  was  steady  and  sure.  They  were
the  years  when  a  new  idea — a  two-year  collegiate  curriculum  in  business  administration
—  was  finding  its  place  in  New  England  education.

Human  institutions  are  as  subject  to  human  frailty  as  they  are  to  human
greatness.  From  the  United  Nations  to  the  youngest  den  of  Cub  Scouts  the  basic
problem  is  to  learn  to  work  together  in  the  pursuit  of  a  goal.  The  effective  techniques
for  co-operative  effort  are  different  for  every  organization.  They  must  be  developed
by  its  members  and  adjusted  to  its  growth.  This  is  a  slow  process  at  best,  but  we  who
watched  it  and  participated  in  it  at  Nichols  were  confident  that  each  unit — sutdent  body
and  faculty,  Justinians  and  Dorm  Council,  Administration,  Trustees  and  Advisory
Council — was  finding  with  increasing  certainty  of  success  its  unique  contribution.  The
years  from  1931  1943  were  also  years  of  learning.

In  a  sense  the  climax  of  these  years  was  Nichols’  contribution  to  the  War.
The  opening  chapter,  the  story  of  the  twelve  peace  time  years,  is  written  down  in  other
“Ledgers”  and  in  the  “Budget.”  Here  is  the  man-by-man  account  of  Nichols’  sons  at
war.

It  is  a  good  story.  It  is  in  most  instances  an  overly  modest  story.  And,
incomplete  though  it  may  be,  it  says  certain  things  clearly  and  unmistakeable.  The
part  these  three  hundred  odd*  alumni  and  faculty  played  is  certainly  proportionately
the  equal  of  any  college  group.

Nichols’  men  went  to  war:

For  the  Army  227

For  the  Navy  69

For  the  Marine  Corps  8

For  the  Coast  Guard  6

For  the  American  Field  Service  4

Total  314

*  Based  upon  data  collected  in  1944-45.

This  is  eighty-three  per  cent  of  those  replying  to  our  questionnaire.  Of  this

number:

28.7  per  cent  were  enlisted  men

36.8  per  cent  were  non-commissioned  officers
34.5  per  cent  were  commissioned  officers

Because  much  of  the  data  were  gathered  nearly  a  year  before  V-E  day,  all
figures  are  tentative  and  it  would  be  unfair  and  misleading  to  enumerate  decorations
and  other  honors.  But  as  early  as  the  fall  of  1944  Bronze  and  Silver  stars  and  Purple
Hearts  were  being  awarded.  Nichols  men  not  only  did  their  jobs,  they  did  them  in  a
manner  which  was  “in  keeping  with  the  highest  traditions  of  the  service.”

Finally,  this  record  tells  us  that  the  institution  which  had  a  part  in  the
development  of  these  men  has  proved  its  worth.  It  should  continue,  grow  and  pursue
its  destiny.  Those  of  us — students  and  teachers — who  no  longer  are  active  participants
wish  it  a  sincere  “God  Speed.”

W.  G.  S.

Cambridge,  Mass.

November,  1946

SPONSORS

E.  S.  BUCKE
F.  X.  DAY

GEORGE  BOYER,  ’32

Class  of  1932

GEORGE  H.  ROYER

George  was  born  on  F ebruary  1 ,  1912  and  prepared  for
college  at  Yonkers  (New  York)  High  School  of
Commerce.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1931  to  1932.
His  permanent  address  is  140  Elm  Street,  Cambridge
40,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

Reporter,  Webster  Times,  Webster,  Massachusetts,  from  June,  1932  to  May,  1933;
editor  and  publisher,  Weekly  World,  Pascoag,  Rhode  Island,  May  to  November,  1933.
Sales  Department,  Kraft  Cheese  Co.,  November,  1933  to  April,  1937,  working  through
New  England  and  New  York  State.  Advertising  Department,  Kraft  Cheese  Company,
Chicago,  from  April,  1937  to  July,  1943.  Immediately  before  returning  to  Boston,
MAR  account  executive  handling  the  Mars  candy  account  for  Grant  Advertising  Agency  in

I  |  -  f  |  Chicago.  At  present  in  charge  of  radio  advertising  for  Alley  &  Richards  Company,  Bos¬

ton  and  New  York  advertising  agency.  Family:  Married  Mary  E.  Hayward  of  Cam¬
bridge,  Massachusetts,  October  4,  1936.  Two  children,  Mary  L.,  born  in  Evanston,
Illinois,  May  24,  1938;  and  Ruth  H.,  also  born  at  Evanston,  January  6,  1943.  Hobby:
Photography.  Active  in  Chicago  Camera  Club  circles,  salon  exhibitor,  and  has  written
several  articles  for  photographic  magazines.

ROBERT  STEPHEN  HAYES

Robert  was  born  on  July  17,  1912  and  prepared  for
college  at  Worcester  Academy,  Worcester,  Massa¬
chusetts.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1931  to  1932.
His  permanent  address  is  267  Gibbs  Avenue,  Newport,
Rhode  Island.  His  temporary  address  is  Cpl.  R.  S.
Hayes,  11004075,  5th  Fighter  Squadron,  52nd  Fighter
Group,  APO  520,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Salesman,  Newport  Coal  Co.,  Newport,  Rhode  Island.  Insurance,  representing  the
Employers’  Group,  Rhode  Island  Department.  March  30,  1942,  enlisted  in  Army
Quartermaster’s  Corps  at  Fort  Devens.  Transferred  to  Army  Air  Corps  Personnel
Division.  August,  1942,  arrived  in  England.  October,  1942,  landed  in  Africa,  during
Tunisian  Campaign.  Promoted  to  Corporal  at  Oran.  Transferred  to  Squadron  Supply
Corps.  May  11,  1943,  cited  for  outstanding  service  in  Africa.  August,  1943,  Sicily.
December,  1943,  Corsica.  May,  1943,  Italy.  July,  1943,  Rome.  Awarded  three
Bronze  Stars.

GORDON  C.  LESLIE

Gordon  was  born  on  May  27,  1911  and  prepared  for
college  at  Nashua  High  School  and  New  Hampton
Prep.  School.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1931  to
1932.  His  permanent  address  is  12  Auburn  Street,
Nashua,  New  Hampshire.  His  temporary  address  is
Camp  Peary,  Virginia.

Since  his  college  days:

Immediately  after  graduation  entered  employ  of  the  Standard  Oil  Company,  managing
stations  in  Nashua  and  Rochester,  New  Hampshire.  Later  was  employed  as  Salesman
for  the  General  Ice  Cream  Company  covering  territory  in  and  around  Boston,  Massa¬
chusetts.  Went  to  Miami,  Florida,  in  1940,  to  manage  a  station  for  the  Gulf  Oil  Company.

For  two  years  prior  to  entering  the  Service  was  employed  by  the  Engineering  Division  of
E.  I.  Dupont  Corporation  as  Cashier  and  Assistant  Office  Manager,  at  Louisville,  ^  A I
Kentucky.  He  is  now  a  Storekeeper  in  the  U.  S.  Navy,  stationed  at  Camp  Peary,  Vir-  LCDLEL
ginia.  Is  married  and  has  one  daughter.

SANFORD  GRANGER  MILLER

Sanford  was  born  on  February  8,  1913  and  prepared
for  college  at  Westfield  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1931  to  1932.  His  permanent  address
is  197  Granville  Road,  Westfield,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  197  Granville  Road,  West-
field,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

September,  1933,  entered  Bay  Path  Institute,  graduated  July,  1934.  Active  in  baseball
and  basketball.  Employed  by  General  Electric  Co.,  Schenectady,  New  York  in  August,
1934,  for  secretarial  work  in  Credit  and  Collection  Department;  transferred  to  Major
Payroll  Division,  1935,  in  charge  of  extra  compensation.  Completed  Business  Training
Course.  Played  basketball  for  the  Y.M.C.A.  and  professionally  for  Schenectady.
Entered  Set-up  Paper  Box  business  in  October,  1936,  as  vice-president  of  Miller  Paper
Box  Co.,  Holyoke,  Massachusetts.  Appointed  treasurer  and  general  manager  in  1938.
Married  January  20,  1940.  Sports— Summer :  golf  and  swimming.  Winter:  basketball
and  handball.  Civic  Activities:  Member  of  United  Commercial  Travelers  of  America,
Westfield  Kiwanis  Club,  Springfield  Y.  M.  C.  A.,  Holyoke  Industrial  Association.

HENRY  BENJAMIN  ROGERS

Henry  was  born  on  June  12,  1911  and  prepared  for
college  at  Norwalk  High  and  Hoosac,  New  York.
He  attended  Nichols  from  1931  to  1932.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  15  Park  Street,  Norwalk,  Connecticut
His  temporary  address  is  Fairfield  State  Hospital,
Newtown,  Connecticut.

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduating  from  Nichols,  Ben  remained  for  some  months  working  at  the  College.
In  the  Fall  of  1933  he  married  Mary  I.  Waterhouse  of  Webster.  They  have  one  daughter.
They  lived  in  Norwalk,  Connecticut,  for  four  years  where  he  worked  for  Sears,  Roebuck
&  Co.,  and  the  Hat  Corporation  of  America.  Shortly  after  coming  to  Norwalk  he  be¬
came  aware  of  physical  disability,  what  is  known  as  “multiple  sclerosis”  and  after  four
years  of  progressive  difficulty  he  was  obliged  to  give  up  work;  and  since  March  of  1943
has  been  in  the  hospital,  recently  recovering  from  diphtheria  and  pneumonia.  As  he  is
so  physically  handicapped,  his  greatest  pleasure  is  in  correspondence  with  old  friends,
and  his  best  wishes  go  to  old  classmates  of  Nichols.

Class  of  1933

iv

JOHN  F.  BALDWIN,  JK.

John  was  born  on  February  25,  1913  and  prepared  for
college  at  Classical  High  School,  Springfield,  Massa¬
chusetts.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1931  to  1933.
His  permanent  address  is  Box  133,  North  Wilbraham,
Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

Just  returned  from  overseas  and  expects  to  be  at  the  following  address  until  after  the
new  year.  Sgt.  John  F.  Baldwin,  Jr.,  0552183,  Hq.  H.C.T.G.,  Water  Tr.  Branch  F.  S.
343,  Camp  Gordon  Johnston,  Florida.

HAL

LEDGER

ROBERT  LAWRENCE  FICKETT

Robert  was  born  on  October  8,  1911  and  prepared  for
college  at  Concord  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1931  to  1932.  His  permanent  address  is  27  Rum-
ford  Street,  Concord,  New  Hampshire.  His  tem¬
porary  address  is  293d  Ordnance  (MM)  Co.,  APO
339,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  leaving  Nichols,  Bob  went  in  his  father’s  store  to  learn  the  watchmaking  and
jewelry  business.  In  1937  he  married  Dorothy  L.  Riford.  In  1939  he  was  made  co¬
owner  of  W.  L.  Fickett  &  Co.  Bob  was  inducted  in  the  Army  and  on  June  21st  he  went
to  Fort  Devens.  He  was  assigned  to  the  293d  Ordnance  (MM)  Co.  as  watchmaker  with
the  instrument  department.  He  received  his  training  at  Fort  Devens,  Washington,
D.C.,  AP  Hill,  Virginia,  and  back  to  Devens.  In  January,  1944,  he  received  a  rating
of  Staff  Sergeant.  He  left  for  overseas  in  February  and  has  been  stationed  in  England,
France  and  is  now  in  Belgium  with  the  same  Company  as  assistant  section  chief  in  the
instrument  department.

DWIGHT  K.  HAGGERTY

Dwight  was  born  on  January  22,  1914  and  prepared
for  college  at  Staunton  Military  Academy  and
Bartlett  High  School,  Webster,  Massachusetts.  He
attended  Nichols  from  September,  1931  to  June,  1933.
His  permanent  address  is  13  Prospect  Street,  Webster,
Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

Bus  driver,  machinist,  assistant  dyer,  American  Woolen  Co.  Married,  Elaine  Hogan,
Southbridge,  1937.  Son,  Michael,  1938;  Daughter,  Ellen,  1940.  Civilian  Defense  Leader,
Scoutmaster,  Sergeant,  Massachusetts  State  Guards.  Blood  Donor  four  so  far.

I fDGEt

HOWARD  H.  HALLOCK

Howard  was  born  on  August  25,  1912  and  prepared
for  college  at  Danbury,  Connecticut.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1931  to  1933.  His  permanent  address  is
106  Maynard  Street,  Springfield,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  816  Q.  M.  Stea.  Co.,  A.P.O.
758,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Salesman,  Coan  Products  Refining  Co.  Married,  three  children.  Entered  Army  in
1941  as  Second  Lieutenant  in  Q.M.  Reserve.  Served  in  North  Africa,  Sicily,  Italy  and
France  and  is  now  a  Captain.

CLARENCE  MORTON  INGRAHAM

Clarence  was  born  on  September  12,  1911  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  The  Choate  School  and  New
Hampton.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1931  to  1933.
His  permanent  address  is  Home:  298  Center  Street,
Bristol,  Connecticut.  Business:  The  E.  Ingraham
Co.,  Bristol,  Connecticut.

Since  his  college  days:

Went  to  work  as  a  cost  accountant  doing  time  study  work  at  The  E.  Ingraham  Company,
manufacturers  of  clocks  and  watches.  Became  assistant  chief  accountant.  Director,
secretary  and  assistant  treasurer  of  said  Company.  Secretary  and  treasurer  of  the
Ingraham  Canadian  Clock  Co.  Ltd.  of  Toronto,  Canada.  Past  president  of  the  Bristol
WAE?  Rotary  Club.  Active  in  community  affairs.  Will  take  a  week’s  vacation  when  F.D.R.,

is  dethroned  one  way  or  the  other!  Favorite  sport  is  fishing,  also.  Married  1937  to
Mary- Jane  Fletcher  (no  hits,  no  runs,  no  errors).

WILLIAM  O.  KOHNKE

William  was  born  on  January  31,  1914  and  prepared
for  college  at  South  Side  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1931  to  1933.  His  permanent  address
is  17  Smith  Street,  Rockville  Centre,  New  York.
His  temporary  address  is  A.S.N.  32107302,  Co.  “C,”
36th  Engineers,  A.P.O.  758,  c/o  Postmaster,  New
York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduation  from  Nichols,  Bill  entered  New  York  University,  School  of  Commerce,
from  which  he  received  his  degree  of  Bachelor  of  Commercial  Science  in  Accounting  in
June,  1936.  Shortly  thereafter  he  was  employed  by  the  U.  S.  Rubber  Co.  at  its  New  York
office  in  the  Sales  Accounting  Department  and  in  1940  he  was  promoted  to  traveling
auditor  for  said  Company  covering  its  plants  in  Syracuse,  Chicago  and  Minneapolis.
On  March  17,  1941,  he  was  inducted  into  the  U.  S.  Army.  After  completing  his  training
at  Fort  Belvoir,  Virginia,  he  was  assigned  as  a  private  to  Co.  “C”  of  the  36th  Engineers
Corps  (Combat).  He  was  made  a  Corporal  in  August,  1941,  and  advanced  to  Sergeant
in  July,  1942,  which  rank  he  now  holds.  In  October,  1942,  he  left  for  overseas  service,
landing  in  French  Morocco  with  the  first  invasion  troops.  He  also  participated  in  the
landings  in  Sicily,  Salerno,  Anzio  Beachhead  and  in  Southern  France,  where,  to  the  best
of  our  knowledge,  he  is  still  stationed.  Bill  is  not  married.  The  above  photograph  was
taken  in  July,  1944,  “Somewhere  in  Italy.”

EDWARD  TOMLINSON

Edward  was  born  on  May  22,  1911  and  prepared  for
college  at  Hebron  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1931  to  1933.  His  permanent  address  is  20
Wood  Road,  Cape  Cottage,  Maine.

Since  his  college  days:

Graduated  Nichols  1933.  Went  to  work  at  Milliken  Tomlinson  Co.,  Wholesale  Grocers,
Portland,  Maine.  Various  positions  in  office  and  warehouse  for  two  years.  Made
office  manager  and  elected  to  board  of  directors  by  stockholders  in  1935.  Spent  all
spare  time  flying  from  1935  on,  much  of  which  was  done  in  the  interest  of  the  Company
and  its  branches  in  Presque  Isle,  Bangor  and  Lewiston,  Maine.  1938  made  manager
of  Institution  Department  and  remained  in  this  capacity  until  entering  U.  S.  Coast
Guard  in  October,  1941.  Was  placed  in  charge  of  Patrol  Boat  on  Anti-submarine  work
with  rank  of  Chief  Boatswain.  Was  released  from  Coast  Guard  in  October,  1942,  to
accept  rank  of  First  Lieutenant  in  Civil  Air  Patrol  flying  as  pilot  from  an  East  Coast
base  on  Anti-submarine  patrols  for  the  Army  and  Navy.  When  Civil  Air  Patrol  bases
were  disbanded  in  August,  1943,  he  returned  to  the  grocery  business  as  assistant  sales
manager.

WAD

LEDGER

Class  of  1934

GEORGE  G.  APPELL

George  was  born  on  June  1,  1941  and  prepared  for
college  at  New  Hampton.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1932  to  1934.  His  permanent  address  is  280
Park  Avenue,  New  York,  New  York.  His  temporary
address  is  Military  Intelligence  School,  Drawer  1004
A,  Yale  Sta.,  New  Haven,  Connecticut.

Since  his  college  days:

After  a  hitch  with  Gimbels  in  New  York,  went  to  Atlanta,  Georgia,  and  worked  on  The
Constitution;  came  north  again  in  1935  and  finished  out  the  year  with  Macy  Papers,  Inc.,
on  the  Mt.  Vernon  (New  York)  Daily  Argus.  During  1936  did  research  for  Chadbourne,
Wallace,  Parke  and  Whiteside,  New  York,  and  publicity  for  the  Democratic  National
Committee.  Went  to  England  free-lancing  in  1937  and  came  back  in  time  to  be  appointed
Deputy  U.  S.  Marshal,  District  of  Puerto  Rico.  In  1938,  went  to  Germany,  France,
Holland  and  Belgium  with  a  typewriter  and  sixty  dollars.  Came  back  in  1939  and  took
a  job  with  Air  Shopping,  New  York.  Was  advertising  manager  until  January  10,  1941,
when  the  bugle  blew.  Commissioned  1942,  wounded  1943  (Sicily),  home  in  1944,  but
expects  to  ship  again  shortly.  Married,  daughter,  dog.  Finally  got  published  (while  in
hospital)  in  Collier’s,  Argosy,  etc.

CECIL  DEXTER  BARNES

Cecil  was  born  on  March  28,  1914  and  prepared  for
college  at  Nashua  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1932  to  1934.  His  permanent  address  is  5
Courtland  Street,  Nashua,  New  Hampshire.

Since  his  college  days:

He  has  held  various  positions  with  different  concerns  in  Nashua  such  as:  payroll  clerk
at  Jackson  Mills,  clerk  in  Indian  Head  National  Bank  and  accountant  at  Benson’s
Animal  Farm.  He  entered  the  Nashua  Mills  of  the  Nashua  Manufacturing  Company
in  August,  1937,  working  in  the  various  departments  of  the  mill,  eventually  working
up  to  Assistant  Personnel  Manager,  which  position  he  has  now  held  since  March,  1942.
He  is  married  and  has  two  sons,  one  seven  and  the  other  two  years  old.  He  has  not  been
called  into  the  Service  as  his  job  is  in  a  concern  which  is  in  War  Work,  therefore  he  is
considered  essential.

EUGENE  E.  BICKFORD

Eugene  was  born  on  January  12,  1914  and  prepared
for  college  at  New  Hampton.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1932  to  1934.  His  permanent  address  is  2A
Pond  Street,  Hingham,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

In  the  fall  of  1934  after  graduating  from  Nichols  I  secured  a  position  with  the  Chase
Parker  wholesale  hardware  distributors  in  Boston,  Massachusetts,  and  remained  there
for  two  years.  In  1936  I  went  to  work  for  the  General  Electric  Co.  in  Bridgeport,  Con¬
necticut  and  after  a  year  of  training  in  the  Construction  Material  and  Power  Apparatus
Division  was  transferred  to  the  General  Electric  Supply  Corporation  in  Boston  with
whom  I  remained  until  June,  1942,  as  their  Southeastern  Massachusetts  representative.
In  1942  I  tried  to  enlist  in  the  service  but  was  rejected  for  physical  defects,  so  to  do  my  bit
for  the  war  effort  I  took  a  leave  of  absence  from  General  Electric  and  came  to  work  for
the  Bethlehem-Hingham  Shipyard,  and  have  remained  here  since  June,  1942.  I  was
married  in  1941  and  have  a  daughter  two  and  one-half  years  old.  I  am  the  town  con¬
stable,  member  of  the  Republican  town  committee  and  going  through  the  line  of  the  Old
Colony  Lodge  of  Masons.

PETER  DOYLE  DOLAN

Peter  was  born  on  June  23,  1913  and  prepared  for
college  at  Westminster  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1932  to  1934.  His  permanent  address  is  36
Whitman  Road,  Worcester,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  Lt.  Peter  D.  Dolan,  3d  Trans¬
portation  Zone,  307  Tower  Bldg.,  Baltimore,  Mary¬
land.

Since  his  college  days:

He  attended  Syracuse  University,  receiving  his  B.S.  degree  in  1936.  He  then  became
associated  with  General  Motors  Corp.  in  New  York  in  their  Export  Division.  He  was
one  of  their  Representatives  at  their  exhibit  at  the  World’s  Fair.  Until  he  entered  the
Service,  he  was  in  General  Motors  War  Office  in  Washington,  in  Transportation  work.
He  volunteered  in  the  U.  S.  Marine  Corps,  and  received  an  Honorable  Discharge  in
March,  1943.  In  June,  1943,  he  entered  the  U.  S.  Army  and  received  his  commission
in  New  Orleans  in  June,  1944.  He  is  now  a  Lieutenant  in  the  Army  Transportation
Corps,  at  present  assigned  to  Baltimore,  Maryland.

FRANCIS  LEON  DWYER

Francis  was  born  on  June  30,  1913  and  prepared  for
college  at  St.  Louis  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1932  to  1934.  His  permanent  address  is  52
Negus  Street,  Webster,  Massachusetts.  His  tem¬
porary  address  is  S/Sgt.  Francis  L.  Dwyer,  11052481,
A.P.O.  758,  1175h  Radio  Signal  Intelligence  Co.,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

HAC

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

Francis,  or  “Did,”  as  he  was  better  known  by  all  his  friends,  was  employed  at  the  Cran¬
ston  Print  Company  in  Webster.  Having  always  been  a  radio  “Ham,”  with  his  own
amateur  station,  when  war  broke  out  he  enlisted  in  Army  Radio  Intelligence,  entering
the  Army  as  a  private  on  May  25,  1942.  Promotions  came  fast,  since  he  was  well  ac¬
quainted  with  the  field  of  radio.  Thirty-five  days  later  he  was  promoted  to  Corporal,
two  months  later  earned  another  stripe,  and  not  long  after  that  was  made  Staff  Sergeant.
Was  stationed  at  Fort  Sam  Houston,  Texas,  for  nine  months,  where  he  taught  Morse
code,  radio  and  typing,  studied  Spanish  and  Japanese.  Went  overseas  March  1,  1943,
first  to  Africa,  then  Italy,  back  to  North  Africa  again,  Corsica,  and  then  France.  “Did”
is  a  bachelor.

WINFIELD  II .  EDWARDS

Winfield  was  born  on  July  30,  1913  and  prepared  for
college  at  Center  Moriches,  New  York,  High  School.
He  attended  Nichols  from  1932  to  1933.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  East  Moriches,  Long  Island,  New
York.  His  temporary  address  is  1st  Lt.  Winfield  H.
Edwards,  0-1633827,  Casual  Detachment  No.  0964C,
A.P.O.  17373,  c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,  Cali¬
fornia.

Since  his  college  days:

Married,  has  two  daughters.  Salesman,  selling  household  appliances,  later  sold  automo¬
biles  up  to  June  2,  1940,  when  he  entered  Army  (Signal  Corps).  Stationed  at  Mitchell
Field,  Long  Island;  then  Winsor  Locks,  Connecticut;  then  maneuvers,  North  Carolina;
then  Officers’ Training  School,  Fort  Monmouth,  New  Jersey;  after  that  he  taught  for
one  year  at  Fort  Monmouth;  then  special  Radio  course;  after  that,  Fort  Benning,  Geor¬
gia;  then  back  to  Fort  Monmouth  acting  as  Pace  and  Training  Officer;  then  nine  weeks
press  wireless,  Hicksville,  Long  Island,  special  course.

HAROLD  ALEXANDER  FRASER

Harold  was  born  on  May  3,  1914  and  prepared  for
college  at  Cushing  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1932  to  1934.  His  permanent  address  is  New
Boston,  New  Hampshire.  His  temporary  address  is
Italy.

Since  his  college  days:

Clerking  and  office  work  generally.  Is  not  married.  Enlisted  in  Air  Force,  December  22,
1941.  Trained  as  Mechanic  at  Keesler  Field,  Biloxi,  Mississippi;  at  Indianapolis,  Indiana,
and  Glendale,  California.  Arrived  in  England  June  5,  1942,  then  in  November  arrived
in  North  Africa,  landing  at  Oran.  Has  been  in  Sardinia  and  is  now  in  Italy,  at  present
he  is  in  Communications,  with  rank  of  Corporal.

WALTER  VINCENT  HAYES

Walter  was  born  on  August  21,  1914  and  prepared
for  college  at  Worcester  Academy,  Worcester,  Massa¬
chusetts.  He  attended  Nichols  from  September,
1932  to  June,  1934.  His  permanent  address  is  90
May  Street,  Newport,  Rhode  Island.  His  temporary
address  is  Sgt.  W.  V.  Hayes,  31247072,  64th  Finance
Disburse  Sec.,  APO  350,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Cashier,  Newport  Trust  Co.,  Newport,  Rhode  Island.  Chief  Cashier,  Savings  Depart¬
ment  Industrial  Trust  Co.,  Newport,  Rhode  Island.  January  5,  1943,  entered  U.  S.
Army  through  Selective  Service,  Fort  Devens,  Massachusetts.  Assigned  to  Finance
Training  Battalion,  Fort  Benjamin  Harrison,  Indiana.  June,  1943,  arrived  in  England.
Promoted  to  Corporal.  July,  1943,  promoted  to  Sergeant.  June,  1944,  landed  in  Nor¬
mandy.  Two  citations  and  two  bronze  stars.  Married  Arlene  Elizabeth  Welch,  Febru¬
ary  14,  1941.

PAUL  MARTENS,  JR.

for  college  at  Blair  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1932  to  1934.  His  permanent  address  is  7  Indian
Spring  Road,  Cranford,  New  Jersey.

Since  his  college  days:

Working  now  at  Eastern  Aircraft  Division  of  General  Motors  Corp.  in  Linden,  New  Jer¬
sey  in  Accounting  Department.  Married  and  has  two  children,  a  boy  two  years  and  a

AVAR

LEDGER

JOHN  CARROLL  MINAHAN

John  was  born  on  May  25,  1914  and  prepared  for
college  at  Haverhill  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1932  to  1934.  His  permanent  address
is  449  Main  Street,  Haverhill,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  Hdqs.  F.  E.  A.  F  (P),  APO  925,
c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Previous  to  his  enlistment  in  the  Air  Corps  he  was  employed  by  Eastern  Air  Lines.  He
enlisted  in  the  Air  Corps  in  1940  and  received  his  commission  as  Second  Lieutenant  at
Geiger  Field,  Spokane,  Washington,  in  September,  1941.  He  was  attached  to  the  19th
Heavy  Bombardment  Group  which  saw  action  in  Java  and  were  the  first  group  to  arrive
in  Australia.  As  bombardier  in  a  flying  fortress  he  was  decorated  by  Gen.  George  Kenney
with  the  silver  star  for  his  accurate  bombing  of  Rabaul.  He  also  has  the  air  medal
and  distinguished  flying  cross  with  oak  leaf  cluster.  After  being  relieved  of  combat  duty
he  was  promoted  to  Captain  and  was  stationed  in  Gen.  Kenney’s  headquarters  in  New
Guinea.  At  present  he  is  in  Far  Eastern  Air  Force  headquarters  in  Brisbane,  Australia.
In  1942  he  married  Miss  Mavis  Monahan  of  Melbourne,  Australia,  and  they  have  one
son.

KENNETH  C.  ORMSBY

Nichols  in  1934.  His  permanent  address  is  53  Eustis

c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Wholesale  Fruit.  Kenneth  is  in  the  Army  Air  Ground  service.

NELSON  ROBERT  SCOTT

Nelson  was  born  on  May  8,  1915  and  prepared  for
college  at  New  Hampton  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1932  to  1934.

Since  his  college  days:

Worked  for  the  Public  Service  Co.  in  Manchester,  New  Hampshire,  for  six  years.  Also
did  part  time  work  in  a  bakery.  Married  on  August  20,  1938.  One  daughter,  born
November  23,  1942.  Was  called  into  Service,  and  chose  U.S.M.C.  Entered  August  18,
1943.  Has  been  stationed  at  Parris  Island,  South  Carolina,  since  date  of  entrance.
Editor’s  note:  We  have  received  word  from  his  wife  that  Nelson  lost  his  life  May  13,  1945,
in  combat  duty  on  Okinawa.

cut.  Army  address  is  613th  A.A.F.B.U.,  Aberdeen

insurance.  In  1941  became  associated  with  the  Rowland  Insurance  Agency,  Inc.,
Waterbury,  Connecticut.  In  1937  was  married  to  the  former  Rita  St.  John  of  Nauga¬
tuck,  Connecticut,  and  has  two  daughters,  Susan,  Harriette  born  in  1938,  Robin  Curtin
born  in  1941.  Enlisted  in  Army  of  the  United  States  in  1942  and  at  present  is  a  Corporal

GEORGE  PRESCOTT  SHERMAN

George  was  born  on  May  6,  1914  and  prepared  for
college  at  Fairhaven  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1933  to  1934.  His  permanent  address  is
63  Laurel  Street,  Fairhaven,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  Co.  A,  565th  Sig.  A.  W.  Bn.,
A.P.O.  159,  c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,  California.

Salesman  for  Pairpoint  Corp.,  New  Bedford,  Massachusetts.  Acushnet  Process  Co.,

ROBERT  IN.  CAMPBELL

Robert  was  born  on  November  18,  1914  and  prepared
for  college  at  Columbia  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1934  to  1936.  His  permanent  address  is
9  Courter  Avenue,  Maplewood,  New  Jersey.  His
temporary  address  is  F/O  Robert  N.  Campbell,
T-120891,  316  Troop  Carrier  Group,  36  Troop  Carrier
Squadron,  A.P.O.  133,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,
New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduating  from  Nichols,  Bob  became  associated  with  the  Loyalty  Group  where  he
went  through  a  course  of  training  in  Fire,  Casualty,  and  Fidelity  insurance.  Subsequent¬
ly,  he  advanced  to  the  position  of  Special  Agent  for  Western  Pennsylvania,  making  his
headquarters  at  Pittsburgh,  Pennsylvania.  He  continued  in  this  capacity  until  Sunday,
December  7th,  when  the  news  of  the  attack  at  Pearl  Harbor  was  announced  over  the
radio.  He  then  enlisted  for  service.  After  training  in  Lubbock,  Texas;  Fort  Bragg,
North  Carolina,  he  went  overseas  as  a  Flight  Officer  in  the  Army  Air  Corps,  assigned  as
a  Glider  Pilot,  during  the  month  of  April,  1943.  He  saw  service  in  North  Africa  and
Sicily.  Then  he  returned  to  England  for  preparation  of  the  Normandy  invasion.  Was
returned  to  Italy  and  took  part  in  the  invasion  of  Southern  France,  after  which  he
returned  to  England  and  last  reports  indicate  he  is  still  stationed  in  England.

Editor's  note:  Bob  has  the  Air  Medal  with  cluster,  the  Distinguished  Unit  Badge  and
five  campaign  stars.

UAL  CHALMERS

Hal  was  born  on  January  16,  1913  and  prepared  for
college  at  New  Hampton  Preparatory  School.  He
attended  Nichols  from  1934  to  1936.  His  permanent
address  is  Dudley  Hill,  Dudley,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  c/o  Navy  V-12,  Dartmouth
College,  Hanover,  New  Hampshire.

Since  his  college  days:

Further  study  at  the  University  of  New  Hampshire.  Teacher-Coach  at  Nichols  Junior
College.  Chief  Petty  Officer,  U.S.N.R.  Enlisted,  September  4,  1942,  as  Physical
Instructor.  Has  been  stationed  in  Norfolk,  Virginia;  Bainbridge,  Maryland;  Pre-
Midshipman  School,  Portsmouth,  Virginia;  and  Dartmouth  College  under  the  V-12
Program.  Has  been  Assistant  Coach  of  Football  and  Baseball  at  Dartmouth.

JOHN  FLORAN  DARLING

John  was  born  on  December  15,  1912  and  prepared
for  college  at  Montpelier  Seminary.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1934  to  1936.  His  permanent  address  is
22  Gretter  Road,  West  Roxbury,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  Overseas,  1st  Lieutenant
Army  Air  Force.

Since  his  college  days:

He  was  employed  by  John  Hancock  Insurance  Co.  and  also  Boston  Shopping  News.

He  left  their  employ  to  join  the  U.  S.  Army  in  November,  1940,  a  year  before  Pearl
Harbor.  Having  enlisted  as  a  private  in  the  National  Guard,  he  was  stationed  at  Camp
Edwards  until  1942.  He  then  was  transferred  to  Wilmington,  Delaware,  and  in  January,

1943,  was  selected  as  a  candidate  for  Officers  Training  School.  Received  his  commission  WAI2
in  April,  1943.  He  was  then  assigned  to  Orlando,  Florida,  to  train  for  a  radar  operator.  |  |  |  |  f  |
He  is  now  overseas  and  was  promoted  to  First  Lieutenant  for  meritorious  work.  He  is
married  and  the  father  of  two  beautiful  sons.

CHARLES  WALTER  LOVE  WELL,  JR.

Charles  was  born  on  November  12,  1916  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  Holliston  High  School.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  1934  to  1936.

Since  his  college  days:

Worked  for  Williams  Shoe  Co.,  Draper  Corp.  and  Employers  Liability  Assurance  Corp.
Took  leave  of  absence  from  Employers,  and  enlisted  in  the  Army,  March,  1942.  As¬
signed  to  Q.M.  Corps,  took  basic  training  at  Fort  Francis  E.  Warren,  thence  to  Fort
Lewis,  Washington.  In  October,  1942,  presented  credentials  and  immediately  accepted
for  Air  Force.  Qualified  at  Nashville  Receiving  Centre  as  Pilot,  Navigator  and  Bom¬
bardier.  Chose  Bombardier  pre-flight  training,  Ellington  Field,  Advanced  School,  Big
Spring,  Texas.  Commissioned,  July,  1943,  as  Second  Lieutenant  and  received  his  wings.
Assigned  Euphrate  Post,  Washington.  Crew  of  Bomber  organized,  then  four  months
cross  country  flying.  Arrived  in  England  early  January,  1944.  Assigned  to  8th  AAF.
Flew  thirty-one  flights  which  included  fifteen  combat  missions  (Official).  Received
Purple  Heart,  Air  Medal  and  clusters,  Presidential  Citation.  His  ship  had  a  comple¬
ment  of  ten  (four  Officers,  six  men).  His  missions  were  over  the  well  known  targets  in
Germany.  Was  killed  in  crash  of  his  ship  in  England,  April  21,  1944.  Was  married  to
Natalie  Kolseth  of  Watertown.

WILLIAM  JAMESON  MAYNARD

William  was  born  on  March  3,  1916  and  prepared
for  college  at  Milton  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1934  to  1936.  His  permanent  address
is  95  Reservation  Road,  Milton,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  Lt.  William  J.  Maynard,
0-703148,  17  Ren.  Sqdn.,  A.P.O.  920,  c/o  Postmaster,
San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

With  Pacific  Mills  Co.  two  years  and  a  half  in  Boston  and  New  York.  With  American
Food  Products  Corporation  two  years,  leaving  this  company  to  enter  the  service,  August,
1941.  Entered  the  Army  Air  Force  1942,  training  in  Navigation,  Aerial  Gunnery  and
Bombardier  Schools  until  April,  1944.  Since  then  in  the  Pacific  Area.  He  is  unmarried.

DONALD  OSCAR  SUMNER

Donald  was  born  April  23,  1914  and  prepared  for
college  at  Worcester  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1934  to  1936.  His  permanent  address  is
21  Prospect  Street,  c/o  Parker,  Greenfield,  Massa¬
chusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  Lt.  Donald  O.
Sumner,  01313062,  Co.  B,  88th  Bat.,  22nd  I.A.T.R.,
Camp  Maxey,  Texas.

Since  his  college  days:

Donald  has  been  employed  by  the  New  England  Power  Co.,  leaving  there  to  accept  the
Stewardship  of  the  Hotel  Weldon  in  Greenfield.  He  married  in  1941.  In  March  of  1941
he  entered  the  Army  and  was  graduated  from  the  Infantry  Officers  Candidate  School,
1942.  Since  that  time  his  work  in  the  Army  has  been  essentially  instructing  and  lectur¬
ing  in  the  following  places:  Camp  Edwards  and  Fort  Devens,  Massachusetts;  Portland,
Maine;  Stoney  Field,  South  Carolina;  Camp  Wheeler,  Georgia;  Fort  Benjamin  Harrison
and  Camp  Atterbury,  Indiana;  Camp  Joseph  T.  Robinson,  Arkansas;  and  at  present
at  Camp  Maxey  in  Texas.

ALFRED  L.  WEBB,  JR.

Alfred  was  born  on  December  28,  1916  and  prepared
for  college  at  Columbia  High  School,  South  Orange,
New  Jersey.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1934  to  1936.
His  permanent  address  is  67  Scotland  Road,  South
Orange,  New  Jersey.

Since  his  college  days:

Al’s  first  work  was  in  Miami,  Florida,  which  terminated  in  the  Spring  of  1937  due  to  the
seasonal  cycle.  On  his  return  to  the  North  he  connected  with  the  Western-Electric  Co.
at  Kearny,  New  Jersey,  as  a  Cost  Accountant  on  telephone  and  other  communication
equipment.  In  the  early  months  of  1938  he  transferred  to  the  Tung-Sol  Lamp  &  Radio
Tube  Co.,  in  Newark,  with  duties,  first  as  Supervisor  of  Factory  Accounting  and  Payroll
departments,  and  later  as  Chief  Cost  Accountant.  He  made  a  further  move  in  January,
1941,  joining  the  Propeller  Division  of  the  Curtiss  Wright  Corporation  as  Plant  Controller
for  a  new  mass  production  plant  at  Indianapolis,  Indiana.  Presently,  A1  is  located  at
the  Propeller  Division’s  home  office  at  Caldwell,  New  Jersey,  as  Division  Supervisor  of
Industrial  Methods  Engineering.  A1  has  been  a  member  of  long  standing  in  the  Na¬
tional  Association  of  Cost  Accountants,  having  served  in  directorships  of  two  chapters,
and  recently  was  elected  to  membership  in  the  American  Accounting  Association.  Mar¬
ried  to  Hazel  M.  Aldrich  of  Webster  on  January  1,  1938,  the  Webbs  have  two  sons.

WILLIAM  PACKARD  WHITE

William  was  born  on  June  5,  1916  and  prepared  for
college  at  Hampton  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1934  to  1936.  His  permanent  address  is  Exeter
Road,  Hampton,  New  Hampshire.  His  temporary
address  is  19th  Repair  Sqd.,  19th  A.D.G.,  A.P.O.  528,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Bookkeeper  one  and  one-half  years,  Noye’s  Lumber  Company.  Gas  station  attendant
and  bookkeeper  one  year.  Co-partner  of  White  s  Gulf  Service  Station  before  entering
the  service.  Activities — President  and  founder  of  the  Hampton  Community  Club.
Active  in  sports:  baseball,  bowling  and  hockey.  War  Record  Entered  the  service  in
July,  1942.  He  attended  the  Buick  School  at  Flint,  Michigan,  for  exacting  Air  Service
Command  training.  He  has  been  overseas  since  June  2,  1943,  serving  in  a  North  African
Air  service  command  base.  Married  in  1942  to  the  former  Elizabeth  Toppan.

LEDGER

Class  of  1937

WILLIAM  CRAIN  BAUER

William  was  born  on  May  20,  1917  and  prepared  for
college  at  Governor  Dummer  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1935  to  June,  1937.  His
permanent  address  is  1605  East  High  Street,  Spring-
field,  Ohio.  His  temporary  address  is  S/Sgt.  Wm.  C.
Bauer,  36557363,  276th  Ord.  Maint.  Co.  (AA),
APO  562,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

WAR

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

Was  in  charge  of  Service  Parts  Stores  at  Detroit  for  Wagner  Electric  Corp.  of  St.  Louis
until  1940  when  he  was  employed  by  The  Bauer  Bros.  Co.  of  Springfield,  Ohio.  Here  he
superintended  the  department  engaged  in  the  roughing-out  operations  in  the  manufacture
of  105  mm.  shells.  Entered  the  Army  as  a  private  in  January  of  1943.  Is  now  an
Ordnance  Staff  Sergeant  with  the  First  Army  in  France.  Was  married  September  25,
1943  to  Miss  Louise  Samuelson  of  Springfield,  Ohio.

ALBERT  W.  BILLINGS

Albert  was  born  on  June  14,  1917  and  prepared  for
college  at  Newton  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1935  to  June,  1936.  His  permanent
address  is  19  Indiana  Terrace,  Newton  Upper  Falls,
64,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  ASN
31064832,  11th  Port,  Surg.  Hosp.,  A.P.O.  159,  c/o
Postmaster,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Graduated  from  Morristown  School,  June,  1938.  Owned  Newton  Coffee  Shop  for  two
years.  Employed  by  the  Gamewell  Fire  Alarm  Co.  until  entering  the  Army,  February,
1942.  After  three  months  training  at  the  Medical  Replacement  Centre,  Camp  Lee,
Virginia,  he  was  sent  to  the  Pacific,  most  of  which  time  has  been  spent  in  New  Guinea,
where  he  is  now  stationed.  Albert  is  now  Private  First  Class  and  not  married.

JESUS  MANUEL  CALYO  GARCIA

Jesus  was  born  on  May  21,  1916  and  prepared  for
college  at  Escuelas  Pias  de  Camaguey.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1935  to  1937.  His  permanent  address  is
Reparto  Beneficencia  No.  5,  (P.  O.  Box  353),  Cama¬
guey,  Cuba.

Since  his  college  days:

After  leaving  Nichols  in  June,  1937,  he  worked  in  New  York  City  until  December  of
the  same  year,  when  he  returned  home  to  Cuba.  Upon  his  return  and  shortly  after  he
went  into  business  with  his  father  and  they  own  a  bakery  and  retail  groceries  store  in
this  city.  He  got  married  to  Miss  Elida  Padron,  his  sweetheart  when  he  left  for  Nichols,
in  the  year  1941,  and  is  already  the  proud  father  of  two  daughters,  Teresa  Herminia,
two  years  four  months,  and  Isabel  Hortensia,  nine  months.  Manuel  is  now  studying
to  become  a  Public  Accountant,  and  is  starting  his  third  year  to  get  his  degree  at  the
University  of  Havana.  He  belongs  to  the  local  Lions  Club.  The  pleasant  memories  of
Nichols  are  always  in  his  heart  and  he  has  a  deep  and  sincere  fondness  of  his  Alma
Mater.

LEDGER

JOHN  WILLIAM  DALZELL

John  was  born  on  July  16,  1915  and  prepared  for
college  at  Kents  Hill,  Maine.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1936  to  June,  1937.  His  permanent
address  is  101  Liberty  Street,  Braintree,  Massachu¬
setts.  His  temporary  address  is  U.S.N.  Hospital
Staff,  Bainbridge,  Maryland.

Since  his  college  days:

He  worked  as  salesman  for  the  Hood  Rubber  Co.  at  their  Chicago  Branch.  On  Septem¬
ber  16,  1939,  he  married  Barbara  Belyea  of  Braintree,  Massachusetts.  They  now  have
one  son,  Richard  Porter  Dalzell,  born  on  Christmas  Day,  1941.  He  then  worked  at
the  Brockton  Perforating  Co.,  Brockton,  Massachusetts,  until  he  enlisted  in  the  Navy
on  December  27,  1943.  He  trained  at  Sampson,  New  York,  and  was  transferred  to  U.  S.
Navy  Hospital  at  Bainbridge,  Maryland,  where  at  the  present  writing  he  still  is  there.
He  is  a  H.  A.  1/c.  In  his  last  year  at  Nichols  he  was  captain  of  baseball  and  hockey  and
co-captain  of  football.

RENE  DOUGLAS  DANIELS

Rene  was  born  on  October  13,  1916  and  prepared  for
college  at  Bartlett  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1935  to  1937.  His  permanent  address  is  Wilson-
ville,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is  Capt.
Rene  D.  Daniels,  AG-Personnel  Hq.  Com.  Z,
ETO — APO  887,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New
York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduating  from  Nichols  in  1937,  Rene  was  Pro  at  the  Webster-Dudley  Golf  Club,
and  later  worked  for  the  Cranston  Print  Works  in  Webster,  Massachusetts.  He  enlisted
in  the  Army  Air  Corps  in  May,  1941,  and  was  first  stationed  at  Westover  Field,  Massa¬
chusetts.  He  was  later  stationed  at  Pendleton  Field,  Oregon;  Davis-Monthan  Field,
^  Arizona;  and  Geiger  Field,  Washington;  and  became  an  Officer  Candidate  at  the  Ad¬

jutant  General  School,  Fort  Washington,  Maryland,  where  he  received  his  commission
i  •  I  *  I  i  in  November,  1942.  He  was  married  before  going  overseas  in  January,  1943,  and  his

first  overseas  station  was  in  England,  where  this  snapshot  was  taken.  He  is  now  with
the  Adjutant  General  Organization,  somewhere  in  France.

WILLIAM  J.  LYTTLE,  JR.

William  was  born  on  August  9,  1916  and  prepared  for
college  at  Greenwich  Union  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1935  to  June,  1937.  His
permanent  address  is  18  Gray  Avenue,  Greenwich,
New  York.  His  temporary  address  is  A.S.N.  32665822
Hq.  and  Hq.  Sqdn.,  83d  Air  Depot  Group,  A.P.O.
492,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Bill  joined  the  firm  of  William  J.  Lyttle  and  Sons  on  leaving  Nichols.  This  business
included  the  distribution  of  Gulf  Oil  Products,  a  Coal  Business,  Electrical  and  Auto¬
motive  Accessories  and  an  Insurance  Business  which  he  took  complete  charge  of.  In
1941  he  went  to  work  in  the  Lynn,  Massachusetts  General  Electric  Plant.  He  had  tried
to  enlist  in  the  Armed  Services  but  his  stature  of  six  feet  eight  inches  did  not  appeal
to  Recruiting  Officers.  However,  in  December,  1942,  he  was  assigned  to  the  Army  Air
Forces  at  the  Basic  Training  Center  in  Atlantic  City.  In  August,  1943,  Bill  was  sent  to
Maxwell  Field  Classification  School  and  emerged  a  Classification  Specialist.  He  served
in  that  capacity  at  the  Greenville  Army  Air  Field  in  Mississippi  until  February,  1944,
when  he  started  on  the  first  leg  of  a  journey  which  has  now  ended  “Somewhere  in  India.”

NICHOLAS  JOSEPH  MIKOLA JCZAIv

Nicholas  was  born  on  September  7,  1916  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  Bartlett  High  School,  Webster,
Massachusetts.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1936  to
1937.  His  permanent  address  is  33  Boyden  Street,
Webster,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is
Btry.  A,  10  Bn.,  4  Reg.,  F.A.R.T.C.,  Fort  Bragg,
North  Carolina.

Since  his  college  days:

Nicholas  J.  Mikolajczak,  known  to  most  of  Webster  &  Dudley  friends  as  “Mickey
Nichols”  has  sketched  himself  quite  a  record  since  those  good  old  school  days.  His
interest  in  athletics  and  current  affairs  still  goes  on — though  there’s  a  slight  intermission
— while  he  does  his  part  in  speeding  up  “V”-Day.  As  captain  of  the  Chaseville  ball  club
he  showed  us  what  good  team  work  means.  He  was  well  supported  and  elected  as  mem-  .

ber"of  the  Board  of  Water  Commissioners  of  Dudley,  Massachusetts.  He  was  an  officer
on^the  Dudley  Police  Force  and  is  now  an  honorary  member.  “Mickey”  worked  in  I  f  DGCL
the  Packard  Mill  as  Spinning  Foreman.  Pearl  Harbor  came  and  without  waiting  for
his  country  to  call  him,  he  enlisted  December  18,  1941,  and  reported  at  Fort  Devens,
Massachusetts  on  December  22,  1941.  At  present  he’s  stationed  at  Fort  Bragg,  North
Carolina,  and  as  a  result  of  hard  work  coupled  with  his  usual  enthusiasm,  “Mickey”
is  now  a  Sergeant  and  is  doing  Cadre  work  in  Signal  Communications  at  the  Replace¬
ment  Center.  Wedding  bells  pealed  for  “Mickey”  on  September  19,  1943,  when  he
married  Dorothy  Theresa  Golash  of  Webster,  Massachusetts.

THOMAS  F.  MULLEN,  JR.

Thomas  was  born  on  June  8,  1916  and  prepared  for
college  at  Portsmouth  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1935  to  1937.  His  permanent  address  is
47  Orchard  Street,  Portsmouth,  New  Hampshire.
His  temporary  address  is  U.S.S.  Y  0-107,  c/o  Fleet
Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

The  first  summer  out  of  school  Tom  was  golf  pro  at  a  country  club  in  Francestown,  New
Hampshire.  That  fall  he  went  to  work  for  an  electrical  appliance  firm  and  then  for  a
wholesale  beverage  concern.  From  that  he  went  to  the  Boston  Beer  Company  and  trav¬
eled  for  them  in  Maine  and  New  Hampshire  up  to  the  time  he  enlisted  in  the  Naval
Reserve  in  December,  1941.  He  was  immediately  assigned  to  a  minesweeper  and  served
on  that  until  the  spring  of  1943  when  he  was  transferred  to  a  Navy  tanker  and  he  is
now  overseas,  based  somewhere  in  the  Pacific.  He  is  a  boatswain’s  mate — 1st  class.  In
July  of  1942,  Tom  married  Miss  Priscilla  H.  Jameson  of  Portsmouth.

Editor’s  note:  Tom  has  been  promoted  to  Chief  Boatswain  Mate  and  is  in  command  of
the  U.S.S.Y.A.  G-53.

EDWARD  SHELDON  POTTER

WAR

LEDGER

Edward  was  born  on  July  8,  1916  and  prepared  for
college  at  Providence  Country  Day  School  and  The
Berkshire  School.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1935
to  1937.  His  permanent  address  is  280  Irving  Avenue,
Providence,  Rhode  Island.  His  temporary  address
is  S/Sgt.  E.  S.  Potter,  11011971,  Squadron  D,  302
AAF  Base  Unit  (SW),  Box  416,  Hunter  Field,
Georgia.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduating  from  Nichols,  took  a  trip  through  Europe  and  the  British  Isles  during
the  summer  of  1937.  September,  1937,  joined  the  employ  of  the  Gorham  Mfg.  Co.,
Providence.  Worked  here  as  member  of  Credit  Department  and  assistant  to  Credit
Manager  until  May,  1941.  At  this  time  joined  the  Army  Air  Force.  In  Fall  of  1941
attended  AAF  Technical  School,  becoming  qualified  Airplane  and  Engine  Mechanic.
Since  beginning  of  War  has  served  with  Air  Force,  being  stationed  at  several  bases  along
Atlantic  Coast  with  exception  of  a  brief  time  of  detached  duty  with  Anti-Aircraft
Artillery  Branch  of  Ground  Forces.  At  present  serving  as  Crew  Chief  on  AAF  Bombers
while  stationed  with  Third  Air  Force  Staging  Wing,  Hunter  Field,  Georgia.  Unmarried.

RICHARD  C.  REDMOND

Richard  was  born  on  October  1,  1915  and  prepared
for  college  at  Irving  School,  Tarrytown.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1935  to  1937.  His  permanent  address  is
Redmon  &  Bramley  Oil  Co.,  Inc.,  Rensselaer,  New

ington.

Since  his  college  days:

He  is  affiliated  with  the  Redmond  &  Bramley  Oil  Co.,  Inc.,  of  Rensselaer,  New  York.
Was  married  in  March  of  1941.  Has  one  son,  Michael  Lloyd,  four  months  old.  War
Record:  Was  located  at  Fort  Bragg,  North  Carolina,  with  the  134th  Medical  Unit.
Transferred  to  Camp  Hood,  Texas,  and  O.  C.  S.  Is  First  Lieutenant,  A.  U.  S.,  and  at
present  instructing  at  Fort  Lewis,  Washington.

GEORGE  RICHARD  RONALDSON

George  was  born  on  November  20,  1916  and  prepared
for  college  at  Springfield  Technical  High  School.  He
attended  Nichols  from  1935  to  1937.  His  permanent
address  is  80  Hawthorne  St.,  Longmeadow  6,  Mass.
His  temporary  address  is  Co.  B  3188  S.S.B.,  c/o  17
Training  Co.,  Camp  Wood,  New  Jersey.

After  attending  Nichols,  Richard  entered  Syracuse  University  in  the  Fall  of  1937,
graduating  from  there  in  1939.  From  there  on  he  has  been  associated  with  his  father  at
the  National  Printing  Company,  Inc.  in  Thompsonville,  Connecticut,  manufacturers  of
greeting  cards.  On  July  20,  1940,  he  was  married  to  Frances  Andrews,  daughter  of
Major  and  Mrs.  Douglas  Andrews  of  Harrisburg,  Pennsylvania.  They  have  a  son
George  Andrews  Ronaldson,  born  November  1,  1943.  In  February,  1944,  he  entered
the  U.  S.  Army  and  was  assigned  to  the  Communications  Division  of  the  Signal  Corps.

JAMES  ROBERT  SISSON

James  was  born  on  August  4,  1915  and  prepared  for
college  at  Athol  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1935  to  1937.  His  permanent  address  is  New
Salem,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is
James  Robert  Sisson,  MM/2C,  117  N.C.B.,  Co.  D-5,
c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

He  entered  the  employ  of  the  L.  S.  Starrett  Company,  makers  of  fine  mechanical  tools,
in  1938,  and  completed  their  Training  Course  in  1941.  He  remained  in  their  employ
until  enlisting  in  the  U.  S.  Navy  “Seabees”  in  June,  1943.  Bob  was  married  to  Miss  Hope
Rockwell,  of  New  Salem,  Massachusetts,  March  21,  1940.  They  have  one  son,  James
Rockwell  Sisson  (Rocky),  born  April  25,  1941.  Bob  received  his  Boot  Training  at  Camp
Perry,  Virginia,  and  his  advanced  training  at  Gulfport,  Mississippi,  was  transferred  to
a  Construction  Battalion  in  February  of  1944  and  sent  to  the  island  of  Oahu.

WAR

LEDGER

DONALD  D.  CHAPMAN

Donald  was  born  on  October  19,  1917  and  prepared
for  college  at  Newark,  New  York.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1936  to  1938.  His  permanent  address
is  57  Grand  Place,  Arlington,  New  Jersey.  His
temporary  address  is  800th  Bomb  Squad,  500th
Bomb  Group,  Walker  AAF,  Victoria,  Kansas.

Since  his  college  days:

Worked  with  W.  H.  Chapman,  General  Insurance,  101  5th  Avenue,  New  York  City,
until  December,  1941.  Attended  Casey  Jones  Aeronautical  School,  Newark,  New
Jersey,  and  graduated  May,  1942.  Appointed  Instructor  at  Harrisburg,  Pennsylvania,
Aeronautical  School,  June,  1942.  Resigned  to  enlist  in  U.  S.  Air  Corps,  September  17,
1942.  Sent  to  Camp  Luna,  New  Mexico,  October  10,  1942.  Then  to  8th  Ferrying  Group,
U.  S.  Army  Air  Base,  Presque  Isle,  Maine,  November,  1942.  Then  appointed  Aviation
Cadet  and  sent  to  Boca  Raton,  Florida,  May  25,  1943.  Then  to  A.A.F.T.C.,  Yale
University,  New  Haven,  on  August  2,  1943.  Graduated  and  commissioned  Second  Lieu¬
tenant  on  January  27,  1944.  Sent  to  Flight  Engineering  School,  Lowry  Field,  Denver,
Colorado,  graduated  as  Flight  Engineer,  May  1944,  sent  to  Walker  A.A.F.  Victoria,
Kansas,  May  9,  1944,  where  he  is  stationed.  Not  married.

NELSON  R.  CHURCH

Nelson  was  born  on  February  18,  1918  and  prepared
for  college  at  Pawtucket  Senior  High  School.  He
attended  Nichols  from  1936  to  1938.  His  permanent
address  is  40  Kossuth  Street,  Pawtucket,  Rhode
Island.

Since  his  college  days:

Upon  graduating  from  Nichols,  he  entered  the  employ  of  Commercial  Investment  Trust,

Inc.,  1  Park  Avenue,  New  York  City,  and  was  employed  in  the  Industrial  Division  where
he  remained  until  the  latter  part  of  1941.  During  1942  and  1943,  he  was  engaged  at  the
Boston  Ordnance  District  in  the  Machine  Tool  Procurement  Division.  At  the  present
time  he  is  Sales  Manager  of  Southbridge  Engineering  Works,  Inc.,  and  Simonds  Machine  M  41
Company  of  Southbridge,  Massachusetts,  manufacturers  of  Optical  Machinery,  Milling
Cutters  and  War  Production  items.  In  addition,  he  operates  his  own  business  as  New  I  i  ■  <  i  ■
England  Sales  Representative  for  several  midwestern  machine  tool  concerns.  He  is
married  and  has  a  daughter  seven  months  old.  We  feel  sure  he  would  welcome  corre¬
spondence  from  his  old  friends  from  Nichols.

RICHARD  C.  CROZIER

Richard  was  born  on  February  16,  1917  and  prepared
for  college  at  Gardner  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1936  to  1938.  His  permanent  address  is
26  Edgell  Street,  Gardner,  Massachusetts.  His  tempo¬
rary  address  is  26  Edgell  Street,  Gardner,  Massa¬
chusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

For  three  years  Dick  was  employed  as  Paymaster  at  the  O.  W.  Siebert  Co.,  in  Gardner,
Massachusetts.  In  February  of  1942  he  was  commissioned  a  Second  Lieutenant  in  the
Army  Reserve  Quartermaster  Corps  which  he  qualified  for  through  the  Army  Q.M.
course  which  he  started  at  Nichols  and  completed  some  three  years  later.  He  was  mar¬
ried  in  April  of  1942  to  the  former  Harriet  J.  Depinet  of  Gardner,  Massachusetts.  Dick
went  overseas  in  June  of  1942.  He  spent  five  months  in  England  and  later  took  part  in
the  African  invasion.  He  received  his  promotion  while  there.  He  has  been  in  Italy  for
a  year  now  in  command  of  a  Q.M.  Truck  Company,  his  original  unit  attached  to  the
Air  Corps,  having  received  his  Captaincy  in  March.

Editor’s  note:  Dick  was  expected  to  return  to  this  country  for  duty.

FREDERIC  CHARLES  ECKELS

Frederic  was  born  on  December  2,  1917  and  prepared
for  college  at  Lincoln  High  School,  Newton,  Massa¬
chusetts.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1936  to  1938.
His  temporary  address  is  784  Senate  Drive,  Banning
Homes,  San  Pedro,  California.

WAR

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

After  being  graduated  from  Nichols  with  the  class  of  1938,  Fred  worked  in  Chicago  and
Green  Bay  for  the  Shefford  Cheese  Co.  In  1940  he  took  his  father’s  place,  the  late  S.  D.
Eckels,  at  the  Northern  Wisconsin  Produce  Co.  In  March,  1942,  he  announced  his
engagement  to  Nan  Oliver,  a  Manitowac  girl.  Four  months  later  he  enlisted  in  the
U.  S.  Navy  at  Great  Lakes.  On  July  11  he  married  Nan  at  Great  Lakes  in  the  Navy
Chapel.  He  was  graduated  with  the  rating  of  3d  class  Petty  Officer.  He  left  for  Radar
School  in  Stillwater,  Oklahoma  and  completed  his  course  in  San  Francisco.  He  par¬
ticipated  in  the  Sicilian,  Gilbert  and  Marshalls,  and  Saipan  invasions.  His  wife  and  son,
James  Oliver,  are  with  him  in  California  where  he  is  waiting  for  his  next  assignment.
He  has  just  been  given  the  rating  of  Warrant  Officer.

ROBERT  GREEN  FORSYTH

Robert  was  born  on  March  2,  1916  and  prepared  for
college  at  Simsbury  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1936  to  1937.  His  permanent  address
is  10  Vermont  Road,  New  Britain,  Connecticut.

Since  his  college  days:

For  about  three  years  after  his  college  days  Bob  worked  as  a  salesman.  In  1940  he  ac¬
cepted  a  position  with  the  Southern  New  England  Telephone  Company  conversion
crew.  He  became  an  installer  for  the  company,  in  Norwalk,  Connecticut,  in  1941.
Two  years  later  he  was  transferred  to  New  Britain,  Connecticut,  and  after  working  there
for  a  few  months  received  a  promotion  to  repairman.  In  1940  he  was  married  and
has  one  daughter.

LEDGER

SAMUEL  ARNOLD  GREENABAUM

Samuel  was  born  on  September  8,  1918  and  prepared
for  college  at  Seaford  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1936  to  1938.  His  permanent  address
High  Street,  Seaford,  Delaware.

Since  his  college  days:

From  September  in  1938  to  March,  1939,  I  worked  on  the  Seaford  Leader  Newspaper.

Division,  in  Seaford.  On  August  27,  1941,  was  married  to  Jean  E.  Tomlinson  from

LEDGER

WILLIAM  FAULKNER  HARDT

William  was  born  on  October  28,  1918  and  prepared
for  college  at  West  Haven  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1936  to  1938.  His  permanent  address
is  71  Fourth  Avenue,  West  Haven,  Connecticut.

Since  his  college  days:

Became  associated  with  a  wholesale  plumbing  house,  where  he  worked  as  a  member
of  the  office  force.  In  1941,  he  became  associated  with  the  High  Standard  Mfg.  Corp.,
as  a  factory  accountant.  In  October  of  1942  he  was  married,  and  the  following  year
became  the  proud  father  of  a  bouncing  baby  boy.  War  activities — They  are  confined
to  work,  which  concerns  the  manufacture  of  machine  guns,  bond  salesman,  and  many
other  local  war  activities.

GEORGE  JOHN  EA  COURSE

George  was  boin  on  July  13,  1917  and  prepared  for
college  at  Canterbury.  He  attended  Nichols  from
1936  to  1938.  His  permanent  address  is  57  George
Street,  Bristol,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address
is  Cpl.  George  J.  La  Course,  20130210,  Co.  D,  169
Inf.,  APO  43,  c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,  Cali¬
fornia.

Since  his  college  days:

George  worked  for  the  City  Engineer  in  Bristol  the  summer  after  graduating  from
Nichols  and  in  the  Fall  he  entered  the  New  York  School  of  Photography.  Completing
the  course  in  color  photography,  he  stayed  on  there  for  six  months  in  the  capacity  of  an
assistant  to  one  of  the  professors.  He  then  returned  to  Bristol  where  he  was  employed
^  in  the  Photographic  Department  of  the  New  Departure  Division  of  the  General  Motors

Corp.  October  16,  1940,  George  joined  the  National  Guard  and  in  February  of  1941
*  *  *  *  *  was  inducted  into  the  Federal  Service.  After  training  at  both  Camp  Blanding  and  Camp

Shelby,  he  left  for  combat  duty  in  the  Southwest  Pacific.  He  was  in  the  battle  of  Munda
and  received  the  Purple  Heart  after  being  seriously  wounded  at  Baanga  Island,  August
3,  1943.  After  several  months  of  hospitalization,  George  returned  to  active  duty  and
is  now  stationed  in  New  Guinea.

Editor’s  note:  George  has  been  promoted  to  Corporal.

GEORGE  ALBERT  PEIRCE,  JR.

George  was  born  on  April  19,  1918  and  prepared  for
college  at  New  Hampton  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1936  to  1938.  His  permanent  address
is  Boscawen,  New  Hampshire.  His  temporary  ad¬
dress  is  U.  S.  Army  Mine  Planter  Baird,  Fort  Con¬
stitution,  New  Hampshire.

Since  his  college  days:

From  April,  1939  to  April,  1940,  George  worked  in  the  National  State  Capitol  Bank,
Concord,  New  Hampshire.  He  then  spent  four  months  taking  C.A.A.  Basic  and  Sec¬
ondary  flying  courses.  In  1940,  he  became  New  England  Manager  of  The  American
Funicular  Corporation.  He  worked  with  the  U.  S.  Army  Engineers  from  August,  1940
to  June,  1941,  surveying  for  the  Franklin  and  Black  Water  Flood  Control  Dams.  Septem¬
ber  26,  1941,  George  was  commissioned  Second  Lieutenant  in  the  Coast  Artillery.
From  July,  1941  to  January,  1942,  he  worked  in  the  Treasury  Department  of  Scott
&  Williams,  Inc.,  in  Laconia,  New  Hampshire.  January  15,  1942,  he  was  called  to
active  duty.  He  reported  at  Fort  Eustis,  Virginia,  and  during  the  following  five  months,
he  attended  the  Seacoast  &  Submarine  Mine  schools  at  Fort  Monroe,  Virginia.  He  was
promoted  to  a  First  Lieutenant,  September,  1942,  and  to  a  Captain,  December,  1943.

JOHN  BARRY  PICKFORD

John  was  born  on  November  24,  1917  and  prepared
for  college  at  Leominster  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1936  to  June,  1938.  His
permanent  address  is  105  Grand  Street,  Leominster,
Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  Cpl.
John  Barry  Pickford,  11056894,  Det.  A,  10th  Dep.
Repair  Sq.  (Oxygen  Unit),  10th  A.D.G.,  A.P.O.  149,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Barry’s  first  position  was  with  the  Brewer  Chemical  Co.  of  Worcester,  Massachusetts,
where  he  was  district  manager  of  one  of  their  largest  outlets.  He  then  turned  to  buying
and  worked  as  a  supply  buyer  for  the  Water  Company  in  a  large  Worcester  County
concern.

But  he  still  had  the  yen  to  write,  an  urge  that  was  instilled  in  him  while  in  his  college
days  at  Nichols.  Barry  then  procured  a  position  as  a  newspaper  reporter  for  the  Wor¬
cester  Telegram  and  Evening  Gazette,  a  position  he  enjoyed  a  great  deal.  He  held  this
position  until  the  time  he  enlisted  in  the  U.  S.  Army.  After  spending  six  months  in  the
United  States  training  for  combat  duty,  he  was  sent  to  England  and  then  on  to  France,
where  he  is  at  the  present  time.  Due  to  an  injury  received  while  training  in  England,
Barry  was  unable  to  participate  in  the  D-Day  landing  but  arrived  soon  afterwards.  In
recent  letters  received  from  Barry,  he  stated  that  things  were  going  quite  well  with  him.

NORMAN  MEARNS  PUFFER

Norman  was  born  on  July  10,  1916  and  prepared  for
college  at  Burlington,  Vermont  High  School  and  Ver¬
mont  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols  from  Septem¬
ber,  1936  to  June,  1938.  His  permanent  address  is
176  Loomis  Street,  Burlington,  Vermont.  His
temporary  address  is  A.P.O.  730,  c/o  Postmaster,
Seattle,  Washington.

Since  his  college  days:

About  one  year  with  Ben  Mont  Paper  Corp.,  Bennington,  Vermont.  About  three  years
with  Railway  Express  Agency,  Burlington,  Vermont.  Enlisted  in  U.  S.  Army,  January,
1942.  After  a  few  days  at  Camp  Devens,  sent  to  Q.M.  School,  Fort  Warren,  Wyoming,
three  months  later  to  Fort  Lawton,  Seattle,  and  shortly  thereafter  to  Sitka,  Alaska.
Returned  to  Seattle  about  a  year  later  for  short  stay,  then  sent  to  an  Aleutian  post  as
Technical  Sergeant  in  the  Army  Transportation  Service,  where  he  still  was  when  last
heard  from,  though  expecting  a  transfer.

LEDGER

FRANK  ELLERY  REDFIEL1)

Frank  was  born  on  July  23,  1917  and  prepared  for
college  at  Tenafly  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1936  to  1938.  His  permanent  address  is  318
Engle  Street,  Tenafly,  New  Jersey.  His  temporary
address  is  Spence  Field,  Moultrie,  Georgia.

Since  his  college  days:

Lt.  Redfield  was  first  connected  with  Columbia  Broadcasting  Co.,  in  New  York  City,
from  graduation  until  the  summer  of  1940.  He  then  went  to  Boston  to  train  as  an
Adjuster  for  Liberty  Mutual  Insurance  Co.  He  returned  to  be  married  on  December  7,
1940,  to  Miss  Eileen  Everson  of  Tenafly.  Mr.  and  Mrs.  Redfield  made  their  home  in
YVAI/  Philadelphia  where  Ellery  as  employed  by  Liberty.  In  March  of  1942  they  returned

I  I  I  I  I  to  New  Jersey  and  Ellery  did  Plant  Planning  for  Wright  Aero.  He  enlisted  in  the  U.  S.

Army  Air  Corps,  January,  1943.  He  received  his  pilot  wings  at  Single  Engine  Adv.
Training  School,  Spence  Field  Georgia.  Ellery  has  reported  to  Randolph  Field  as  one
of  the  expert  pilots  selected  for  training  in  AAF  Central  Instructors  School.  Upon  com¬
pletion  of  specialized  training  he  will  go  to  another  field  of  the  AAF  Training  Com.
to  be  instructor  of  cadets.  Mrs.  Redfield  will  join  him.

FREDERICK  V.  RICHMOND

Frederick  was  born  on  December  23,  1915  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  Williston  Academy  and  Cheshire
Academy.  He  attended  Nichols  from  September,
1936  to  June,  1938.

Since  his  college  days:

Worked  for  the  United  Electric  Corp.  in  Easthampton  until  he  volunteered  late  in  1941.
The  following  is  taken  from  a  recently  received  letter:  “I  can  fully  appreciate  the  shock
you  must  have  received  with  the  notice  from  the  War  Department  that  Fred  was  killed
in  action  on  March  6,  1944.  .  .  .  Your  belief  that  Fred  may  be  still  alive  shows  untold
Faith  in  God,  but  it  is  my  unpleasant  duty  to  verify  the  War  Department  notification.
Your  son  was  killed  by  enemy  fighters  after  he  left  the  airplane  and  was  parachuting  to
earth.  I  saw  him — went  to  administer  first  aid,  and  found  him  dead.  ...  on  March  6,
Fred  realized  one  of  his  greatest  ambitions — to  bomb  the  city  of  Berlin.  He  was  a  great
man — one  I  shall  never  forget.  .  .

for  college  at  Tabor  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1937  to  1938.  His  permanent  address  is  22J4
Kay  Street,  Newport,  Rhode  Island.  His  temporary
address  is  U.  S.  Army,  31113568,  Hq.  Co.,  3142,  Sig.
Service  G.  P.  A.,  P.  O.  464.

Since  his  college  days:

He  has  been  employed  as  an  insurance  salesman,  account  clerk,  insurance  and  real  es¬
tate  salesman,  cost  clerk,  time  keeper  and  order  clerk,  office  manager,  automobile  sales
company  until  he  entered  the  service  of  his  country  on  April  24,  1942,  at  Fort  Monmouth,
New  Jersey,  in  the  Army  Signal  Corp.  Also  he  was  stationed  at  Fort  Crowder,  Missouri,
until  he  embarked  for  somewhere  in  North  Africa  where  he  is  stationed  now  as  sergeant,
U.  S.  Signal  Corp.  He  is  married,  but  he  has  no  children.

LEDGER

WILLIAM  B.  SMITH

William  was  born  on  August  26,  1917  and  prepared
for  college  at  Mercersburg  Academy,  Pennsylvania.
He  attended  Nichols  from  1936  to  1938.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  834  Windsor  Road,  Cumberland,
Maryland.  His  temporary  address  is  Company  “T,”
School  Regiment,  The  Quartermaster  School,  Camp
Lee,  Virginia.

Since  his  college  days:

Associated  with  the  Second  National  Bank  of  Cumberland  from  the  Fall  of  1938  until
the  Fall  of  1940.  Left  the  bank  to  go  with  Travelers  Insurance  Co.  Received  a  Reserve
Commission  in  the  Army  as  a  Second  Lieutenant  in  the  Quartermaster  Corps,  March,
1940,  and  was  called  to  active  duty  December  of  that  year  reporting  at  Holabird  Q.M.
Depot.  Transferred  to  Camp  Lee,  Virginia,  in  February,  1941.  Promoted  to  First
Lieutenant,  February,  1942  and  left  for  a  tour  with  the  Army  War  Show.  Returned  to
Camp  Lee,  October,  1942,  as  a  Captain  and  was  soon  sent  to  Camp  Phillips,  Kansas,
with  the  477th  Q.M.  Truck  Regiment— Left  for  the  Alaska  Highway,  January,  1943,
and  served  in  British  Columbia  and  the  Yukon  Territory  under  the  Northwest  Service
Command  until  April,  1944.  Returned  to  Fort  Meade,  Maryland,  then  to  Camp  Lee,
Virginia,  and  is  now  training  Cadets  to  be  Commissioned  Officers.

of  West  Newton,  Massachusetts.  They  have  one  child,  Susanne  Elizabeth.  He  is  now
^  serving  in  the  Army  of  the  United  States.

Woodman,  Ord.  0-395259,  Hq.  S.P.B.C.  Ord.  Section,
A.P.O.  502,  c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,  California.

Employed  by:  Montgomery  Ward;  World’s  Fair — Guide  and  Quartermaster  Depart¬

Married  Helen  Kate  Berry  of  Muskogee,  Oklahoma,  December  24,  1941.

Class  of  1939

JOSE  CAR DEN AL  ARGUELLO

Jose  was  born  on  June  30,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Colegio  Centro  America.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1938  to  May,  1939.  His
permanent  address  is  Managua  D.  N.,  Nicaragua.

AVAR

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

He  was  sorry  to  return  without  having  finished  his  studies  at  Nichols.  Immediately
after  coming  back  he  started  working  as  sales  clerk  in  my  Retail  Store  in  Granada,
Nicaragua,  later  he  ascended  to  be  a  wholesale  clerk.  The  24  of  January,  1940,  he  mar¬
ried  Miss  Violeta  Viva  Chamorro,  and  in  March,  1940,  he  became  manager  of  my  branch
wholesale  and  retail  drygoods  store  in  Managua,  Nicaragua’s  capital.  At  his  present
position  he  has  shown  brilliant  business  visions.  On  February  9,  1941,  arrived  his  first
first  baby  boy  named  also  Jose.  He  is  now  expecting  a  second  boy,  or  his  first  girl.

JOSEPH  L.  CAWLEY

Joseph  was  born  on  July  7,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Bristol  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1937  to  June,  1939.  His  permanent
address  is  43  Bellevue  Avenue,  Bristol,  Connecticut.
His  temporary  address  is  Hdg.,  210th  Bn.,  65th
Regt.,  Camp  Blanding,  Florida.

Since  his  college  days:

Spent  one  year  at  J.  H.  Russells,  Wholesale-Retail  Dealers,  Holyoke,  Massachusetts,
entered  business  with  father  under  trade  name,  Bristol,  Hardware  Company,  Inc.  On
April  1,  1942,  enlisted  in  United  States  Army,  sent  to  Camp  Devens,  from  there  to  Fort
Terry,  New  York.  On  June,  1948,  entered  Anti-Aircraft  Artillery  Officers’  Candidate
School,  Camp  Davis,  North  Carolina,  graduating  as  Second  Lieutenant.  October  7,
1943,  next  Camp  Edwards,  Massachusetts,  two  months  Infantry  School,  Fort  Benning,
Georgia.  At  present  stationed  Camp  Blanding,  Florida.

Editor’s  note:  Latest  information  is  that  he  was  stationed  in  Germany  and  was  promoted
to  First  Lieutenant.

FRANK  V.  CINQUEMANI

Frank  was  born  on  October  20,  1917  and  prepared  for
college  at  Roxbury  School,  Connecticut.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  September,  1937  to  June,  1939.
His  permanent  address  is  227  East  106th  Street,  New
York,  29,  New  York.  His  temporary  address  is
S/Sgt.  Frank  V.  Cinquemani,  Kennedy  General
Hospital,  Memphis,  Tennessee.

Since  his  college  days:

Attended  American  Academy  of  Embalming  and  Mortuary  Research,  Inc.  from  Septem¬
ber,  1939  to  March,  1940,  graduating  with  a  mark  of  Grade  AA.  On  August  5,  1941,  he
entered  the  U.  S.  Army  and  received  his  Embalmer’s  and  Undertaker’s  licenses  on  August
12,  1941.  After  one  year’s  training  in  the  United  States,  he  left  for  overseas  duty  on
August  5,  1942.  He  served  in  the  Medical  Corps  attached  to  the  Combat  Engineers.
He  traveled  from  England,  Africa,  Sicily,  England  and  then  to  France.  On  July  11,
1943,  he  received  a  Silver  Star  for  gallantry  at  Gela,  Sicily.  On  June  6,  1944,  on  D-Day
at  Normandy,  France,  he  was  seriously  wounded  in  action.  He  then  was  sent  back  to
the  General  Hospital  in  England.  He  arrived  in  the  United  States  on  October  13,  1944,
and  is  now  stationed  at  the  Kennedy  General  Hospital  in  Memphis,  Tennessee.

JOHN  NELSON  COLE

John  was  born  on  March  7,  1918  and  prepared  for
college  at  Phillips  Academy,  Andover.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1937  to  June,  1939.  His
permanent  address  is  35  Morton  Street,  Andover,
Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  J.  N.  Cole,
0-424074,  14th  Q.M.  Co.  (trk.),  A.P.O.  886,  c/o
Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Two  years  at  The  Andover  Press.  Summer  course  in  printing  at  Carnegie  Institute  of
Technology.  Commissioned  Second  Lieutenant,  1941,  in  Quartermaster  Corps.  Mar¬
ried  December  26,  1941,  to  Betty  Lane  of  Millbury,  Massachusetts.  One  child,  Nancy,
born  January  2,  1943.  Stationed  in  various  camps  in  this  country.  Commissioned
First  Lieutenant  in  January,  1943,  and  went  overseas  to  India  in  May,  1943.

JOHN  C.  DEAIPSEY

college  at  Southside  High  School,  Rockville  Centre,
New  York.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1937  to  1939.
His  permanent  address  is  67  Oxford  Road,  Rockville
Center,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Investigator,  Liberty  Mutual  Insurance  Co.,  1941  to  1942.  Married  Jane  Van  Alst,
March  13,  1942.  Entered  Army  April  8,  1942.  Basic  training  at  Camp  Lee,  Virginia,
April  26  to  June  21,  1942,  with  “This  is  the  Army”  from  June  21  to  September,  1943.
Toured  the  country  and  made  the  motion  picture  at  Hollywood  with  training  division
of  Army  since  September,  1943,  and  touring  the  camps  of  the  country  at  present  time.

LEDGER

GORDON  GENT

college  at  Scarsdale  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1937  to  June,  1939.  His
permanent  address  is  175  Brewster  Road,  Scarsdale,
New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  a  trip  West  with  his  roommate,  Bill  Carter,  Gordon  worked  for  a  year  for  the
Rumford  Chemical  Works,  Rumford,  Rhode  Island.  He  was  then  called  to  New  York
to  work  in  the  advertising  department  of  the  United  Fruit  Company  where  he  remained
for  two  years.  After  being  discharged  by  the  Selective  Service  Induction  Board,  the
Civil  Service  Commission  employed  him.  Through  the  Civil  Service  Commission  Gor¬
don  is  employed  by  the  Bureau  of  Aeronautics  at  Tarrytown,  New  York.

RICHARD  C.  HAMANT

Richard  was  born  on  August  9,  1917  and  prepared  for
college  at  New  Hampton.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1937  to  1938.  His  permanent  address  is  81
Eliot  Avenue,  West  Newton,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

Started  with  Filene’s  at  the  Warehouse  Department  in  Cambridge  and  later  was  in  the
Stock  Department  in  the  Main  Store  in  Boston.  Not  being  eligible  for  active  war  service
he  transferred  to  the  Raytheon  Manufacturing  Co.,  Newton,  Massachusetts,  makers  of
electronic  devices.

AARON  ADDISON  HOBART

Aaron  was  born  on  April  14,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Tabor  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1937  to  1939.  His  permanent  ad¬
dress  is  Pearl  Street,  Caryville,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  A.  A.  Hobart,  Chief  S.  K.,
Navy  248,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  by  Liberty  Mutual  Insurance  Co.,  Boston,  Massachusetts  and  Coca-Cola
Company,  Boston,  Massachusetts.  Enlisted  in  Naval  Reserve  in  1941.  Newport  Train¬
ing  Station,  March,  1941  to  September,  1943,  the  latter  part  of  which  he  was  instructor
in  Storekeeper  Classes.  In  September,  1943,  was  ordered  to  report  to  the  newly  com¬
missioned  USS  Adonis  at  Norfolk,  Virginia,  which  is  at  present  in  the  Atlantic  area.
WAC  “Hobbie”  married  Barbara  Stevens  of  Wellesley  Hills,  Massachusetts,  October  4,  1941,

and  has  one  daughter  named  Stephanie,  born  May  15,  1943.

Editor’s  note:  “Hobbie”  has  received  a  new  rating  and  is  now  Chief  S.  K.

HAROLD  CHRISTIE  KEYS,  JR.

Harold  was  born  on  July  26,  1918  and  prepared  for
college  at  Pingry  School.  He  attended  Nichols  from
1937  to  1939.  His  permanent  address  is  623  North
Broad  Street,  Elizabeth  3,  New  Jersey.  His  tem¬
porary  address  is  Sgt.  H.  C.  Keys,  Jr.,  A.S.N.
12092979,  H.  Q.  Co.,  8th  P.O.E.,  APO  780,  c/o  Post¬
master,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

One  year  with  American  Agricultural  Chemical  Co.,  Cartaret,  New  Jersey.  Resigned  to
help  in  his  father’s  Real  Estate  and  Insurance  business  as  men  had  left  to  go  in  Army
or  defense  work.  Stayed  six  months  with  Father  then  went  into  defense  work  at  General
Motors  for  six  months,  then  went  with  American  Type  Founders,  Munitions  Depart¬
ment  for  five  months,  leaving  there  to  enlist  in  U.  S.  Army,  June  6,  1942.  After  three
weeks  at  Camp  Dix  was  stationed  at  Newark  Armory  until  January,  1943,  when  ordered
to  Boston  until  April,  1943,  when  ordered  to  Camp  Kilmer,  from  which  he  was  ordered
overseas  the  last  of  April,  1943.  Has  been  various  places  in  Africa,  ten  months  in  Bizerte.
In  March,  1944,  he  was  ordered  to  Italy  where  he  is  at  present  in  the  Medical  Corps.

WILLIAM  REYNOLDS  LEWIS

William  was  born  on  July  3,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Loomis.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1937
to  1939.  His  permanent  address  is  97  Brookview
