Since  his  college  days:

On  leaving  college,  started  work  with  The  Bassick  Co.,  of  Bridgeport,  Connecticut.
Left  The  Bassick  Co.  after  six  months  for  a  better  opportunity  with  The  H.  O.  Canfield
Rubber  Co.  of  Bridgeport,  Connecticut.  Left  The  H.  O.  Canfield  Rubber  Co.  to  volun¬
teer  under  the  Selective  Service  Act  on  April  1,  1941.  At  Camp  Edwards,  Massachusetts,
until  January,  1942,  at  which  time  sailed  to  Australia;  and  in  the  Fall  of  that  year  moved
up  to  New  Guinea,  where  from  last  accounts  he  is  still  serving  in  the  grade  of  Sgt./T.

LEDGER

MARSHALL  S.  NICHOLS

Marshall  was  born  on  December  23,  1917  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  New  Hampton.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1937  to  June,  1939.  His
permanent  address  is  26  Ruthven  Place,  Summit,
New  Jersey.  His  temporary  address  is  S/Sgt.  M.  S.
Nichols,  Finance  Office,  Dale  Mabry  Field,  Talla¬
hassee,  Florida.

Since  his  college  days:

From  Nichols  he  went  to  Syracuse  University  in  the  Fall  of  1939.  Graduated  in  the
Spring  of  1941.  He  studied  Business  Administration,  majoring  in  finance.  In  the
Summer  of  1941  he  worked  with  the  American  Tel.  &  Tel.  Co.  during  their  sale  of  stocks.
Then  he  was  with  the  Summit  Trust  Co.  until  January  11,  1942.  On  the  12th  he  left
I  for  Camp  Dix  and  three  days  later  for  Q.M.  training  at  Camp  Lee,  Virginia.  After

I  |  |  (  |  |  preliminary  training  and  a  few  weeks  at  Camp  School,  he  was  told  to  report  to  the

Finance  Officer  at  Bowman  Field,  Louisville,  Kentucky.  Some  three  or  four  months
later  he  was  transferred  to  the  3d  Air  Force  at  Columbia,  South  Carolina.  In  July,  1943.
was  again  transferred  to  the  Finance  Office  at  Dale  Mabry  Field,  Tallahassee,  Florida,
He  is  still  there,  working  in  various  departments,  but  mostly  on  officers’  pay  and  as
cashier.

FRED  ALLEYNE  OTIS,  JR.

Fred  was  born  on  January  15,  1917  and  prepared  for
college  at  Loomis  School,  Windsor,  Connecticut.
He  attended  Nichols  from  September,  1937  to  June,
1939.  His  permanent  address  is  21  Harwich  Road,
Providence,  Rhode  Island.  His  temporary  address
is  U.  S.  Coast  Guard,  Headquarters  Co.,  C.O.T.P.,
Constitution  Base,  Boston,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

“Ted”  worked  for  a  few  months  in  the  Providence  plant  of  the  Coca-Cola  Co.  He  then
went  with  the  Franklin  Process  Co.,  a  dyeing  concern  in  Providence,  where  he  worked
until  he  enlisted  in  the  U.  S.  Coast  Guard  in  Boston,  Massachusetts,  in  January,  1942.
The  following  summer  he  went  to  the  Manhattan  Beach  Training  School  in  New  York
and  shortly  afterwards  received  his  Coxswain’s  rating.  In  1943  he  was  advanced  to
Boatswain’s  Mate,  2nd  class.  Until  September,  1944,  when  he  was  sent  to  the  Gunner’s
Mate  School  in  Florida,  he  was  on  patrol  duty  at  the  Constitution  Base  in  Boston.
He  continues  to  like  tennis  and  golf,  but  has  had  very  few  opportunities  to  play  since
he  has  been  in  the  service.  He  is  still  single.

CLARENCE  S.  REDDY,  JR.

Clarence  was  born  on  August  10,  1914  and  prepared
for  college  at  Cushing  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1937  to  1939.  His  permanent  address
is  6  Black  Horse  Lane,  Cohasset,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  1638t.  Ordnance  Co.,
A.P.O.  629,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

His  first  position  was  as  a  salesman  with  the  Automotive  Supply  Company  in  Boston,
Massachusetts.  In  1941  he  was  married  to  Barbara  Barker  of  Lowell,  Massachusetts.
In  April  of  the  same  year  he  was  called  by  the  Selective  Service  and  entered  the  United
States  Army  as  a  member  of  the  Coast  Artillery  Harbor  Defense.  His  first  assignment
was  at  Fort  H.  G.  Wright,  New  York,  from  there  he  was  transferred  to  the  Military
Police  detachment  in  New  London,  Connecticut.  In  1942  he  went  to  Kelly  Field  Avia¬
tion  Ordnance  School  in  Texas.  He  was  selected  for  Officers  Candidate  School  in  Aber¬
deen,  Maryland,  and  in  1943  he  was  graduated.  He  was  attached  to  the  A.A.F.T.C.
in  Miami  Beach,  Florida  and  after  six  months  was  sent  to  a  P.O.E.  in  Kearns,  Utah.
He  left  for  overseas  in  October  and  landed  in  North  Africa.  After  five  months  he  was
transferred  to  Burma,  India,  to  be  in  charge  of  service  and  maintenance  of  ammunition.
On  the  first  of  July  he  received  his  First  Lieutenancy.

LEDGER

CHARLES  A.  REYNOLDS

Charles  was  born  on  December  27,  1916  and  prepared
for  college  at  Brown  University.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1937  to  1939.  His  permanent  address  is  9
Thomas  Street,  Providence,  Rhode  Island.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduation  from  Nichols  worked  for  the  Atlantic  Refining  Co.  until  August  18,
1942,  as  a  station  attendant,  retail  merchandiser,  station  director,  and  as  fuel  oil  sales¬
man.  In  April,  1942,  enlisted  in  Army  Air  Corps  as  aviation  cadet  being  called  for  active
duty  August  18,  1942.  Reported  for  pilot’s  pre-flight  training  at  San  Antonio  Aviation
Cadet  Center  in  Texas.  A  recurrence  of  an  old  knee  injury  suffered  while  playing  foot¬
ball  at  Nichols  finally  resulted  in  a  medical  discharge  on  August  16,  1943.  Returned  to
Providence  and  on  November  26,  1943  was  married  to  Jean  Perry  of  Providence.  Now
working  for  the  Warren  Teaming  Co.  in  Providence  as  Assistant  Treasurer.

FRED  BYRD  THORNLEY

Fred  was  born  on  December  7,  1917  and  prepared
for  college  at  St.  Paul’s.  He  attended  Nichols  from
1937  to  1939.  His  permanent  address  is  3  Locust

U.  S.  A.,  FIME  Fuel  Officer,  APA  787,  c/o  Postmaster,

Since  his  college  days:

Fred  was  employed  by  the  Home  Insurance  Co.,  New  York  City,  before  enlisting  in  the

Virginia.  On  May  3,  1942,  he  married  Miss  Florence  Gaiser  from  his  home  town.
WAI  Three  months  later  he  went  overseas.  After  receiving  promotion  to  Captain  in  June,

I  DC  I  D  1943,  he  was  acting  Liaison  Officer  with  A.T.C.  and  traveled  to  eighteen  different

countries.  September,  1944,  he  came  home  for  thirty  days  and  then  back  overseas  to
his  new  post  as  Fuel  Officer  at  Headquarters  for  China  and  Middle  East.

Since  his  college  days:

Upon  his  graduation  from  Nichols  College,  he  was  awarded  a  position  with  the  Boston
News  Bureau  and  became  assistant  to  the  manager.  He  served  in  that  capacity  until
he  entered  the  Army;  he  was  inducted  in  June,  1943.  He  received  his  basic  training  at
Camp  Lee  with  the  Q.M.C.  From  there  he  was  sent  to  Houston  College  for  training
in  Administration.  Thence  to  Camp  Reynolds,  and  thereafter  to  California.  He  is
at  present  in  New  Guinea.

JOHN  RICHARD  TRANOR

John  was  born  on  October  5,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Bogota  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1937  to  1939.  His  permanent  address  is  442
Leonia  Avenue,  Bogota,  New  Jersey.  His  temporary
address  is  Sgt.  J.  R.  Treanor,  32456685,  Squadron  F,
Box  533,  Hunter  Field,  Georgia.

Since  his  college  days:

Following  graduation  went  with  The  Flintkote  Company,  Rutherford,  New  Jersey,  as
Chief  Mail  Clerk.  From  August,  1941  to  August,  1942,  Cost  Accountant  with  the
Bogota  Paper  Board  Corporation,  (a  Robert  Gair  Company,  Inc.  subsidiary),  Bogota,
New  Jersey.  Entered  the  U.S.A.A.F.  August,  1942.  Basic  training  Atlantic  City,  New
Jersey.  Transferred  to  the  Air  Forces  Technical  School,  Lowry  Field,  Colorado.  Upon
graduation  from  Aircraft  Armorers  School  and  the  Instructor  Training  Course  was  as¬
signed  as  Instructor  in  the  Air  Forces  Technical  School  at  Lowry  Field,  Colorado.
July,  1944,  assigned  to  the  3d  Air  Force  and  transferred  to  Hunter  Field,  Georgia,  as  a
Specialist  in  Aircraft  Armament.  Present  rank  Sergeant.  Unmarried.

RICHARD  M.  WHITNEY

Richard  was  born  on  June  4,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Newton  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1937  to  1939.  His  permanent  address  is  430
Albemarle  Road,  Newtonville,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  by  Fireman’s  Fund  Insurance  Co.  of  Boston,  Massachusetts,  and  General
Electric  Co.,  Lynn,  Massachusetts.  Entered  U.  S.  Army  in  April,  1941.  Transferred
to  U.  S.  Army  Air  Force  in  October,  1942.  Commissioned  at  Randolph  Field,  June,

1942.  Assigned  to  Tow  Target  Squadron,  Otis  Field,  Massachusetts.  Heavy  Bomber
Training  (B-24),  Alamogordo,  New  Mexico.  Commissioned  a  First  Lieutenant,  April,

1943.  Went  overseas  November,  1943.  Piloted  B-24,  Liberator,  in  the  15th  Air  Force
on  operations  from  Italian  bases.  Reported  “Missing  in  Action  over  Austria,”  February
23,  1944.

WAR

LEDGER

Class  of  1940

RALPH  HOWARD  REAN

WAR

LEDGER

Ralph  was  born  on  December  28,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Governor  Dummer  Academy.  He
attended  Nichols  from  1938  to  1939.  His  permanent
address  is  15  Eighth  Avenue,  Lowell,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

Was  employed  in  the  advertising  department  of  The  Courier-Citizen  Newspaper  Co.,  of
Lowell,  Massachusetts,  until  June,  1941,  when  he  enlisted  in  the  U.  S.  Marine  Corps,
training  at  Parris  Island,  South  Carolina  and  Quonset  Point,  Rhode  Island.  Volunteered
for  the  Amphibian  Corps,  trained  at  Dunedin,  Florida,  and  at  New  River,  North  Carolina.
Was  made  a  Corporal  in  February,  1943,  and  sent  to  the  South  Pacific  as  operator  of  an
Amphibian  “Alligator.”  Has  been  in  combat  with  the  Japanese  at  Guadalcanal,  Bougain¬
ville  and  Guam,  the  “Alligators”  proving  valuable  for  landing  troops  and  transporting
supplies  to  the  boys  in  the  front  line  before  roads  could  be  built  in  the  jungle  suitable
for  other  apparatus.  Is  now  in  Guam  and  claims  to  be  in  good  health  and  good  morale.
At  times  he  serves  as  an  instructor  in  combat  swimming  for  the  Marines.

MAURICE  W.  BOYNTON

Maurice  was  born  on  August  4,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  New  Hampton  Preparatory.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address
is  Hillsboro,  New  Hampshire.  His  temporary  address
is  V-12  Unit,  Rensselaer,  Troy,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Upon  graduation  from  N.J.C.  associated  with  father  in  grocery  and  produce  business  at
Hillsboro,  New  Hampshire.  Joined  U.  S.  Naval  Reserve,  January  12,  1942.  Called  to
active  duty,  April  23,  1942.  Completed  twenty-eight  months  sea  duty  in  the  Caribbean
area  this  September,  1944,  and  is  now  at  Pre-midshipman’s  school,  Rensselaer  University,
Troy,  New  York.

I).  DIRCK  BRINCKERHOFF

Dirck  was  born  on  May  19,  1918  and  prepared  for
college  at  Loomis  and  Avon  Old  Farms.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1938  to  June,  1940.  His
permanent  address  is  340  Weaver  Street,  Larchmont,
New  York.  His  temporary  address  is  Naval  Air
Technical  Train.  Cen.,  87th  St.  and  Anthony  Ave.,
Chicago,  Illinois.

Since  his  college  days:

July  3,  1940  Sworn  into  Class  V  7  U.S.N.R.,  immediately  followed  by  a  month’s  cruise
on  the  USS  Wyoming  as  A.S.  August  10,  1940 — Midshipman,  USNR  aboard  USS
Illinois  (later  renamed  USS  Prairie  State).  June  6,  1941 — Commissioned  Ensign,
USNR,  attached  to  Naval  Air  Force  Patrol  Squadron  72,  Air  Wing  1.  (PBY  Squadron.)
Active  Service,  Newfoundland  and  Quonset,  Rhode  Island  Air  Base.  December  14,
1941  to  Hawaii.  June  10,  1942  Promoted  to  Lieutenant  Junior  Grade,  USNR.  Sep¬
tember,  1942,  to  South  Pacific,  based  at  New  Caledonia;  duty  there,  in  New  Hebrides
and  Guadalcanal.  March  1,  1943 — Promoted  to  Lieutenant,  USNR.  April,  1943.
Technical  Training  Center,  Chicago,  Illinois.  October  16,  1943  Married  Virginia  Lee
Fiske,  of  Wilmette,  Illlinois.  September  24,  1944-  Son,  John  Fiske  Brinckerhoff,  born.
Ribbons:  American  Defense  Service,  with  one  star  (Newfoundland)  American  Theater;
and  Asiatic-Pacific  Theater,  with  three  stars.

ROBERT  ALAN  CLARKE

Robert  was  born  on  March  6,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Westminster  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is  49
Western  Avenue,  Westfield,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  9  Camp  Avenue,  Quonset
Point,  Rhode  Island.

Since  his  college  days:

Upon  graduation  entered  the  employ  of  The  Torrington  Company,  Torrington,  Connecti¬
cut.  After  a  training  period  through  various  factory  departments,  he  became  Assistant
Sales  Manager,  Specialities  Division.  Left  The  Torrington  Company,  March,  1942,  to
enlist  in  the  Navy.  Married  Frances  Willcutt,  April,  1942.  Became  attached  to  the
Naval  Air  Base,  Quonset  Point,  Rhode  Island,  with  subsequent  training  at  Jacksonville,
Florida.  Rating:  Storekeeper  First  Class.  One  child  Robert  Alan  Clarke,  Jr.  Born:
January,  1944.

WAR

LEDGER

ALBERT  WILLIAM  CURRIER

WAR

LEDGER

Albert  was  born  on  July  31,  1918  and  prepared  for
college  at  Worcester  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1938  to  1939.  His  permanent  address  is  New
Ipswich,  New  Hampshire,  Post  Office,  Greenville,
New  Hampshire  (R.F.D.).

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  as  machinist  at  J.  W.  Moore  Machine  Co.,  Everett,  Massachusetts,  from
September,  1939  to  March,  1940.  Self-employed  at  New  Ipswich  building  special
machinery  from  March  to  August,  1940.  August,  1940  to  December,  1943,  at  Watertown
Arsenal  as  machinist  and  war  production  trainer.  Further  study  in  engineering  subjects
evenings  at  M.I.T.  and  Northeastern.  Since  December,  1943,  at  own  shop  in  New  Ip¬
swich  as  experimental  machinist  on  automatic  machinery  for  Independent  Lock  Co.  of
Fitchburg,  Massachusetts.  Ski  instructor  at  Temple  Mountain  in  Temple,  New  Hamp¬
shire  seasons  of  1941  and  1944  on  weekends.  Built  and  operated  Ashby  Alps  Ski  Tow
at  Ashby,  Massachusetts  in  1942.  Appointed  to  National  Ski  Patrol  as  a  patrol  leader
in  1941.  Instructor  of  first  aid  for  Boston  Metropolitan  Chapter  Red  Cross,  1942-1944.

KENNETH  DORMAN

Kenneth  was  born  on  April  16,  1919  and  prepared
for  college  at  Lawrenceville.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is  19
Durham  Road,  Bronxville  8,  New  York.  His  tem¬
porary  address  is  Capt.  K.  Dorman,  0-425893,  A.P.O.
15819,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Ken  was  first  associated  with  The  Magazine  Marketing  Service  in  New  York  City,  where
he  worked  on  circulation  breakdowns  and  other  types  of  statistical  work  in  connection
with  national  magazines.  Early  in  1941,  he  joined  the  selling  force  of  the  Philadelphia
office  of  the  Pitney  Bowes  Postage  Meter  Company.  In  September,  1941,  he  was  called
on  active  duty  with  the  rank  of  Second  Lieutenant  in  the  Quartermaster  Corps  at  Camp
Lee,  Virginia.  After  a  transfer  to  the  Ordnance  Department  at  Fort  Knox,  Kentucky,
he  was  advanced  to  First  Lieutenant  as  Maintenance  Officer,  78th  Armored  Medical
Battalion.  He  then  went  to  Camp  Campbell,  Kentucky,  as  Assistant  Automotive  Officer,
20th  Armored  Division  and  later  became  Acting  Assistant,  G-4  Automotive  of  that
Division,  obtaining  his  Captaincy  in  July,  1943.  Transferred  back  to  Fort  Knox,  Ken¬
tucky,  he  is  today  Supply  Officer  of  the  Gunnery  Department,  The  Armored  School.
Incidentally,  Kenneth  is  still  a  bachelor.

PAUL  W.  FINAN

Paul  was  born  on  September  1,  1920.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address
is  27  Maple  Street,  Terryville,  Connecticut.  His
temporary  address  is  P.  W.  Finan,  E.M.  3/C,  U.S.C.G.
No.  553-993,  USS  Belfast,  P.F.  35,  c/o  Fleet  Post
Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

He  was  employed  at  the  Connecticut  Light  and  Power  Company  for  six  months  and  then
in  the  Production  Department  of  the  New  Departure  Division  of  General  Motors.

He  enlisted  in  the  U.  S.  Coast  Guard  in  August  of  1942,  and  until  recently  has  been
stationed  in  Boston,  Massachusetts,  and  Providence,  Rhode  Island.

WAC

LEDGER

GEORGE  ADAM  GROMELSKI

George  was  born  on  September  5,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Bartlett  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is
3  Perryville,  Webster,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

He  worked  in  the  Branch  Accounting  Department  of  the  American  Optical  Company
with  two  Nichols  alumni,  Francis  Fitzgerald  and  Howard  Sargent.  After  two  years  he
resigned  and  accepted  a  position  in  the  Quartermaster  Office  at  Fort  H.  G.  Wright,  New
York.  He  claimed  Dudley  Hill  had  keen  competition  from  this  island  when  deciding
which  place  was  the  windiest.  Eight  months  later  he  transferred  to  the  U.  S.  Army
Distribution  Center  at  Willimantic,  Connecticut.  This  installation  was  activated
and  commanded  by  Col.  James  L.  Conrad  until  his  assignment  overseas.  This  position
afforded  him  an  opportunity  to  work  with  Mrs.  Andrews  of  the  Nichols  business  staff.
As  a  result  of  a  physical  defect  he  has  experienced  no  military  training.  He  is  not  mar¬
ried.  He  has  often  passed  by  Nichols  at  night,  only  to  see  a  quiet,  dormant  hilltop.
He  hopes  that  soon  the  day  will  return  when  Dudley  Hill  will  be  light  again  and  Nichols
will  be  a  bustle  of  activity.

GEORGE  R.  HOLLAND,  JR.

WAC

LEDGER

George  was  born  on  May  20,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Westfield  Senior  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1938  to  June,  1940.  His
permanent  address  is  170  Harrison  Avenue,  West-
field,  New  Jersey.

Since  his  college  days:

He  has  worked  in  the  personnel  office  and  maintenance  shops  of  Calco  Chemical  Division
of  American  Cyanamid  of  Bound  Brook,  New  Jersey.  He  then  graduated  from  the  Casey
Jones  School  of  Aeronautics,  with  a  Master  Mechanic  Certificate.  The  next  three  years
were  spent  with  Civil  Service  at  the  Middletown  Air  Depot,  Middletown,  Pennsylvania,
as  an  Aircraft  Inspector,  working  on  the  Flight  Test  line  doing  final  inspections  on
aircraft  overhauled  after  war  duty.  He  continued  glee  club  work  by  singing  in  a  Metho¬
dist  Church  Choir  where  he  met  the  girl  who  is  now  his  wife.  They  have  a  third  Holland
now,  Kenneth  Lee,  who  is  four  months  old  and  tips  the  scales  at  twelve  and  a  half
pounds.  November  30,  1944,  finds  him  selected  for  military  or  naval  service.

JAMES  S.  KNIGHT

James  was  born  on  May  21,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Worcester  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is  Woods-
ville,  New  Hampshire.  His  temporary  address  is
Sgt.  J.  E.  Knight,  11039975,  9th  Dep.  Rep.  Sqdn.,
Maint.  Div.,  APO  636,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,
New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  by  Jones  and  Lamson,  Springfield,  Vermont,  until  June  10,  1942,  when  he
enlisted  in  the  Air  Corps.  He  was  sent  to  Miami,  Florida,  for  basic  training.  From
there  he  went  to  Ohio  Institute  of  Aeronautics,  Columbus,  Ohio,  and  finished  his  train¬
ing  as  an  engineman.  He  spent  several  months  in  San  Antonio,  Texas,  and  Robinsfield,
Georgia,  before  going  overseas,  October,  1943.  He  is  not  married.

DONALD  F.  LEAKE

Donald  was  born  on  November  24,  1915  and  prepared
for  college  at  Higgins  Classical,  U.  of  M.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent
address  is  24  King  Street,  Worcester,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  Sgt.  D.  F.  Leake,  31146505,
Company  “B”,  148th  Med.  Tng.  Bn.,  Fort  Lewis,
Washington.

Since  his  college  days:

Salesman  for  Luden’s  Cough  Drop  Company,  Massachusetts.  Entered  Army,  August  3,

1942.  Military  Police  until  recently,  now  is  Supply  Sergeant  at  Fort  Lewis,  Tacoma,

Washington.  He  is  not  married.  At  Fort  Ethan  Allen,  Vermont,  a  year  as  Supply
Sergeant  and  Military  Police.  Camp  Edwards,  one  year  as  Military  Police.  Present
time  at  Fort  Lewis,  Washington.

LEDGER

JOHN  P.  LEAROYD

John  was  born  on  December  30,  1918  and  prepared
for  college  at  Hebron  Academy.  He  attended  Nich¬
ols  from  September,  1938  to  June,  1940.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  144  Colon  Street,  Beverly,  Massa¬
chusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

I  have  worked  for  a  law  firm  and  am  now  with  the  West  Lynn  Works  of  the  General
Electric  Company.  I  served  fourteen  months  in  the  Army  at  Fort  Benning,  Georgia,
being  discharged  the  25th  of  November  last  year.  It  was  an  Honorable  Discharge.
I  am  not  married  nor  engaged  right  now.

FAIRLIE  DINNING  LOCKHART,  JR.

Fairlie  was  born  on  June  26,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Manhasset  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address
is  92  Clapham  Avenue,  Manhasset,  Long  Island,  New

WAD

IEDLEL

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduation  was  employed  by  W.  R.  Grace  and  Co.  Entered  the  U.  S.  Army,
February  20,  1941,  assigned  to  Co.  K,  9th  Infantry,  2nd  Division  at  Fort  Sam  Houston,
Texas,  where  he  received  his  basic  training.  The  division  was  then  transferred  to  Camp
McCoy,  Wisconsin,  and  October,  1943,  was  shipped  overseas  where  they  received  further
training  in  Northern  Ireland.  While  there  he  was  made  a  Sergeant.  From  Ireland  the
division  was  sent  to  England  where  they  remained  until  June  7,  1944,  when  the  invasion
of  France  took  place.  Was  in  battle  continuously  from  June  7th  to  August  3d,  when
wounded.  Has  been  awarded  the  Purple  Heart  and  expects  to  rejoin  his  regiment  now
on  their  way  to  Berlin.

Editor's  note:  Fairlee  was  taken  prisoner  on  December  17,  1944,  in  the  “Belgian  Bulge.”
He  was  liberated  April  13,  1945,  in  Germany.

DUNCAN  T.  MACDONALD

Duncan  was  born  on  December  31,  1918  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  Suffield.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1938  to  1939.  His  permanent  address  is  133
Walker  Street,  Manchester,  Connecticut.

Since  his  college  days:

Enlisted  in  the  Navy,  June  1,  1941,  serving  at  Newport  Naval  Hospital,  Newport  Tor¬
pedo  Station,  Brooklyn,  New  York  Navy  Hospital,  Navy  Department,  Washington,
D.  C.,  Bethseda,  Maryland,  Hospital.  Discharged  May  28,  1943,  for  Medical  Reasons.
Now  employed  by  the  Connecticut  State  Highway  Department.  Married  to  Miss  Flora
Wallace,  Millinocket  Maine.  Duncan  Taylor,  Jr.,  born  August  19,  1944.

WILLIAM  JOHN  MacINNIS,  JK.

William  was  born  on  March  14,  1919  and  prepared
for  college  at  Beacon  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is  8
Hovey  Street,  Gloucester,  Massachusetts.  His  tem¬
porary  address  is  S/Sgt.  W.  J.  Maclnnis,  Jr.,  31002050,
Adm.  Sec.  “B”,  P.O.  No.  2,  558  AAF-BU,  FD— ATC,
Municipal  Airport,  Nashville,  Tennessee.

Since  his  college  days:

Bill  entered  the  Army  November  19,  1940.  After  serving  a  year  he  was  transferred  to
the  Reserve  and  got  a  job  with  the  Suburban  Gas  &  Electric  Co.  at  Revere,  Massachu¬
setts.  The  attack  on  Pearl  Harbor  the  next  month  caused  his  re-call  and  in  October,

1942,  he  left  the  United  States  and  was  next  heard  from  at  a  South  African  port  on  his

way  to  the  Middle  East.  His  destination  was  Palestine  and  letters  from  him  told  of  MAI

visits  to  Jerusalem,  Nazareth,  Bethlehem,  the  Mount  of  Olives,  Jericho,  Garden  of  |  fDGCC

Gethsemane,  Tel  Aviv  and  the  Dead  Sea.  He  is  now  a  Staff  Sergeant  in  the  Middle

East.  A  recent  letter  said  he  had  spent  his  first  furlough  in  two  years  in  Alexandria,

Egypt.

Editor's  note:  Bill  is  back  in  this  country  now,  stationed  in  Tennessee.

BERNARD  AUSTIN  Me  ALPINE

Bernard  was  born  on  June  8,  1918  and  prepared  for
college  at  Concord,  New  Hampshire.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is

11023711,  H/S  Co.,  165th  Engr.  Combat.  Br.,  A. P.O.
403,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

From  June,  1940  to  October,  1940,  he  was  manager  of  McAlpin  Arms,  York  Beach,
Maine.  From  October,  1940  to  March,  1941,  he  was  Assistant  Manager  of  McAlpine
Warehouse  and  Apartments  at  103  North  State  Street,  Concord,  New  Hampshire.  On
March  6,  1941,  he  entered  the  United  States  Army.  He  has  attended  Army  schools  in
the  following  states:  Vermont,  Massachusetts,  Connecticut,  Mississippi,  Tennessee,  and
Kentucky.  From  Kentucky  he  was  sent  overseas  to  England  and  from  there  across  the
channel  to  somewhere  in  France,  where  he  is  now  at  the  present  writing.  He  is  still
single.

Employed  at  the  Toledo  Steel  Tube  Co.  after  college.  Entered  the  Army  in  September,
1941,  serving  in  the  Infantry  for  six  months.  Married  to  Christine  Close  in  March,  1942,
at  Delmonte,  California.  Transferred  to  the  Air  Corps  as  an  Aviation  Cadet.  Washed
out  of  pilot  training  and  became  a  Link  Trainer  instructor  before  entering  anti-aircraft
Officers’  Candidate  School  in  April,  1943.  Received  commission  in  August  and  was  as¬
signed  to  a  half-track  outfit.  Transferred  to  ordnance  in  March,  1944,  when  many
anti-aircraft  units  were  dissolved,  and  attended  ammunition  school  at  Aberdeen,  Mary¬
land.  Assigned  to  ammunition  company  at  Fort  Bragg,  North  Carolina,  at  the  present
time.  Has  a  son,  George  F.  McKisson,  Jr.,  five  months  old.

RICHARD  A.  McLELLAN

Richard  was  born  on  August  3,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Newton  High  School.  He  attended  Nich¬
ols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is
36  Winchester  Street,  Brookline  46,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduating  from  Nichols,  Dick  graduated  from  the  Syracuse  University  School  of
Business  Administration  in  the  class  of  1942  where  he  was  a  member  of  Sigma  Phi
Epsilon  Fraternity.  In  April,  1942,  he  enlisted  in  the  Naval  Reserve  V-7  Class  and  re¬
ceived  a  medical  discharge  in  July,  1942.  At  present  he  is  working  for  the  New  England
Mutual  Life  Insurance  Company  in  Boston  as  an  underwriter.

CHARLES  MOLESWORTH  MEN  AG  1 1

Charles  was  born  on  January  4,  1944  and  prepared
for  college  at  Newark  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  October  1,  1938  to  June  15,  1940.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  20  Park  Road,  Maplewood,  New
Jersey.  His  temporary  address  is  U.S.S.L.C.I.  (L)
420,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

In  the  Fall  of  1940,  he  entered  Franklin  and  Marshall  College  at  Lancaster,  Pennsyl¬
vania,  as  a  junior  in  the  course  in  Business  Administration  and  completed  this  year.  In
the  second  selective  service  draft  he  was  No.  39,  the  seventh  number  called  and  he  im¬
mediately  enlisted  in  the  U.  S.  Naval  Reserve  in  New  York  City.  During  his  college
vacations  he  had  been  employed  by  the  Standard  Oil  Co.  of  New  Jersey  and  at  the
time  of  his  enlistment  was  with  them.  He  was  sworn  in  on  September  18,  1941,  as  a
Third  Class  Seaman  and  called  for  active  duty  on  December  7,  1941,  and  served  for
almost  two  years  in  censorship.  He  was  later  transferred  to  Bainbridge,  Maryland,  for
further  training.  As  a  second  class  petty  officer,  he  was  assigned  to  a  Lt.  Commander  in
charge  of  a  fleet  of  L.C.I.(L)s  and  stationed  at  the  Solomon  Island  base  in  Maryland.
Eventually  going  overseas  for  invasion  duty,  he  took  part  in  the  invasion  of  Normandy
on  June  6,  1944,  (D  Day).  Since  that  time  he  has  been  stationed  in  the  European  Thea¬
ter  of  war.  On  August  1,  1944,  he  was  promoted  to  a  First  Class  Petty  Officer.

L.  GORDON  MILLER,  JR.

Gordon  was  born  on  August  23,  1918  and  prepared
for  college  at  Wooster  School,  Danbury,  Connecticut.
He  attended  Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  Rural  Route  No.  1,  Loveland,  Ohio.

Since  his  college  days:

Started  to  work  for  Wright  Aeronautical  Corporation  on  August  23,  1940.  Became
engaged  to  Mary  Marcy  Smith  of  Glen  Ridge,  New  Jersey,  on  April  5,  1941.  Was  trans¬
ferred  to  Wright  Aeronautical  Corporation,  Cincinnati  Plant,  on  April  15,  1941.  Was
married  in  Glen  Ridge,  New  Jersey,  on  October  25,  1941.  Tom  Hill,  Nichols  1941,  was
best  man.  Ken  Applegate,  Nichols  1941  and  Lou  Spencer,  Nichols  1940,  were  ushers.
A  son,  L.  Gordon  Miller,  III,  was  born  in  Cincinnati,  on  October  11,  1942.  In  May,
1944,  was  classified  as  SBF  by  the  Army.  Am  a  Process  Engineer  in  the  Production
Engineering  Department.

A

SAMUEL  LYMAN  MUNSON,  III

Samuel  was  born  on  February  5,  1918  and  prepared
for  college  at  Lenox  School,  Lenox,  Massachusetts.
He  attended  Nichols  from  September,  1938  to  June,
1940.  His  permanent  address  is  563  Providence
Street,  Albany,  New  York.  His  temporary  address
is  S.  L.  Munson,  III,  Y  3/c,  S.L.M.,  U.S.N.R.,
U.S.S.-P.C.  488,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  New  York,
New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduation  in  1940  from  Nichols,  Sam  entered  the  junior  class  of  the  University  of
Virginia.  In  January,  of  his  senior  year,  1942,  just  after  Pearl  Harbor,  he  enlisted  in
the  Navy  and  in  May  left  for  training.  In  July,  landed  in  a  naval  hospital  for  an  opera¬
tion.  Out,  and  by  Thanksgiving,  shoved  off  on  a  P.C.  from  Staten  Island  for  “parts  un¬
known.”  Sam  was  out  of  the  Continental  United  States  for  fifteen  months,  convoying,
WA  *  guarding  the  South  Atlantic  waters  and  eventually  seeing  interesting  ports,  etc.  The  snap-

g  I  I  I  I  shot  of  him  was  taken  on  his  P.C.  in  Rio.  Someday  you  will  like  hearing  some  of  his

experiences.  Last  January,  Sam  was  home  on  his  first  leave.  The  ship  was  overhauled
and  off  they  shoved — only  to  be  rammed  and  several  sent  to  a  hospital.  At  this  writing,
rumor  has  it  he’s  headed  North,  perhaps  towards  home.  He  is  not  married.  Says  Sam,
“Let’s  get  this  mess  over  and  get  home — there  is  time  for  a  job  and  a  wife!”  and  let’s
hope  it  won’t  be  long  before  he,  his  brother  in  England,  and  all  other  brothers  are  home
— safe.

JAMES  J.  OWENS,  JR.

James  was  born  on  February  28,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  St.  Paul’s  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is  14
Quimby  Street,  Haverhill,  Massachusetts.  His  tem¬
porary  address  is  4th  Ferrying  Group,  Municipal
Airport,  Memphis,  Tennessee.

Since  his  college  days:

Jim  worked  for  the  Coca  Cola  concern  in  New  Britain,  Connecticut,  the  fall  of  1941.
On  January  19,  1942,  he  enlisted  in  the  Army  Air  Corps  and  was  sent  to  Selma,  Alabama,
for  his  initial  training.  He  spent  the  year  of  1942  as  a  Cadet  in  the  Army  Air  Corps
and  received  his  wings  and  commission  as  a  Second  Lieutenant  in  January,  1943.  He
was  assigned  to  the  4th  Ferrying  Group  at  Memphis,  Tennessee,  after  receiving  his
commission.  Since  that  time  has  has  been  ferrying  planes  throughout  this  country  and
overseas  to  Africa,  Egypt,  Russia,  India,  England,  and  China.  He  received  his  pro¬
motion  to  First  Lieutenant  in  March  of  1944.  He  is  married  to  the  former  Margaret
Costello  of  Bradford,  Massachusetts,  and  has  one  son,  James  J.  Owens,  III.

ROGER  ANDERSON  SANRORN

Roger  was  born  on  April  7,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Manchester,  New  Hampshire.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is
608  Central  Street,  Manchester,  New  Hampshire.
His  temporary  address  is  Lt.  Roger  A.  Sanborn,
A-01321252,  Co.  G,  86th  Inf.,  Camp  Swift,  Texas.

Since  his  college  days:

Roger  worked  a  year  for  the  Granite  State  Optical  Company  in  Manchester,  New
Hampshire,  then  he  did  social  service  work  in  the  A.Y.H.  and  also  in  the  South  End
House,  Boston,  Massachusetts.  He  went  through  basic  training  in  the  Naval  Air
Corps  at  Squantum,  Massachusetts,  from  which  he  was  discharged.  Later  in  November,

1942,  he  enlisted  in  the  Army  and  received  his  basic  training  at  Camp  Croft,  North  WAt

Carolina,  and  took  Officers  Training  at  Fort  Benning,  Georgia.  After  he  received  his  |  |  |  (  |  |
commission  he  was  transferred  to  the  Mountain  and  Ski  Troops  at  Camp  Hale,  Colorado,
and  from  there  to  Camp  Swift,  Texas.  Roger  married  a  Colorado  girl  in  April,  1944,
and  she  is  staying  with  him  in  Texas.

ROBERT  READ  SHAW

Robert  was  born  on  July  27,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Hope  High,  Providence,  Rhode  Island.
He  attended  Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  7  Arnold  Street,  Providence,  Rhode
Island.  His  temporary  address  is  Capt.  R.  R.  Shaw,
0-428769,  1330th  A.A.F.  Base  Unit,  ATC-ICD,

Squadron  “B”,  APO  466,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,
New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Immediately  after  graduating  from  Nichols,  Read  became  associated  with  The  Providence  Mutual  Fire
Insurance  Co.,  Providence,  Rhode  Island.  Enlisted  in  103  Field  Artillery,  R.  I.  N.  G.,  in  November,  1940.
Appointed  Aviation  Cadet,  U.  S.  Army  Air  Force,  March  17,  1941.  Primary  training  at  Darr  Aero  Tech.
Albany,  Georgia.  Basic  training  at  Gunter  Field,  Montgomery,  Alabama,  and  advanced  training  at
Barksdale  Field,  Shreveport,  Louisiana,  in  two  engine  planes,  receiving  his  pilot’s  wings  and  commission
as  Second  Lieutenant  on  October  31,  1941.  Spent  two  months  in  training  at  Jackson,  Mississippi.  In
January,  1942,  assigned  to  the  Ferry  Command  based  at  Long  Beach,  California,  ferrying  planes  to  all
parts  of  the  United  States  and  to  Australia.  In  November,  1942,  promoted  to  First  Lieutenant  and  trans¬
ferred  to  the  4th  Ferrying  Group,  Memphis,  Tennessee.  Married  in  Memphis  to  Miss  Helen  Nemey  of
Attleboro,  Massachusetts,  December  23,  1942.  Made  many  trips  over  the  South  Atlantic  delivering
planes  to  Africa  and  Middle  East.  Promoted  to  Captain  in  June,  1943.  October,  1943,  assigned  to  four
engine  planes  in  which  he  made  many  flights  over  the  North  Atlantic  to  England  and  Scotland.  July,
1944,  transferred  to  St.  Joseph,  Missouri,  for  further  training  in  Air  Transport  Command.  Daughter  born
July  27,  1944.  September  1,  1944,  transferred  to  Reno,  Nevada,  in  preparation  for  foreign  duty.
Editor’s  note:  Read  was  sent  overseas  in  October,  1944,  and  is  now  based  in  India  as  a  pilot  in  the  Air
Transport  Command.

ROBERT  LAWRENCE  SPARKS

Robert  was  born  on  May  8,  1918  and  prepared  for
college  at  Wakefield  High  and  St.  Johnsbury  Academy,
St.  Johnsbury,  Vermont.  He  attended  Nichols  from
1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is  24  Stedman
Street,  Wakefield,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary
address  is  S/Sgt.  Robert  L.  Sparks,  20115639,  Hq.
Sq.  19,  Service  Group,  Casual  Replacement  Center,
A.P.O.  650  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Bob  associated  himself  with  the  Sun  Life  Assurance  Co.,  of  Canada,  at  their  New  Haven
Connecticut,  office  in  the  fall  after  graduation  from  Nichols.  As  his  draft  number  for
Army  Service  was  a  low  one,  indicating  that  he  would  be  called  early,  he  enlisted  in  the
service  in  January,  1941,  and  was  in  the  first  group  to  go  to  Camp  Edwards  when  the
camp  opened.  In  January,  1942,  he  went  to  Australia  and  thence  to  New  Caledonia
I  [)  where  he  remained  for  a  year  and  a  half.  He  returned  to  this  country  for  six  months;

at  the  end  of  which  time  he  was  sent  to  North  Africa,  Corsica  and  Italy  where  he  is  at
the  present  time  (August,  1944),  in  the  Headquarters  Squadron  of  the  Air  Force.

April  9,  1942.  Became  Supply  Sergeant  in  the  Ground  Crew  of  the  Air  Force,  November,
1942.  Went  overseas  April,  1943,  and  is  at  present  stationed  in  England.

WALLACE  CHARLES  STEBBINS

Wallace  was  born  on  October  13,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Turners  Falls  High  School.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  September,  1938  to  June,  1940.
His  permanent  address  is  12  High  Street,  Millers
Falls,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is
Rm.  2/c  W.  C.  Stebbins,  W.T.S.  Hamblen  Detail,
Newport,  Rhode  Island.

Since  his  college  days:

Worked  in  office  of  Millers  Falls  Co.,  Greenfield,  Massachusetts,  from  July  1,  1940  to
April  5,  1941.  Worked  in  office  of  Millers  Falls  Paper  Co.,  Millers  Falls,  Massachusetts,
from  April  7,  1941  to  April  25,  1942.  He  enlisted  in  the  Navy,  April  27,  1942,  and  re¬
ceived  his  basic  training  at  Newport,  Rhode  Island.  On  May  31  he  was  transferred  to
Fargo  Barracks  at  South  Boston  and  attended  Massachusetts  Naval  Radio  and  Tele¬
graph  School  and  was  one  of  twenty  who  graduated  from  a  large  class  with  a  rating  of
Petty  Officer,  third  class  radioman.  On  November  1,  1942,  he  left  New  York  to  serve
as  a  radioman  at  a  Navy  land  base  in  North  Africa,  and  still  holds  that  same  position.
Editor’s  note:  After  serving  twenty-six  months  in  Africa,  he  returned  to  this  country
and  is  now  serving  in  Newport,  Rhode  Island,  as  2d  Class  Radioman.

BERNARD  F.  STICKELS

National  Bank  where  he  was  employed  when  he  entered  the  Armed  Forces,  April  23,

ROBERT  DAVIS  TAFT

Robert  was  born  on  February  6,  1918  and  prepared
for  college  at  Worcester  Classical  High.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address
is  86  Moore  Avenue,  Worcester,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  T/Sgt.  Robert  D.  Taft,
31186784,  436th  T.C.C.  Group,  79th  Squadron,
A.P.O.  133,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  from  September,  1940  to  October,  1942,  in  Purchasing  and  Service  Depart¬
ments  of  Leland  Gifford  Co.,  Worcester,  Massachusetts.  Inducted  into  U.  S.  Armed
Forces  at  Fort  Devens,  October  27,  1942.  Assigned  to  Air  Corps  and  sent  to  Miami,
Florida.  Trained  at  Gulfport  Field,  Mississippi;  Douglas  Aircraft  Co.,  Long  Beach,
California;  Kearns  Field,  Utah;  Baer  Field,  Fort  Wayne,  Indiana;  and  Laurenburg-
Maxton  Army  Air  Base,  Maxton,  North  Carolina.  Married  to  Miss  Dorothy  V.  New¬
ton,  of  Shrewsbury,  Massachusetts,  on  August  25,  1943,  in  Shrewsbury  Congregational
Church.  Assigned  to  Troop  Carrier  Command,  and  specialized  as  a  mechanic  for  trans¬
port  planes.  Flew  overseas  as  crew  chief  of  C-47  plane  via  South  America  and  Africa
in  December,  1943,  and  arrived  in  England  in  January,  1944.  Took  part  in  “D”  day
operations.  Was  one  of  selected  group  for  special  mission  to  Italy  and  Southern  France,
in  July  and  August.  Now  in  England.

THOMAS  I).  SWEET

college  at  Moses  Brown  School  and  Wilbraham
Academy.  His  permanent  address  is  69  Dryden
Avenue,  Pawtucket,  Rhode  Island.  His  temporary
address  is  3d  Engine  Overhaul  Sqdn.,  15th  Air  Depot
Group,  A.P.O.  922,  c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,
California.

Since  his  college  days:

During  his  vacation  he  attended  Kinyons  Commercial  School  for  Typing  and  Shorthand,
which  has  been  of  great  help  to  him  in  his  work  with  the  Providence  Journal  reporting
sports,  before  entering  the  service.  He  entered  the  service  August  25,  1942,  and  was
assigned  to  the  Air  Corps.  He  had  his  basic  training  at  Keesler  Field,  Mississippi,  and
at  New  Orleans,  Air  Base,  where  he  was  chief  clerk  of  his  Squadron.  He  is  now  work¬
ing  along  the  same  line  including  his  sports  reporting  and  Official  Scoring.  He  arrived
in  Australia,  July  5,  1943,  where  he  has  been  ever  since.  He  is  not  married.

ADRIANO  VALLE  LOPEZ

for  college  at  Belen  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address

entre  13  7  15,  Miraman,  Havana.

man,  making  me  feel  very  proud  of  him  and  of  his  two  years  of  Nichols.  Next  year  he
will  probably  take  a  two  months’  vacation  to  go  over  to  the  States  and  be  among  you
for  a  while.”

BICKFORD  GLOVER  WHITE

Bickford  was  born  on  October  19,  1919  and  prepared
for  college  at  Newton  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1938  to  1940.  His  permanent  address
is  25  Sumner  Street,  Newton  Center,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  Lt.  (jg)  B.  G.  White,  VF  85,
c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Was  employed  by  Hood  Rubber  Co.,  Watertown,  Massachusetts.  Enlisted  in  the  Naval  Reserve  the  day
following  the  Jap  attack  on  Pearl  Harbor,  trained  at  Squantum  and  Atlanta  Air  Bases  and  was  made  an
Ensign  in  December,  1942,  at  Lee  Field,  Jacksonville,  Florida.  The  Carrier  he  was  on  last  February
had  the  rudder  blown  off  by  a  Jap  sub  near  Truk  so  they  hurried  back  to  Pearl  Harbor  for  repairs,  then  he
was  transferred  to  the  Atlantic  Coast  where  he  spent  most  of  the  summer  at  Otis  Field  training  bomber
and  fighting  pilots.  He  then  went  back  to  the  Pacific  on  the  new  carrier  Shangri  La  and  is  at  present
somewhere  between  Hawaii  and  China.  Was  awarded  Air  Medal,  accompanying  citation  which  was  “for
meritorious  achievement  in  the  line  of  his  profession  and  for  especially  courageous  and  meritorious  con¬
duct  under  fire,  on  an  attack  near  Truk  on  February  16,  1941,  he  pressed  home  his  attack  against  an  enemy
light  cruiser  and  in  spite  of  heavy  anti-aircraft  fire,  scored  a  direct  hit  which  stopped  all  gunfire  from  the
Cruiser  and  left  it  dead  on  the  water.  This  allowed  an  aerial  torpedo  attack  to  be  launched  unopposed
which  sank  the  Cruiser.  His  cool  and  effective  performance  of  duty  while  under  fire  with  total  disregard
for  his  personal  safety,  were  in  keeping  with  the  highest  traditions  of  the  Naval  Service.”  Bicky  was
married  on  June  3,  1943,  in  Coronado,  California,  to  Barbara  Hobbs  of  Arlington,  Massachusetts.

CHARLES  ROGER  WILLIAMS,  JR.

Charles  was  born  on  July  27,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Hope  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1938  to  June,  1940.  His  permanent
address  is  21  Mount  Hope  Avenue,  Providence,
Rhode  Island.  His  temporary  address  is  310  Ferrying
Squadron,  APO  635,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,
New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Rog  went  to  work  for  Swift  &  Co.  after  graduation  and  stayed  there  until  March,  1941.
then  with  American  Bitumuls  Co.  for  a  few  weeks  and  to  Brown  &  Sharpe  Mfg.  Co.
until  induction  on  June  25th.  From  Devens  he  was  sent  to  Camp  Lee,  Virginia,  Quarter¬
master  Regiment  and  in  December  he  transferred  to  Fort  Davis,  Rhode  Island.  While
home  on  a  furlough  in  November  his  engagement  to  Martha  Wheaton  Young  of  Provi¬
dence  was  announced.  In  May,  1942,  he  went  to  Maxwell  Field  for  pilot  training.
Roger  and  Martha  were  married  November  28th  and  then  he  went  to  OCS,  Miami  Beach,
where  he  was  commissioned  a  Second  Lieutenant,  in  the  Army  Air  Forces  in  March,
1943.  Then  followed  a  short  course  at  the  School  of  Applied  Tactics,  Orlando,  a  brief
stay  at  Atlantic  City,  and  overseas  to  England  the  latter  part  of  May.  On  September
1st  of  this  year  he  was  promoted  to  First  Lieutenant.  He  has  met  several  friends  over
there,  among  them,  Reed  Shaw  and  Bob  Taft.

WAR

LEDGER

WARREN  S.  WOOLLEY

Warren  was  born  on  April  7,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Newark  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1938  to  June,  1940.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  38  South  Walnut  Street,  East  Orange,
New  Jersey.

WAR

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

After  having  a  summer  vacation,  he  started  to  work  for  the  American  Sugar  Refining
Company  in  their  Cost  Accounting  Division.  In  the  summer  of  1942,  he  married  Miss
Catherine  H.  Frissell  of  Dudley,  Massachusetts.  In  the  fall  of  1943,  Rutgers  University
accepted  his  credits  and  he  is  now  working  at  night  for  a  degree.  Shortly  after  the
beginning  of  the  new  year,  he  started  to  work  for  Price,  Waterhouse  and  Company  as  an
accountant.  On  July  17,  1944,  a  baby  son  was  born  in  Orange,  New  Jersey.  His  name
is  Warren  Hubert.

Class  of  1941

KENNETH  POMEROY  APPLEGATE,  JR.

Kenneth  was  born  on  April  4,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Wooster.  He  attended  Nichols  from
September,  1939  to  June,  1941.  His  permanent
address  is  308  North  Quaker  Lane,  West  Hartford,
Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is  Lt.  (jg)
K.  P.  Applegate,  VPB  125,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,
New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  at  Veeder-Root,  Inc.,  Hartford,  Connecticut.  Aviation  Cadet,  U.S.N.R.:
Iowa  Pre-Flight,  School,  June-September,  1942;  Olathe,  Kansas,  September,  1942-
January,  1943;  Corpus  Christi,  Texas,  January,  1943-May,  1943.  Ensign  U.S.N.,  May,
1943-August,  1944.  Lieutenant  Junior  Grade,  August,  1944.  He  has  had  bomber
patrol  duty  at  Manteo,  North  Carolina,  Cherry  Point,  North  Carolina,  and  at  Boca
WAC  Chica,  Florida,  in  addition  to  his  present  duty  overseas.  He  married  Janet  Campbell

I  |0||  Kane  on  June  5,  1943,  at  Hartford,  Connecticut.  William  Mount  Applegate  born  at

Hartford,  Connecticut,  June  6,  1944.

FREDERICK  WARREN  BITTNER

Frederick  was  born  on  July  9,  1922  and  prepared  for
college  at  Lyndhurst  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address
is  635  Second  Avenue,  Lyndhurst,  New  Jersey.  His
temporary  address  is  S/s  F.  W.  Bittner,  P.O.W.  2466,
Stalag  Luft  6,  Germany.

Since  his  college  days:

Worked  for  H.  Baker  Linen  House,  New  York  City,  C02  Fire  Extinguishers,  Newark,
New  Jersey,  Photogravure  &  Color  Co.,  New  York  City.  Enlisted  in  Army,  September,
10,  1942 ;  sent  to  Camp  Upton,  Miami  Beach,  then  to  AAF  Flexible  Gunnery  School,  Fort
Meyer,  Florida.  Graduated,  November  15,  1942.  Then  to  Salt  Lake  City  to  U.  S.  Air
Forces  Technical  School.  Graduated  19th  day  of  December,  1942.  Then  to  Denver,
Colorado,  Pierre,  South  Dakota,  Rapid  City,  South  Dakota,  Geiger  Field,  Spokane,  Wash¬
ington,  Walla  Walla,  Washington,  Blythe,  California,  Herrington,  Kansas.  Had  his
first  furlough  in  July,  1943.  Went  overseas  to  England,  November,  1943.  Was  tail
gunner  on  the  Flying  Fortress  “Slightly  Dangerous.”  Wears  the  Air  Medal  and  two
Oak  Leaf  Clusters  and  had  taken  part  in  seventeen  missions  before  his  plane  was  shot
down  over  Berlin  on  March  4,  1944.  On  April  13th,  his  parents  were  notified  their  son
was  a  prisoner  in  Germany.

WILLIAM  MORROW  RUCHER

William  was  born  on  April  13,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  New  Mexico  Military  Institute.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1940.  His  permanent
address  is  305  Riverside  Drive,  New  York,  New  York.
His  temporary  address  is  Lt.  William  M.  Bucher,  A.C.,
47th  T.  C.  Sq.,  313  T.  C.  Gr.,  APO  133,  c/o  Post¬
master,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Bill  was  called  to  active  duty  in  1941  as  a  Second  Lieutenant  in  the  Cavalry.  He  later
transferred  to  the  Air  Corps  and  received  his  wings  as  a  Glider  Pilot.  He  has  been  in
the  European  Area  since  the  Spring  of  1944,  attached  to  the  47th  Troop  Carrier  Squadron.

WALTER  GRAY  RUCKLE Y,  JR.

Walter  was  born  on  December  15,  1919  and  prepared
for  college  at  Mount  Hermon.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is  9  Hill
Avenue,  Southbridge,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary
address  is  T/5  Gray  Buckley,  31061878,  Hq.  Co.,  24th
Armored  Eng.  Bn.,  A.P.O.  254,  c/o  Postmaster,
New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Immediately  following  graduation  he  began  working  for  Hygrade-Sylvania  of  Salem,
where  he  remained  until  entering  the  Army  on  February  5,  1942.  On  June  13,  1942,  he
was  married  to  Miss  Phyllis  Whiteoak  of  Southbridge,  and  on  April  28,  1943,  Walter
Gray  Buckley,  III,  or  “Buck,”  arrived.  The  family  remained  together  much  of  the  time
until  Gray  went  overseas,  shortly  after  Christmas,  1943.

HAROLD  A.  CAMPBELL,  JR.

Harold  was  born  on  April  28,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Valley  Forge  Military  Academy.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent
address  is  1629  Watchung  Avenue,  Plainfield,  New
Jersey.  His  temporary  address  is  A  Bty,  436th  A. A. A.,
A.P.O.  758,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Was  employed  in  the  purchasing  department  of  the  Ingersoll  Rand  Company,  Phillips-
burg,  New  Jersey,  from  graduation  to  November,  1941.  Entered  the  Army  on  Novem¬
ber  10,  1941.  Attended  O.C.S.  and  received  his  commission  as  Second  Lieutenant  in
the  anti-aircraft  artillery  in  July,  1942.  Took  part  in  the  African  invasion,  landing  near
^  Casa  Blanca  in  November,  1942.  Landed  with  invasion  forces  in  Sicily,  July  10,  1943.

Was  promoted  to  First  Lieutenant  while  in  Sicily  and  moved  from  there  to  Italy  early
LEDGER  in  1944.  Present  location  indefinite  but  believe  he  is  now  in  France  with  the  Seventh

Army.

(BILL)  STUART  SHAW  CAVES,  JR.

Bill  was  born  on  May  13,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Massanutten  Military  Academy,  Woodstock
Virginia.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.
His  permanent  address  is  East  Bloomfield,  New  York.
Business  address,  Holcomb,  New  York.  His  tem¬
porary  address  is  Lt.  Stuart  S.  Caves,  Jr.,  2044th
Q.  M.  Trk.,  Co.  Avn.,  A.P.O.  149,  c/o  Postmaster,
New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

From  June,  1941-January  1,  1944,  was  associated  with  the  Stuart  S.  Caves  Lumber
Corporation  at  Holcomb,  New  York.  Enlisted  December  31,  1941,  as  Truckmaster
at  Grenier  Field,  Manchester,  New  Hampshire.  Was  called  January  20,  1942,  and  was
located  at  Manchester  until  September  28.  Sent  to  Q.  M.  Officer  Candidate  School  at
Camp  Lee,  Virginia,  and  commissioned  a  Second  Lieutenant  in  Quartermaster  Transporta¬
tion  and  attached  to  the  Air  Corps.  January  10,  1943,  reported  to  Atlantic  City  as
Transportation  Officer.  June  13,  1943,  was  transferred  to  Goldsboro,  North  Carolina.
January  26th  was  made  First  Lieutenant  and  in  March  sent  to  Kelly  Field,  Texas,  where
he  Picked  UP  a  new  Company  and  sailed  for  England  in  April  and  has  been  stationed  in
,J  5Pl|  England  since.  Bill  was  married  to  Miss  Mary  Beth  Wood  of  East  Bloomfield,  August

25,  1942  and  welcomed  a  daughter,  Susan,  December  8,  1943.

ALLAN  BERNARD  CLARK

Allan  was  born  on  October  24,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Bordentown  Military  Institute.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1940.
His  permanent  address  is  97  Oakwood  Avenue,  West
Hartford  6,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is
Station  Hospital,  AAF  Pilot  School  (Spec.  4E),
Courtland  Army  Air  Field,  Courtland,  Alabama.

Since  his  college  days:

Attended  Morse  Business  College,  Hartford,  Connecticut,  September,  1940  to  June,
1941.  Employed  at  Pratt  &  Whitney,  West  Hartford,  Connecticut,  from  June,  1941  to
October,  1941.  Inducted  in  the  Army  14  October,  1941.  Received  Basic  Training  at
Camp  Lee,  Virginia  (Medical  Department).  First  station  after  basic  training  Hendricks
Field,  Sebring,  Florida.  Attended  Medical  Administrative  Corps  Officers  Candidate
School,  Camp  Barkeley,  Texas,  from  7  September,  1942  to  25  November,  1942.  As¬
signed  to  Courtland  Army  Air  Field  10  December,  1942.  Promoted  to  rank  of  First
Lieutenant  20  July,  1943,  and  on  25  May,  1944,  promoted  to  the  rank  of  Captain.
Married  to  Elizabeth  Brown  of  Hartford,  Connecticut,  19  November,  1941,  at  Rich¬
mond,  Virginia.  Son  born,  David  Allan,  26  July,  1944,  at  Decatur,  Alabama.  At  the
present  time  Captain  and  Mrs.  Clark  are  living  at  1506  29th  Street,  Sheffield,  Alabama.
Captain  Clark  is  both  Adjutant  and  Registrar  at  the  Courtland  Army  Air  Field  Hospital.

DON  J.  CURTIS

Don  was  born  on  February  18,  1922  and  prepared
for  college  at  Mount  Hermon.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is  1439
Northampton  Street,  Holyoke,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  1st  Lt.  D.  J.  Curtis,  0720203,
738th  Bomb  Squadron,  454th  Bomb  Group,  APO
520,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Don  took  Primary  and  Secondary  C.P.T.  training  before  entering  the  Army  in  January
1943,  as  an  Aviation  Cadet.  He  received  his  commission  as  Second  Lieutenant  and  his
Pilot’s  wings  at  Frederick  Oklahoma,  in  April,  1944.  From  there  he  went  to  B-24
Transition  School  in  Fort  Worth,  Texas.  At  present  he  is  stationed  at  the  Army  Air
Base,  near  Mountain  Home,  Idaho,  where  he  and  his  crew  are  finishing  their  final  phase
of  training  in  a  Liberator.

I.EDGER

ALLEN  F.  DIEFENDERFER,  JR.

Allen  was  born  on  March  5,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Montclair  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is
105  Inwood  Avenue,  Upper  Montclair,  New  Jersey.
His  temporary  address  is  T/Sgt.  Allen  F.  Diefender-
fer,  Jr.,  U.S.M.C.  Air  Station,  Edenton,  North
Carolina.

Since  his  college  days:

Went  into  the  advertising  field  in  July,  1941.  After  Pearl  Harbor  attack  in  December,
1941,  applied  for  enlistment  in  the  United  States  Marine  Corps  and  was  sworn  into  the
Corps  April  22,  1942.  Had  basic  training  at  Parris  Island,  South  Carolina,  and  then
was  assigned  to  the  Marine  Corps  Air  Station  at  Quantico,  Virginia.  Had  course  of
training  at  Sound  Motion  Picture  Technicians  School  at  the  Marine  Barracks,  Navy
Yard,  Brooklyn,  New  York,  in  the  Fall  of  1942,  returning  to  Quantico  upon  completion
of  the  course,  and  in  April,  1943,  was  transferred  to  a  new  Marine  Air  Base  at  Edenton,
North  Carolina,  where  he  now  is  in  charge  of  the  Training  Film  Library  for  Marine
Operational  Training  Group  81.

CHARLES  FREDERIC  EDGARTON

Charles  was  born  on  June  17,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Milton  Academy,  Massachusetts.  He
attended  Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1941.
His  permanent  address  is  Nashawtuc  Road,  Concord,
Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  Naval
R.O.T.C.,  Box  848,  Holy  Cross  College,  Worcester,
Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

Enlisted  in  U.  S.  Naval  Reserve  as  Seaman  1st  Class  following  graduation  in  June,
1941.  Shipped  aboard  USS  Bowdoin  for  defence  work  in  Greenland,  leaving  Portsmouth
Navy  Yard,  June,  28  1941.  Returned  to  Portsmouth  just  prior  to  Pearl  Harbor.  Ship
in  dry  dock  for  repairs  most  of  that  winter.  Spring,  1942,  transferred  to  the  Y.P.  222
with  rating  of  Coxswain.  On  Shore  Patrol,  based  at  Lockwood  Basin,  East  Boston,
until  February,  1943,  when  transferred  to  Northern  Patrol  based  at  Bar  Harbor,  Maine.
Promoted  to  Boatswain’s  Mate  2nd  Class,  September,  1942.  In  May,  1943,  recommended
by  Commanding  Officer  of  Base  for  Navy  V-12  Officer  Training  and  assigned  to  Bates
College  where  he  report  July  1,  1943.  Back  to  the  “Grind”  again  for  two  terms  at  Bates.
March  1,  1944,  transferred  to  Naval  R.O.T.C.  at  Holy  Cross  from  which  place,  with
luck,  should  receive  Commission  of  Ensign,  USNR,  sometime  in  1945.

JAMES  A.  FALCONER,  JR.

James  was  born  on  August  7,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Classical  High  School,  Springfield,  Massa¬
chusetts.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.
His  permanent  address  is  37  Lincoln  Park,  Long-
meadow,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is
Radioman  1/c,  USS  SC  629,  Fleet  Post  Office,  San
Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Worked  in  a  paper  mill  in  Maine  until  his  enlistment  September,  1941.  Not  married.
Has  been  based  in  the  Pacific  since  1942.  He  is  on  a  sub-chaser.  He  corresponds  with
Mr.  Manhard  every  month.

Editor’s  note:  Most  recent  information  says  that  Jimmy  “misses  Mr.  Manhard  very
much.”  Also  he  left  the  629  and  was  awaiting  a  new  assignment.

WAR

LEDGER

ALFRED  R.  FISHEL

Alfred  was  born  on  September  24,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  East  High  School,  Cleveland,  Ohio.
He  attended  Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,
1941.  His  permanent  address  is  1513  East  115th
Street,  Cleveland,  Ohio.  His.  temporary  address  is
Alfred  R.  Fishel,  1513  East  115th  Street,  Cleveland,
Ohio.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduation  from  Nichols,  Alfred  worked  for  a  manufacturing  concern  in  Cleveland
for  a  short  time.  He  then  went  to  Dyke  School  of  Business  and  completed  a  course
in  shorthand  and  typing.  In  July,  1942,  he  enlisted  in  the  Army,  receiving  his  training
in  the  Signal  Corps  at  Camp  Crowder,  Missouri.  Then  he  was  transferred  to  Tucson,
Arizona,  and  attached  to  the  Air  Corps.  At  the  end  of  October,  1942,  he  was  shipped
overseas,  arriving  in  North  Africa  the  second  week  of  the  invasion.  Shortly  after  his
arrival  overseas  he  was  promoted  to  the  rank  of  Sergeant.  His  unit  traveled  across
North  Africa,  then  to  Sicily,  and  at  the  present  time  is  in  Corsica.  Most  of  the  time
he  has  been  a  teletype  operator  and  has  done  some  work  in  message  centre.

Editor’s  note:  A1  has  received  a  medical  discharge  after  twenty-three  months  of  foreign
service  and  three  months  of  service  in  the  States.

RICHARD  BRADFORD  FISHER,  JR.

college  at  Emerson  School  in  Exeter,  New  Hampshire,

Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  Co.  D,
346  Engineers  (GS),  Serial  No.  31095071,  A.P.O.  350,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

With  Victor  G.  Bloede  Co.,  Inc.,  Baltimore,  Maryland.  Trained  with  Engineer  Corps
in  Alexandria,  Louisiana,  May,  1942.  In  England,  August,  1942-June,  1944.  In  France
June,  1944.

JOHN  SPEAR  FRASER

John  was  born  on  July  3,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Hillhouse  and  Woodbridge  Country  Day
School.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1940  to  1941.
His  permanent  address  is  Woodbridge,  New  Haven,
Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is  Cpl.  John  A.
Fraser,  A.S.N.  31407173,  339th  Harbor  Craft  Co.,
A.P.O.  168,  c/o  of  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Jack  worked  at  the  Whitney  Blake  Co.  in  New  Haven,  Connecticut,  a  short  time  after
leaving  college.  Due  to  his  interest  in  Aeronautical  Engineering  he  took  a  course  in
Bridgeport,  Connecticut.  He  worked  at  Gruman  Aircraft  Corp.,  Bethpage,  Long  Island,
for  a  year  and  a  half,  also  learned  to  fly  seaplanes.  Shortly  after  the  Bristol  Aeronautical
Corp.  came  to  New  Haven,  Connecticut,  he  joined  their  organization  and  was  with  them
until  October,  1943.  In  November,  1943,  he  joined  the  Army  and  trained  at  Amphibious
Training  Center,  Camp  Gordon  Johnston,  Florida.  He  left  for  overseas  in  May,  1944,
and  was  in  England  for  a  few  months.  He  is  now  somewhere  in  France.

EDWARD  G.  FUNK

Edward  was  born  on  August  21,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Bristol  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1941.  His
permanent  address  is  38  Carleton  Place,  Bristol,
Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is  Headquarters
Company,  2nd  Battalion,  24th  Marine  Regiment,
4th  Marine  Division,  F.M.F.,  c/o  F.P.O.,  San  Fran¬
cisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Ed  was  employed  in  the  sales  department  office  of  the  New  Departure  Division  of  Gen¬
eral  Motors  until  he  enlisted  in  the  U.  S.  Marines  on  May  1,  1942.  He  received  his  “boot”
training  at  Parris  Island,  South  Carolina,  and  was  assigned  to  Paymaster  Department
there,  where  he  was  promoted  to  the  rank  of  Corporal.  On  December  1,  1942,  he  vol-
teered  for  overseas  combat  service  and  was  sent  to  Camp  Lejeune,  New  River,  North
Carolina,  as  a  Drill  Instructor.  Ed  was  assigned  to  Camp  Pendleton  in  California,  in
February,  1943,  to  join  the  Infantry-Headquarters  Company,  Intelligence  Section.
He  went  overseas  to  participate  in  the  invasion  of  the  Marshall  Islands,  battles  of
Namour  and  Roi  and  the  invasion  of  Saipan  and  Tinian  Islands.

for  college  at  Langley  High  School,  Pittsburgh,  Penn¬
sylvania.  He  attended  Nichols  from  September,
1939  to  June,  1940.  His  permanent  address  is  308
Riverview  Drive,  New  Kensington,  Pennsylvania.
His  temporary  address  is  A.S.N.  33236099,  2971  Fin.

Since  his  college  days:

After  attending  Nichols  Junior  College  he  continued  his  educational  courses  at  the
University  of  Pittsburgh.  He  was  attending  the  University  of  Pittsburgh  when  he  en¬
tered  the  U.  S.  Army  on  April  22,  1942.  He  has  been  in  the  armed  service  continuously
since  that  date  and  has  been  overseas  since  November,  1942.

HOWARD  J.  HALL,  JR.

Howard  was  born  on  July  13,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Ashville  School  for  Boys.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is
25  Warren  Place,  Montclair,  New  Jersey.  His
temporary  address  is  Pfc.  Howard  I.  Hall,  Jr.,
32182615,  Co.  “B,”  15th  Engr.  Bn.,  APO  9,  9th  Div.,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

In  July,  1941,  he  sailed  for  Honolulu  and  upon  his  return  in  August  he  enlisted  in  the
Army  as  a  volunteer.  He  then  entered  his  father’s  business  and  after  six  weeks  he  was
called  to  service.  He  entered  the  Army,  October  3,  1941,  trained  at  Belvoir  in  Virginia,
then  to  Fort  Bragg,  North  Carolina.  In  December,  1942,  he  went  overseas  and  has  seen
combat  in  Africa,  Sicily,  and  is  now  in  France,  having  been  in  the  invasion  with  troops
that  took  Cherbourg.

DEAN  WILLIAM  I1ANAFORD

Dean  was  born  on  April  10,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Hope  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is  52
Mount  Hope  Avenue,  Providence,  Rhode  Island.
His  temporary  address  is  Company  D,  141st  Med.
Tng.  Bn.,  ASFTC,  Ft.  Lewis,  Washington.

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  by  Brown  &  Sharpe  Mfg.  Co.  for  fourteen  months  in  the  general  office.
Drafted  into  the  Army  in  November,  1942,  and  reported  at  the  Fort  Devens  Reception
Center.  Became  DEML  and  served  thirteen  months  at  the  Fort  Devens  Armed  Forces
Induction  District.  Following  the  closing  of  that  station  he  was  sent  to  the  New  Haven
Armed  Forces  Induction  District;  remaining  in  recruiting  service.  In  April,  1944,  he
was  sent  to  the  1108th  Service  Command  Unit  at  Fort  Adams,  Rhode  Island,  Hq.  HD
of  Narragansett  Bay.  Qualified  for  overseas  duty  he  reported  to  Fort  Devens  for  re¬
assignment  and  sent  to  the  Medical  Training  Section,  ASFTC,  Fort  Lewis,  Washington,
where  he  is  stationed  at  the  present  time,  having  completed  medical  training,  and  await¬
ing  subsequent  overseas  duty.

I  EDGE  15

CARLTON  LEE  HAYWARD

Carlton  was  born  on  December  6,  1917  and  prepared
for  college  at  The  Huntington  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1941.  His
permanent  address  is  7  Kipling  Road,  Wellesley
Hills,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is
Panagra,  Limatambo,  Lima,  Peru,  South  America,
Box  6.

Since  his  college  days:

Started  C.P.T.  during  his  senior  year  and  continued  at  Worcester  Tech,  after  graduation,
receiving  his  commercial  pilot’s  license  in  December.  Signed  with  Pan-American  Airways,
January,  1942,  for  service  with  the  Pan-African  Corps  and  left  in  February  for  Africa,
carrying  supplies  and  military  personnel  from  British  West  Africa  to  Cairo  and  east  to
India.  Remaining  until  December,  1942,  when  the  Army  took  over.  Returned  to  Bos¬
ton  and  signed  with  Pan-American  Grace.  Spent  two  months  at  Forth  Worth  training.
Married  Marguerite  Jennings  of  Wellesley  Hills,  at  Forth  Worth,  on  February  26,  1943.
Carlton  and  his  wife  left  for  Lima,  Peru  in  March  where  they  are  now  living.  He  is  now
flying  from  the  Canal  Zone  to  Chile  and  Buenos  Aires.

Editor’s  note:  Jefferson  Lee  Hayward  was  born  April  23,  1945.

THOMAS  S.  HILL

Thomas  was  born  on  February  16,  1919  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  Albany  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is
R.D.  1,  Averill  Park,  New  York.  His  temporary
address  is  T/Sgt.  Thos.  S.  Hill,  U.S.M.C.R.,  V.M.F.
121,  M.A.G.  11,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  San  Francisco,
California.

Since  his  college  days:

Tom  worked  with  his  Dad  in  the  Office  and  Engineering  Supply  Business  at  Troy,  New
York,  up  to  the  time  when  he  enlisted  with  the  U.  S.  Marines,  immediately  after  Pearl
Harbor.  He  is  still  single  and  claims  that  no  one  will  have  him.  He  is  attached  to  the
Air  Arm  of  the  Marine  Corps  and  was  a  member  of  that  famous  squadron  121,  command-
ed  by  Major  “Joe”  Foss  on  Guadalcanal  during  the  terrific  fighting  of  the  Fall  of  1942.
I  I  I  I  I  Stationed  at  Henderson  Field,  Tom  and  his  companions  were  under  constant  bombard¬

ment  from  the  sea  and  from  the  air.  He  is  a  member  of  the  First  Division  and  wears
the  Presidential  Citation.  After  a  nine  months  stay  in  the  States,  Tom  is  again  engaged
in  active  duty  in  the  Pacific,  and  would  like  to  hear  from  his  old  friends.

ROBERT  S.  HOWLAND

Robert  was  born  on  January  24,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Hebron  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1938  to  June,  1941.  His
permanent  address  is  25  Massachusetts  Avenue,
Walpole,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is
SK,  2nd  U.S.N.R.,  N.A.S.,  Banana  River,  Florida.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduating  from  Nichols  Bob  applied  as  a  flyer  in  Uncle  Sam’s  Navy.  However,
before  he  was  accepted  it  was  necessary  for  him  to  undergo  an  operation.  He  was  op¬
erated  on  in  October  and  was  not  active  until  July  of  the  following  year.  He  entered
the  Navy  in  July,  1942,  and  was  assigned  as  an  instructor  of  boot  trainees  at  Newport,
Rhode  Island.  He  was  transferred  to  an  air  base  in  Fort  Lauderdale,  Florida,  as  SK
2nd  class  in  the  Commissary  Department  in  November,  1943.  He  was  transferred  again
this  August  to  Banana  River,  Florida,  where  he  is  at  present.  He  is  unmarried  and  has
two  brothers  in  the  Navy.

DAVID  NEAL  IVERSON,  JR.

David  was  born  on  March  20,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Peekskill  Military  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address
is  2  Wykagyl  Terrace,  New  Rochelle,  New  York.
His  temporary  address  is  Hq.  &  Hq.  Detch.,  O.S.S.,
A.P.O.,  413,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days :

David  went  directly  into  the  Army,  being  commissioned  a  Second  Lieutenant  in  the
Quartermaster  Corps.  He  was  attached  to  the  44th,  Division  and  went  through  the  man¬
euvers  in  the  Carolinas  until  returning  to  Fort  Dix  in  December,  1941.  Toward  the  end
of  January,  1942,  his  Division  was  transferred  to  Camp  Claibourne,  Louisiana.  He
remained  there  until  May  when  he  was  transferred  to  Camp  Barkley,  Texas,  and  attached
to  the  55th  Q.M.  Heavy  Maintenance  Regiment.  In  less  than  a  month’s  time  he  was  WAR
back  in  Camp  Dix  and  left  for  overseas  in  June,  1942.  He  has  apparently  been  in  and  LEDGER
out  of  the  United  Kingdom  many  times  during  the  past  two  and  one-quarter  years  as  he
has  written  of  days  being  terrifically  hot  and  frightfully  cold  in  the  places  he  has  been.

He  has,  of  course,  not  been  able  to  mention  the  names  or  locations  of  such  places.  Some
time  in  April  or  May  he  was  attached  to  Hq.  &  Hq.  Detch.,  O.S.S.,  the  same  unit  to
which  Ensign  Arthur  Wurtmann  is  attached  and  until  recently  Arthur  and  David  shared
a  flat  in  London.  It  was  through  Arthur  that  David  became  attached  to  the  Office  of
Strategic  Services.  His  last  letter  indicated  he  might  go  to  France  or  be  home  shortly.

ROBERT  HOWE  JAMES

Robert  was  born  on  September  13,  1921.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent
address  islO  Devon  Road,  Leominster,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  Sgt.  Robert  H.  Janes,  855
South  Broadway,  Bartow,  Florida.

Since  his  college  days:

Bob  went  to  work  for  his  father  at  the  Leominster  Daily  Enterprise  Co.  soon  after  his
graduation  in  1941.  On  March  23,  1942,  he  enlisted  in  the  Army  Air  Force  Cadets  as
a  Pilot,  but  in  Basic  Flying  he  was  eliminated  and  transferred  to  the  ground  crew  as  a
clerk.  In  three  months  time  Bob  worked  up  to  the  grade  of  Corporal  and  was  sent  to
an  Engineering  and  Operations  Clerical  School  at  Central  State  Teachers  College,  Okla¬
homa.  At  the  completion  of  the  course  he  was  transferred  to  the  56th  Fighter  Sq.,
54th  Fighter  Gp.  at  Bartow,  Florida,  where  Bob  has  been  stationed  since  May,  1943.
On  August  15,  1943,  Bob  married  Miss  Marjorie  Thurlow  of  Leominster,  Massachusetts.
Dean  W.  Hanaford,  ’41,  who  was  his  roommate  was  best  man.  Bob  is  now  a  Sergeant
and  is  residing  with  his  wife  in  Bartow  where  he  is  Chief  Clerk  of  the  Sq.  O  Engineering
Office.

RICHAKI)  BURNS  JOHNSTON

Richard  was  born  on  April  3,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Bradford,  Pennsylvania.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is
157  Congress  Street,  Bradford,  Pennsylvania.

WAR

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

Visited  San  Diego,  California,  in  1940.  Remained  there  as  a  flyer  at  Ryan  School  of
Aeronautics.  Entered  the  armed  forces  in  1942  and  is  a  Lieutenant  in  the  Field  Artillery.
Recently  was  returned  to  the  United  States  after  spending  more  than  a  year  in  the
Mediterranean  Theater,  where  he  saw  considerable  action  as  Executive  Officer  of  a
light  howitzer  battery,  in  a  veteran  division  of  the  African  and  Italian  campaigns.
Lieutenant  Johnston  is  married  and  has  two  children,  Lael  Dianne  and  Richard  Burns
Johnston,  Jr.

JOHN  STEPHEN  KELLEHER

John  was  born  on  November  19,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Deerfield  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address
is  221  Main  Street,  South  Deerfield,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  S/Sgt.  J.  S.  Kelleher,  311-
86529,  721  Bomb  Sq.,  450  Bomb  Gp.,  APO  520,  c/o
Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  leaving  Nichols  John  had  a  position  in  the  Greenfield  Tap  &  Die  Co.  He  worked
in  the  administration  department  while  there.  October,  1942,  John  was  inducted  in  the
Army.  He  was  sent  to  Miami  Beach,  Florida,  for  his  basic  training,  and  later  was  sent
to  Oklahoma  A.  &  M.  to  school.  Later  he  was  transferred  to  Clovis,  New  Mexico,  and
from  there  to  Alamagordo,  New  Mexico.  In  November,  1943,  he  was  sent  overseas  and
is  now  stationed  somewhere  in  Italy.

RALPH  OTTO  KINDLER

Ralph  was  born  on  December  21,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Bartlett  High.  Webster,  Massachusetts.
He  attended  Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,
1941.  His  permanent  address  is  9  Mt.  Pleasant  Street,
Webster,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is
T/4  R.  O.  Kindler,  31255545,  APO  627,  Z  Force,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Ralph  assisted  his  father  in  the  Kindler  Hardware  &  Plumbing  Business,  then  went  to  the
shipyards  in  Quincy,  Massachusetts,  where  he  did  sheetmetal  work.  He  was  inducted
into  the  Army  in  December,  1942,  in  the  Engineers  Corps  and  trained  at  Fort  Jackson,
South  Carolina.  Here  he  was  made  a  Corporal.  He  volunteered  for  overseas  duty  and
was  accepted  and  arrived  in  North  Africa  in  October,  1943,  thence  to  India  and  finally
to  China,  where  he  now  is.  In  China  Ralph  attended  a  school  for  the  training  of  Chinese
soldiers  in  the  use  of  American  fire-arms.  Ralph  has  recently  become  Sergeant  Techni¬
cian.  He  is  attached  to  the  Chinese  Army.
