PHILIP  MERRILL  KYLE

Philip  was  born  on  May  13,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Newton  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September  1939,  to  June,  1941.  His  permanent
address  is  119  Austin  Street,  Newtonville,  Massa¬
chusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  Philip  M.  Kyle,
0-817973,  305  T.C.S.,  442  T.C.Gr.,  APO  133,  c/o
Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Philip  took  the  Civilian  Pilot  Training  course  at  Nichols,  got  his  license  and  hoped  to
continue  there.  Finally  he  volunteered  in  the  Army  Air  Corps.  While  awaiting  call  he
took  a  course  in  welding  at  Wentworth  Institute  in  Boston  and  worked  in  navy  yards  in
Portland,  Brooklyn  and  Boston.  He  was  accepted  as  Aviation  Cadet  in  March,  1943.
He  got  his  pilot’s  wings  and  second  lieutenant’s  commission  at  Marianna,  Florida,  in
March,  1944,  as  a  fighter  pilot.  His  first  assignment  was  to  the  Troop  Carrier  Com¬
mand  as  a  pilot  of  a  C-47  Troop  Carrier.  He  flew  to  England  via  South  America  and
North  Africa  in  May,  1944,  and  his  present  base  is  near  Birmingham,  England.  He
expected  to  drop  paratroopers  behind  the  enemy  lines,  tow  gliders  and  carry  back  the
wounded.  In  May  this  year,  Philip  announced  his  engagement  to  Miss  Nancy  Peirce
of  Arlington,  Massachusetts.

WILLIAM  M.  LEVY,  3D

LEDGER

William  was  born  on  August  19,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Taft  School,  Watertown,  Connecticut.
He  attended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  119  Court  Street,  Plattsburg,  New
York.  His  temporary  address  is  William  M.  Levy,  3d,
0-1050343,  13th  Traffic  Reg.  Group,  APO  887,  c/o
Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  leaving  Nichols,  Bill  worked  in  Boston  until  February,  1942,  at  which  time  he
enlisted  in  the  Army.  He  had  his  basic  training  in  the  Infantry  at  Fort  McClellan,  Ala¬
bama.  In  October  of  the  same  year,  he  entered  Anti-Aircraft  Officer’s  Candidate  School
from  which  he  received  his  Commission  as  Second  Lieutenant  in  January.  Bill  was  sent  to
the  Canal  Zone  where  he  manned  the  guns  for  four  months  in  the  jungle.  Following  his
return  to  the  States  in  October,  1943,  he  was  transferred  to  the  13th  Traffic  Regulation
Group  and  sent  overseas  in  May.  For  three  months  he  was  stationed  in  England  and
at  the  present  time  is  in  France.

STEPHEN  VIELE  LEWIS,  II

Stephen  was  born  on  July  19,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Albany  Academy,  Albany,  New  York.  He
attended  Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1941.
His  permanent  address  is  275  Pawling  Avenue,  Troy,
New  York.  His  temporary  address  is  Cpl.  S.  V.  Lewis,
2nd,  Section  L,  BMC  No.  3,  Boca  Raton  Field,
Florida.

Since  his  college  days:

July,  1941  to  December,  1941,  attended  Stenotype  School.  Then  worked  for  The  Ready-
Jell  Mfg.  Co.  and  for  W.  &  L.  E.  Gurley,  both  of  Troy,  New  York.  Worked  for  a  short
time  as  an  insurance  investigator  and  then  entered  business  with  his  father  as  partner
in  Read-Lewis  Machine  Company  of  Troy,  manufacturers  of  Army  Ordnance.  Enlisted
in  the  Army  in  September,  1942,  and  attended  Radio  School  in  Troy  and  New  York
City,  (Signal  Corps),  and  at  Camp  Crowder  until  June,  1943.  Entered  University  of
Chicago  (ASTP  Course),  and  in  February,  1944,  transferred  to  Truax  Field  at  Madison,
Wisconsin.  Attended  Pre-Radar  School  there  and  at  Chanute  Field,  Illinois  until  August,
1944.  Since  that  date  at  Boca  Raton,  Florida,  in  Radar  School.  Promoted  to  Corporal,
September,  1944.  Unmarried.

LEDGER

JOHN  ROBERT  McCANN

John  was  April  13,  1921  and  prepared  for  college  at
St.  Bernard’s  High.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1939
to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is  612  Westminster
Street,  Fitchburg,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary
address  is  Welch  Convalescent  Hospital,  Daytona
Beach,  Florida.

Since  his  college  days:

John  was  employed  by  the  Eastern  Steamship  Company  of  Boston  at  the  time  of  his
enlistment  into  the  Army  in  March,  1942.  After  completing  his  basic  training  at  Camp
Lee,  Virginia,  he  was  sent  overseas.  He  was  stationed  at  Iceland  and  England  before
going  to  North  Africa.  He  was  in  Libia  and  took  part  in  the  Tunisian  Campaign.  He
served  with  the  1st  Armored  Ordnance  Division,  as  well  as  with  the  British  8th  Army.
Last  June  he  was  rotated  back  to  the  States,  after  two  years  overseas.  He  is  now  at
Daytona  Beach,  Florida.

WAR

LEDGER

RAYMOND  CAMON  MILLER

Raymond  was  born  on  October  21,  1919  and  prepared
for  college  at  Ridgefield  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is  Cannon-
dale,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is  Base
Operation  AAB,  Bedford,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

Raymond  entered  the  employ  of  Gilbert  and  Bennett  Mfg.  Co.  as  assistant  secretary,  at
Georgetown,  Connecticut,  in  July,  1941,  where  he  remained  until  his  induction  into  the
Army  on  January  12,  1943.  He  received  his  training  at  Miami  Beach,  Florida,  and
Stillwater,  Oklahoma.  Then  he  was  stationed  at  the  Flying  Field  at  Manchester,  New
Hampshire,  for  awhile,  and  has  since  been  at  the  Base  Operation  at  Bedford,  Massa¬
chusetts.  He  is  now  Corporal.  He  was  married  to  Lois  Gimpel  of  Norwalk,  Connecticut,
in  July,  1943,  and  now  has  a  daughter,  Dianne,  two  weeks  old.

HARRY  AUSTIN  MISTCHER

Harry  was  born  on  October  7,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Bordentown  Military  Institute.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  September  1939  to  June,  1941,
His  permanent  address  is  22  North  Hillside  Avenue,
Chatham,  New  Jersey.

Since  his  college  days:

August,  1941  to  March,  1942,  Accounting  Clerk,  Sperry  Products,  Inc.,  Hoboken,  New
Jersey.  March,  1942  to  June,  1942,  U.  S.  Army  Field  Artillery  Replacement  Center,
Fort  Bragg,  South  Carolina.  Honorable  Discharge,  June  23,  1942.  July,  1942  to  July,
1943.  Statement  Clerk,  Public  Service  Electric  and  Gas  Co.,  Newark,  New  Jersey.
July,  1943  to  present,  Time  Study  Engineer,  Elastic  Stop  Nut  Corp.  of  America,  Union,
New  Jersey.  At  present  I  am  single  and  living  with  my  parents.

ROBERT  MOLLOY

Robert  was  born  on  June  26,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  McBurney’s,  New  York,  New  York.  He
attended  Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  February,
1940.  His  permanent  address  is  12-161  60th  Street,
Beechhurst,  Long  Island,  New  York.  His  temporary
address  is  Pfc.  Robert  Molloy,  12127951,  21st  Signal
Service  Company,  APO  862,  c/o  Postmaster,  New
York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

He  attended  DeForest  Training  School,  Chicago.  Went  to  work  for  Western  Electric
Co.,  New  York,  and  later  in  Washington.  Enlisted  in  a  telephone  unit  of  Signal  Corps,
August,  1942.  September,  1942,  was  sent  to  Newfoundland  and  is  still  there.

ALFRED  EDWARD  MONAHAN

Alfred  was  born  on  December  1,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  St.  Bernard  High,  Fitchburg,  Massa¬
chusetts.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1940  to  1941.
His  permanent  address  is  717  Boston  Street,  Lynn,
Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  Sec.  H,
Club  P.  O.,  Boca  Raton  Field,  Florida.

Since  his  college  days:

Attended  Northeastern  while  employed  by  General  Electric  Co.  at  Lynn,  Massachusetts.
Married  in  November,  1942.  Entered  U.  S.  Army,  March,  1943  and  now  in  the  Air
Corps.  Commissioned  Second  Lieutenant  in  May,  1944.  Has  a  daughter  born  in
June,  1944.

JOHN  L.  MORRIS

John  was  born  on  August  29,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Wilbraham  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1939  to  June,  1941.  His  permanent
address  is  20  Arnoldale  Road,  West  Hartford  7,
Connecticut.

Since  his  college  days:

Upon  graduation  from  Nichols,  John  immediately  was  employed  by  the  Hartford
Machine  Screw  Company.  He  was  hired  as  a  piece  work  checker  by  the  Payroll  Depart¬
ment.  In  December,  1941,  he  transferred  to  the  Production  Department  of  the  Com¬
pany  as  a  stock  chaser.  In  October,  1943,  John  transferred  again  to  the  Grinding  De-
partment  where  he  remained  until  he  terminated  with  the  Company  in  April,  1944.
M  In  June,  1944,  he  accepted  an  offer  by  the  Service  Department  of  the  Pratt  &  Whitney

LEDGER  Aircraft,  East  Hartford,  Connecticut.  He  is  now  in  training  for  the  job  having  already

completed  several  courses  in  the  Company’s  schools.  John  is  not  married,  and  he  is
now  living  at  home.

HOWARD  RANDLETT  MORSE,  JR.

Howard  was  born  on  June  16,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Loomis  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is  The
Island,  Windsor,  Connecticut.

Since  his  college  days:

Randy  joined  the  Air  Corps  in  November,  1941;  then  he  attended  flying  school  in  East
St.  Louis,  Randolph  Field,  and  Lubbock  Field.  He  was  graduated  a  pilot  in  May,  1942.
He  spent  a  short  time  at  Westover  Field  before  he  went  overseas  with  the  Troop  Carrier
Command.  In  twenty-four  months  overseas  he  was  in  England,  the  invasions  and  cam¬
paigns  of  North  Africa,  Sicily,  and  Italy,  and  with  Stillwell’s  forces  in  Burma  and  India.
He  wears  the  Asiatic  Ribbon  with  one  star,  European  with  five  stars,  American  Theater,
American  Defense,  Air  Medal  and  one  cluster,  and  the  D.F.C.  Randy,  still  unmarried,
is  now  home  on  leave,  after  which  he  will  return  to  duty  in  the  United  States.  He  has
run  into  Warren  Manhard  several  times  overseas.

Editor’s  note:  Married  Joellen  Anderson  on  October  7,  1944.

HERBERT  ALLAN  NEWELL

Herbert  was  born  on  December  18,  1919  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  Pawtucket  High  School.  He
attended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent
address  is  10  Blaisdell  Avenue,  Pawtucket,  Rhode
Island.  His  temporary  address  is  Herbert  A.  Newell,
ASN  31173253,  112th  General  Hospital,  APO  649,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  by  Louis  J.  G.  Martelle  (Real  Estate).  Entered  U.  S.  Army  on  August  25,
1942.  Stationed  at  Fort  Devens,  Massachusetts,  until  June,  1944.  Present  rank,
Sergeant.  Married  Miss  Eileen  Marian  Black  of  Pawtucket,  Rhode  Island,  on  Novem¬
ber  2,  1943.

WAI2

RONALD  EL  WOOD  NOBLE

Ronald  was  born  on  October  11,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Wethersfield  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is
100  Church  Street,  Wethersfield,  Connecticut.  His
temporary  address  is  S/Sgt.  Ronald  E.  Noble,  564th
Bomb  Sq.,  389th  Bomb  Gr.  (H),  A.P.O.  558,  c/o  Post¬
master,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Following  graduation,  Ronnie  secured  a  position  in  the  Purchasing  Department  of  the
Hamilton  Standard  Propellers,  a  branch  of  United  Aircraft  in  East  Hartford,  Connecti¬
cut.  August,  1942,  the  Army  claimed  him,  sending  him  to  Fort  Devens,  from  where  he
was  next  sent  to  Atlantic  City  for  basic  training.  Then  followed  a  series  of  location
changes:  Lowry  Field  in  Denver,  Colorado,  for  turret  technician  training;  three  months
later  to  Detroit,  Michigan,  for  more  advanced  training;  next  he  went  to  Salt  Lake  City,
Utah,  and  Biggs  Field,  Texas.  He  returned  to  Lowry  Field  then  a  final  location  in  Bruns¬
wick,  New  Jersey.  In  July,  1943,  he  went  to  England,  where  he  is  with  the  Eighth  Air
Force.  In  the  Spring  of  1944,  he,  along  with  other  members  of  his  squadron,  received  a
Presidential  Citiation  for  raids  on  the  Ploesti  Oil  Fields.

LESTER  FERRIS  ORR

Lester  was  born  on  November  10,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  McBurney  School,  New  York.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  parents’  ad¬
dress  is  9  Boulevard  Malba,  Long  Island,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Lester  devoted  his  entire  time  to  the  Navy.  Immediately  upon  graduation  he  made
application  for  flight  training.  He  was  accepted  and  reported  at  Squantum,  Massa¬
chusetts,  on  September  15,  1941.  Following  pre-flight  school  he  was  sent  to  Jacksonville
for  pilot  training.  He  received  his  commission  as  Ensign  on  May  16,  1942,  and  was  then
designated  as  Flight  Instructor  for  training  at  Jacksonville.  He  taught  at  New  Orleans,
August  5,  1942,  and  was  there  six  months.  Then  he  taught  at  Glenview,  Illinois,  for  a
year,  during  which  time  he  was  made  a  Lieutenant  Junior  Grade.  After  this  he  took
training  in  dive  bombing  at  Wildwood,  New  Jersey,  and  joined  his  carrier  group  at  Otis
Field,  Camp  Edwards,  and  while  there  received  his  full  lieutenancy.  While  engaged  in  a
routine  gunnery  flight  in  the  Pacific  Area,  his  plane  entangled  with  a  towed  target  and
part  of  the  tail  of  his  plane  was  lost  as  it  struck  the  water  at  a  steep  angle.  The  crash
in  which  Lester  lost  his  life  occurred  on  September  14,  1944.

LEONARD  BENEDICT  PANELLA,  JR.

Leonard  was  born  on  December  27,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Newton  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is
314  Elliot  Street,  Newton  Upper  Falls,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  Ens.  L.  B.  Panella,  Bombing
Squadron  136,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  San  Francisco,
California.

Since  his  college  days:

Len  has  done  a  number  of  things.  He  worked  at  the  Hood  Rubber  Co.  in  Watertown  for
one  year  and  then  volunteered  for  service  in  the  Naval  Air  Corps.  Len  started  his  train¬
ing  in  July  of  1942,  and  in  October,  1943,  he  received  his  rating  of  Ensign  from  the  Naval
Air  Training  Station  at  Corpus  Christi,  Texas.  During  his  training  he  was  stationed  in
seven  different  states  so  he’s  had  a  slight  view  of  the  country.  At  practically  every
station  he’d  write  home  and  say  he’d  met  another  one  of  his  college  pals  and  since  he’s
been  overseas  Len  wrote  to  say  how  swell  it  was  when  he  discovered  one  of  his  Nichols
classmates  stationed  with  the  Army  Unit  nearby.  Len  has  been  overseas  since  Febru¬
ary.  A  short  while  ago  we  received  a  letter  from  the  Navy  Department  saying  that  Len
has  been  missing  in  action  since  August,  19th.  Our  only  prayer  now  is  that  he  returns
to  his  base  safely  and  that  maybe  one  day  real  soon  he’ll  come  back  home  again.
Editor's  note:  We  are  happy  to  report  that  Len  is  on  duty  in  the  United  States.

HARRY  BEVINS  PEACE

Harry  was  born  on  December  11,  1918  and  prepared
for  college  at  Dwight  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1939  to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is  32-05
155  Street,  Flushing,  Long  Island,  New  York.  His
temporary  address  is  Cpl.  H.  B.  Peace,  32118084,
72nd  Q.  M.  Depot  Co.,  APO  246,  c/o  Postmaster,
San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Had  a  position  with  Home  Insurance  Co.,  59  Maiden  Lane,  New  York,  New  York.
May  5,  1941,  was  inducted  in  the  U.  S.  Army  at  Camp  Upton,  New  York.  The  following
November  6th,  Harry  was  married  to  the  former  Claire  Brannan  of  Flushing,  Long  Is¬
land.  He  was  then  stationed  at  Camp  Livingston,  Louisiana,  where  he  remained  until
he  left  for  the  Canal  Zone  where  he  spent  twenty-five  months.  Upon  his  return,  Harry
spent  some  time  at  Fort  Dix,  New  Jersey,  and  at  Elkins,  West  Virginia.  In  the  begin¬
ning  of  next  year  Harry  and  his  wife  expect  to  be  blessed  with  a  minor  edition.

Editor’s  note: A  daughter  was  born  on  February  14,  1945.

JOHN  BEACHER  PERRY,  II

John  was  born  on  September  19,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Proctor  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is  5  Alden
Roxd,  Wellesley  Hills,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary
address  is  T/Sgt.  J.  B.  Perry,  Group  1,  Squadron  86,
SAACC,  San  Antonio,  Texas.

WAR

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

Jack  worked  at  the  Hood  Rubber  Company  in  Watertown,  Massachusetts,  the  summer
of  1941,  under  the  program  sponsored  by  the  Miller  Associates.  He  received  a  scholar¬
ship  from  Babson  Institute  and  graduated  from  that  school  in  1942.  He  entered  the
U.  S.  Army  in  June,  1942,  being  sent  to  Miami,  Florida,  for  basic  training.  Then,  trans¬
ferred  to  the  U.S.A.A.F.,  he  received  radio  training  at  Sioux  Falls,  South  Dakota,  and
gunnery  training  at  Fort  Myers,  Florida.  In  the  spring  of  1943  he  was  assigned  to  a
B-26  Marauder,  and  after  further  training,  was  sent  overseas  in  February,  1944.  Now
a  Technical  Sergeant,  Jack  has  completed  more  than  fifty  combat  missions  over  Europe
as  radio-operator  gunner  on  the  Marauder  bomber  “Flying  Dutchman,”  taking  part  in
the  Ninth  Air  Force  offensive.  He  has  been  awarded  the  Air  Medal  with  one  Silver
Cluster,  and  four  Bronze  Oak  Leaf  Clusters.

FREDERICK  CHURCH  POND

Frederick  was  born  on  October  25,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Holderness  School,  Plymouth,  New
Hampshire.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.
His  permanent  address  is  11  Norwood  Road,  West
Hartford,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is
Cpl.  F.  C.  Pond,  11045443,  175th  Signal  Repair  Co.,
A.P.O.  230,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Fred  graduated  from  Nichols  College  in  June,  1941,  and  immediately  joined  the  Arrow-
Hart,  Hegeman  Electric  Co.,  Hartford,  Connecticut.  He  remained  with  this  concern
until  he  enlisted  in  January,  1942,  in  the  Signal  Corps,  U.  S.  Army.  Following  basic
training  at  Fort  Monmouth,  New  Jersey,  he  was  assigned  to  the  175th  Signal  Repair
Co.  and  trained  with  this  outfit  and  sailed  with  it  for  England  in  December,  1942.  After
further  training  there  he  sailed  for  France  with  the  same  unit  in  June,  1944.  He  is  at
present  located  with  the  U.  S.  Army  in  France.  He  is  single  and  prior  to  his  service
with  the  Armed  Forces  he  followed  the  hobby  of  Radio  building.

CHARLES  BLAKESLEE  RAZEE

Charles  was  born  on  January  30,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Woodbridge  Country  Day  School.  He
attended  Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  December,
1939.  His  permanent  address  is  Woodbridge,  Con¬
necticut.  His  temporary  address  is  Cpl.  C.  B.  Razee,
31143860,  Sqd.  B-l,  APO  19242  B,  c/o  Postmaster,
New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  leaving  Nichols  Charles  worked  for  his  father  in  the  building  business.  Then  he
went  to  Voight-Sikorsky  to  learn  sheet  metal  work  and  aircraft  maintenance,  after  which
he  worked  there  until  he  was  called  into  service  on  July  18,  1942.  He  first  went  to
Devens  then  to  Miami  Beach  for  a  few  weeks.  From  there  he  went  to  Atlantic  City.
He  was  sent  to  Bainbridge,  Georgia,  in  September,  1942,  and  is  still  there.  He  is  “Crew
Chief”  on  the  ground  service  in  the  Air  Force.  He  is  a  Corporal.

CHARLES  KENNETH  SCHOTT

Charles  was  born  on  November  17,  1919  and  prepared
for  college  at  Lawrenceville  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1941.  His
permanent  address  is  65  North  Fullerton  Street,
Montclair,  New  Jersey.  His  temporary  address  is
Headquarters  Battery,  Division  Artillery,  APO  37,
c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Upon  graduation  from  Nichols,  as  a  member  of  the  Four- Year  Plan,  he  commenced
work  with  Lever  Brothers  Company  in  Cambridge,  Massachusetts.  This  work,  how¬
ever,  was  interrupted  when  he  was  drafted  on  January  6,  1942.  After  basic  training  at
Fort  Bragg,  North  Carolina,  he  was  assigned  to  the  37th  Division  and  went  overseas
soon  after.  He  saw  action  in  New  Georgia  and  Bougainville  in  the  Solomon  Islands.
In  July,  1944,  he  was  fortunate  enough  to  be  sent  home  for  a  thirty-day  furlough,  and
then  rejoined  his  unit  in  the  Solomons.

RICHARD  HARTWELL  SEWALL

Richard  was  born  March  23,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Holderness  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1939  to  June,  1941.  His  permanent
address  is  291  Bacon  Street,  Waltham,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  Lt.  (jg)  Richard  Hartwell
Sewall,  USNR,  VB-86,  c/o  F.P.O.,  New  York,  New
York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduation,  he  was  employed  by  the  United  Shoe  Machinery  Corporation  until
his  enlistment  in  the  Naval  Air  Corps  in  March,  1942.  He  received  his  commission
as  Ensign  in  December,  1942,  and  after  three  months  of  further  training,  he  left  the
States  to  join  a  dive-bombing  squadron  in  the  South  Pacific.  Upon  his  return  to  the
States  in  April,  1944,  he  was  married,  and  after  a  month’s  leave,  he  received  orders  to
1_EDGEE>  join  a  carrier-based  squadron  forming  on  the  East  Coast.

HAROLD  SIDNEY  SHEFFIELD

Harold  was  born  on  December  17,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Mt.  Hermon  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is
85  Halsted  Street,  East  Orange,  New  Jersey.  His
temporary  address  is  4th  Marine  Regt.,  c/o  Fleet
Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Harold  enlisted  in  the  Marines,  January  5,  1942.  Trained  at  Parris  Island  and  left  for
South  Pacific,  June,  1942.  Has  participated  in  the  following  combats:  Tulagi,  Bougain¬
ville,  Saipan  and  Guam.  He  is  now  Sgt.  Harold  S.  Sheffield,  with  4th  Marine  Regt.
(Rein.);  1st  Marine  Brigade  (Prov.);  Regt.  Weapons  Co.;  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  San
Francisco,  California.

JAMES  BRUCE  SPILMAN

James  was  born  on  May  4,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  New  Hampton  School  for  Boys,  New  Hamp¬
ton,  New  Hampshire.  He  attended  Nichols  from  1939
to  1940.  His  permanent  address  is  145  Gibbs  Street,
Newton  Centre,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  ad¬
dress  is  Sgt.  James  Bruce  Spilman,  839th  Bomb
Squadron,  487th  Bomb  Group  (H),  A.P.O.  559,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Bruce  worked  with  Agfa  Ansco  Film  Corp.  of  Boston.  He  entered  the  service  in  1942.

On  November  13,  1943,  he  married  Dorothy  Slaney  of  Needham  Heights,  Massachu¬
setts.  He  is  now  serving  in  England  in  the  Army  of  the  United  States  as  an  aerial
photographer.

WAR

LEDGCK

HOWARD  M.  STARK  Y

Howard  was  born  on  March  11,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Lawrenceville  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address
is  2309  East  Second  Street,  Duluth,  Minnesota.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduating  I  moved  to  the  Boston  Y.M.C.A.  and  worked  in  the  Shawmut  Bank
until  February,  1942.  At  that  time  I  was  rejected  for  military  service,  and  shortly  after
I  started  working  for  the  First  and  American  National  Bank  in  Duluth.  During  my  two
years  there  I  was  both  bookkeeper  and  teller.  In  July,  1944,  I  entered  the  grain  business
as  an  employee  of  the  Capitol  Elevator  Company.  I  am  also  a  member  of  Duluth’s
Volunteer  Port  Security  Force.

EDWARDS  G.  STEINHOPE

Edwards  was  born  on  May  10,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Newton  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  1940.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  4  Briar  Lane,  Newtonville,  Massa¬
chusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  4th  AAA  Group
Hq.,  APO  512,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

WAR

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  at  Ucinte  until  his  induction  into  the  Army,  March,  1942.  From  Fort  Devens
he  was  sent  to  Camp  Stewart,  Georgia,  for  his  basic  training.  Then  to  the  West  Coast
where  he  had  the  opportunity  of  attending  the  University  of  California.  After  com¬
pleting  his  course  at  Officers  School  he  went  to  Florida  for  special  training.  In  January,
1943,  he  went  overseas  as  a  First  Lieutenant.  Campaigns  in  Africa,  Sicily,  and  Casseni
followed.  Now  a  Captain  in  Hq.  Btry.  of  the  5th  Army  in  Italy.

FREDERICK  K.  STEPHENSON,  JR.

Frederick  was  born  on  June  15,  1919  and  prepared  for
college  at  Lawrenceville  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1940  to  June,  1941.  His  permanent
address  is  25  East  77th  Street,  New  York,  New  York.
His  temporary  address  is  116  South  Continental
Avenue,  Atlantic  City,  New  Jersey.

Since  his  college  days:

Stevie  spent  his  first  summer  after  graduation  on  the  staff  of  Valley  Ranch,  Wyoming,
completing  his  fourth  summer  there.  That  Fall  he  enlisted  in  the  Army  Air  Corps,  and
after  a  brief  stay  at  Mitchell  Field  was  sent  to  Randolph  Field,  as  an  Air  Cadet.  Won
his  Wings  on  Armistice  Day,  1942.  Received  additional  training  as  a  Troop  Carrier  pilot
in  C-47  planes,  at  Alliance,  Nebraska.  Flew  to  North  Africa  in  May,  1943.  Took  part
in  the  Sicilian  and  Italian  invasions.  Awarded  the  Air  Medal  for  his  work  in  the  Sicilian
invasion.  Shortly  afterwards,  was  made  a  First  Lieutenant.  In  April,  1944,  was  trans¬
ferred  to  England.  On  August  19,  1944,  was  promoted  to  Captain.  Before  leaving  for
Randolph  Field  in  1942  his  engagement  to  Herta  M.  Drey,  a  New  York  girl,  whom  he
met  at  Valley  Ranch,  was  announced.  Their  wedding  took  place  in  San  Antonio,  Texas,
His  letters  express  a  desire  to  stay  in  aviation  work,  possibly  in  the  advertising  end.

GEORGE  ANDERSON  TIMMONS,  JR.

George  was  born  on  March  17,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Peekskill  Military  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1941.  His
permanent  address  is  Riverview  Avenue,  Peekskill,
New  York.  His  temporary  address  is  52nd  F.C.S.,
A.P.O.  637,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

He  was  associated  with  Standard  Brands,  Inc.,  of  Peekskill,  until  April,  1942,  when  he
enlisted  in  the  United  States  Air  Corps.  He  received  his  training  at  Miami  Beach,
Florida,  Dundan  Field,  Texas,  and  Jefferson  Barracks,  Missouri.  He  arrived  overseas
in  August,  1943,  and  is  with  an  English  A.A.F.  Fighter  Wing,  “somewhere  in  England.”
Three  times  he  has  shared  in  the  Commendations  this  Eighth  A.A.F.  Fighter  Wing  has
earned.  One  Commendation  was  delivered  by  Lt.  Gen.  James  H.  Doolittle.  He  is
assigned  to  the  operations  room  of  the  Eighth  Fighter  Command’s  oldest  operational
Control  Fighter  Wing,  as  a  plotter  in  Air-Sea  Rescue.

PAUL  TREUMAN

Paul  was  born  on  September  15,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  John  Burroughs  School,  St.  Louis.
He  attended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  46  Crestwood  Drive,  Clayton  5,
Missouri.  His  temporary  address  is  Pvt.  P.  Treu-
man,  37386074,  Btry.  13-692  F.  A.  Bn.,  APO  339,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Paul  worked  for  Rice-Stix  Dry  Goods  Co.,  St.  Louis,  from  August,  1941  to  September,
1942,  as  apprentice  to  a  traveling  man.  Joined  the  Armed  Forces  in  October,  1942.  Has
been  at  Camp  Bowie,  Fort  Sill  and  Camp  Houze,  Texas.  Is  now  on  his  way  overseas.
Not  married.

ROBERT  ARMSTRONG  TURNER

Robert  was  born  on  January  11,  1918  and  prepared
for  college  at  Huntington  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1939  to  1941.  His  permanent  address
is  44  Harris  Street,  Brookline,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  Lt.  Robert  A.  Turner,  H.  &  S.
Co.,  323d  Eng.  Bn.,  APO  98,  c/o  Postmaster,  San

Since  his  college  days:

Bob  worked  a  few  months  for  Kellog  Corn  Flakes  Co.  as  a  salesman  until  his  enlistment
in  the  regular  Army,  May  1,  1942.  He  served  in  the  8th  Armored  Division  at  Fort  Knoxt
graduated  from  the  Engineers’  School  at  Fort  Belvoir,  and  also  served  at  Camp  Chaffee
and  went  overseas.

JOHN  H.  VANDERVEER,  JR.

John  was  born  on  October  26,  1918  and  prepared  for
college  at  Irving,  Tarrytown,  New  York.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  September,  1938  to  June,  1941.
His  permanent  address  is  114  Puritan  Avenue,  Forest
Hills,  New  York.  His  temporary  address  is  S/Sgt.  J.
H.  Vanderveer,  Jr.,  32174408,  Service  Co.,  14th  Inf.,
APO  360,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Graduated  from  Nichols,  June,  1941.  Entered  the  service  October  3,  1941.  Trained  at
Camp  Wheeler,  Georgia.  Served  eighteen  months  in  the  Canal  Zone.  In  June,  1943,
returned  to  the  States.  Stationed  at  Camp  Carson,  Colorado.  In  February,  1944,  went
to  Camp  Roberts,  California,  on  three  months’  maneuvers.  In  June,  1944,  was  trans¬
ferred  to  Fort  Benning,  Georgia,  with  a  promotion  to  rank  of  Staff  Sergeant.

Editor's  note:  John  went  overseas  with  Gen.  Patch’s  7th  Army.

WENDELL  J.  WALKER

Wendell  was  born  on  February  2,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Mt.  Vernon  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1940.  His
permanent  address  is  205  East  Vine  Street,  Mt.  Ver¬
non,  Ohio.  His  temporary  address  is  Ord.  183,  Squad
B.D.C.,  Aberdeen  Proving  Ground,  Maryland.

Since  his  college  days:

Until  the  time  he  entered  the  Army,  September  4,  1942,  Wendell  was  assistant  manager
of  his  father’s  retail  lumber  business.  Upon  entering  the  Army  he  was  assigned  as  clerk
in  Headquarters  Section,  Camp  Campbell,  Kentucky,  and  held  the  rank  of  Corporal.
On  June  2,  1944,  he  was  transferred  to  Bomb  Disposal  School,  Aberdeen  Proving  Ground,
Maryland.  Upon  completion  of  this  course  he  will  be  assigned  to  oversea  duty.  Wendell
is  engaged  to  Miss  Harriett  Graham  and  plans  to  be  married  after  returning  from  the
Service.  He  will  resume  interest  in  the  lumber  business  after  he  is  demoblized  from  the
Army.

THEODORE  W.  WALTERS

Theodore  was  born  on  May  2,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  John  Fitch  High.  His  permanent  address
is  27  Hillcrest  Road,  Windsor,  Connecticut.  His
temporary  address  is  Lt.  T.  W.  Walters,  USMCR,
Marine  Scout  Bombing  Squadron  333,  c/o  Fleet
Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Production,  Pratt  &  Whitney,  September  28,  1942.  Joined  the  Navy  as  an  Aviation
Cadet,  Pre-flight,  at  Chapel  Hill,  North  Carolina,  Anascostia,  Washington,  D.  C.  Re¬
ceived  his  “Wings”  as  pilot  at  Pensacola,  Florida,  further  training  at  Jacksonville,
Florida.  Transferred  to  Marine  Corps  as  bomber  pilot,  sent  to  Cherry  Point,  North
Carolina,  then  to  Fort  Worth,  Texas.  Ted  has  done  instructing,  testing  and  at  present
taking  six  weeks  dive  bombing  at  Port  Arthur,  Texas.  After  flying  hours,  he  is  assistant
official  aerial  photographer.

EUGENE  BATEMAN  WILLIAMS,  JR.

Eugene  was  born  on  March  19,  1919  and  prepared
for  college  at  Hill  School,  Pottstown,  Pennsylvania,
1933-1936;  Brown  and  Nichols,  1936-1938;  Bowdoin
College,  1938-1939.  He  attended  Nichols  from
September,  1939  to  June,  1941.  His  permanent
address  is  Longwood  Towers,  Brookline,  Massachu¬
setts.  His  temporary  address  is  T/Sgt.  Eugene  B.
Williams,  Jr.,  Ship’s  Permanent  Army  Staff,  USS

WAR

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

With  Fafnir  Ball  Bearing  Company,  New  Britain,  Connecticut,  until  induction  in  the
Army,  April  22,  1942.  Went  through  basic  training  at  Fort  McClellan,  Alabama.  In
July,  1942,  ordered  to  Hampton  Roads,  Port  of  Embarkation,  Newport  News,  Virginia.
Within  about  three  months  was  assigned  to  Transportation  Division  and  raised  from
Private  to  Sergeant  Technician.  In  early  1943  raised  to  Staff  Sergeant.  In  late  1943
raised  to  Technical  Sergeant  and  a  assigned  to  Ship’s  Permanent  Army  Staff  on  army
transport  Empress  of  Scotland,  delivering  troops  and  supplies  to  India,  and  returning
Singapore  evacuees  from  South  Africa  to  England.  Spring  of  1944  assigned  to  troop
transport  USS  General  Randall,  operating  between  West  Coast  ports,  India  and  South
Pacific.

JOHN  WOODBURY

John  was  born  on  January  21,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Tilton  School,  Tilton,  New  Hampshire.
He  attended  Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,
1940.  His  permanent  address  is  44  Hillcrest  Road,
Belmont  78,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address
is  Lt.  John  Woodbury,  0806571,  H.  Q.  U.S.F.,
China  Theatre,  APO  879,  c/o  Postmaster,  New
York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

In  June,  1940,  went  to  work  at  Second  National  Bank  of  Boston.  In  July  joined  Na¬
tional  Guard  with  a  group  of  boys  from  bank,  and  went  to  Plattsburg,  New  York,  for
three  weeks  of  training.  Remained  at  the  bank  until  January,  1941,  when  the  National
Guard  became  part  of  the  U.  S.  Army.  Ordered  to  Camp  Edwards  in  the  101st  Infantry.
In  August,  became  Corporal  of  Transportation.  Went  South  on  maneuvers  and  Fort
Devens.  June,  1942,  transferred  into  the  Air  Corps  and  started  training  in  September,

1942.  After  attending  the  various  schools  John  graduated  as  a  2nd  Lt.  Pilot  on  June  30,

1943,  at  Napier  Field,  Dotham,  Alabama.  Married  there  the  same  day  to  Janet  I.
Hogan  of  Southbridge,  Massachusetts.  Ordered  into  Air  Transport  Command.  June
30,  1944,  made  First  Lieutenant  in  AAF  Air  Transport  Command,  Ferrying  Division.
A  Class  V  Pilot  and  sent  overseas  August,  1944.

ARTHUR  O.  WURTMANN

Arthur  was  born  on  August  1,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Teaneck  High  School,  Teaneck.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1941.
His  permanent  address  is  269  Edgemont  Terrace,
Teaneck,  New  Jersey.  His  temporary  address  is
U.  S.  Navy,  No.  931,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  New
York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

He  went  to  P.  Lorillard  Company,  General  Office,  from  August,  1941,  to  March,  1942.
In  March,  1942,  he  became  connected  with  the  Office  of  Co-Ordinator  of  Information,
Washington,  D.  C.,  to  August  22,  1942.  This  organization  later  became  known  as  the
Office  of  Strategic  Services.  On  August  22,  1942,  the  Office  of  Strategic  Services  trans¬
ferred  him  to  their  office  in  London,  England.  In  July,  1943,  he  was  commissioned  as
Ensign  in  the  United  States  Navy.  His  experience  has  been  exceedingly  interesting  and
in  connection  with  his  duties  he  has  met  many  prominent  and  interesting  people.  On
February  22,  1944,  he  returned  to  the  United  States  on  official  business  to  Washington,
returning  to  London,  March  31,  1944.  As  to  the  kind  of  work  he  is  doing,  that  cannot  be
described  now  for  military  reasons.  The  latest  word  from  him  indirectly  is  that  he  is
somewhere  in  France.  He  is  not  married.

Class  of  1942

LEDGER

ROBERT  EMMONS  ARERG

Robert  was  born  on  August  4,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Peekskill  Military  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is
25  Meadow  Woods  Road,  Great  Neck,  New  York.
His  temporary  address  is  NAF,  Box  KK,  Navy  412,
c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

He  entered  the  employ  of  Eastern  Air  Lines  and  was  located  at  LaGuardia  Field  in  New
York  and  later  at  Washington,  D.  C.  In  July,  1942,  he  became  a  U.  S.  Naval  Aviation
Cadet  and  started  his  training  at  R.  P.  I.  at  Troy,  New  York,  then  to  the  University  of
North  Carolina  at  Chapel  Hill;  the  Naval  Air  Station  at  Glenview,  Illinois;  and  finally
the  Naval  Air  Station  at  Corpus  Christie,  Texas,  where  he  was  commissioned  an  Ensign
and  received  his  wings.  Thereafter  assigned  for  PBM  Squadron  at  Banana  River,  Flori¬
da,  and  Panama  City,  Panama.  As  first  pilot  sank  his  first  Nazi  Submarine  off  Jamaica.
Now  assigned  to  VP  203,  Air  Fleet  Wing  16  in  Brazil.

CHARLES  HARVEY  ANDREWS

Charles  was  born  on  December  6,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Gorton  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is
19  Madeline  Parkway,  Yonkers,  New  York.  His
temporary  address  is  721  Sqd.,  450  Group,  APO  520,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

“Shafty,”  as  he  was  nicknamed  while  at  Nichols,  enlisted  in  the  U.  S.  Army  Air  Corps
in  June,  1942.  He  waited  until  February  of  the  following  year  before  entering  the
service.  In  December  of  that  year  he  received  his  pilot  wings  and  commission  as  a
Second  Lieutenant  and  went  overseas  in  May.  On  April  15th,  he  married  Miss  Barbara
Sue  Lawrence  of  Yonkers.  He  has  flown  on  more  than  twenty-five  missions,  and  on
July  23d  was  promoted  to  First  Lieutenant  at  his  base  in  Italy.  He  has  since  been  made
Flight  Leader  and  wears  the  Air  Medal.

JOHN  PHILIP  HENSON

John  was  born  on  July  7,  1922  and  prepared  for
college  at  St.  Bernard’s  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1943.  His  permanent  address  is
103  Pratt  Road,  Fitchburg,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  John  Philip  Benson,  Sp.  1/c
(A),  A  &  R  Depts.,  Unit  2,  U.S.N.T.S.,  Newport,
Rhode  Island.

Since  his  college  days:

He  was  called  into  active  service  February  24,  1943,  reporting  at  Boston,  Massachusetts.
At  five  o’clock  the  same  day  he  started  for  Farragut,  Idaho,  where  he  completed  his
boot  training.  He  was  honor  man  of  his  company,  receiving  the  company  flag.  From
there  he  came  on  to  Bainbridge,  Maryland,  in  May  to  study  for  instructor  in  the  athletic
and  recreational  departments  of  the  Navy.  He  finished  his  course  the  latter  part  of  June
with  the  rank  of  Sp.  1/c  (A)  and  was  assigned  to  the  Naval  Base  at  Newport,  Rhode
Island  where  he  is  still  located.  He  is  engaged  to  be  married  to  Miss  Marion  Roy.

■ELGCP

DURLAND  R.  BROWN

Durland  was  born  on  October  14,  192  2  and  prepared
for  college  at  Marblehead  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1940  to  May,  1942.  His
permanent  address  is  50  Brookhouse  Drive,  Marble¬
head,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is
Cpl.  D.  R.  Brown,  31240615,  Hdq.  15th  Army  Group
G-2,  APO  777,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Entered  the  employ  of  Sylvania  Electric  Products,  Inc.,  Salem,  Massachusetts,  in
August,  1942,  being  assigned  to  the  radio  testing  laboratory.  Entered  the  U.  S.  Army,
December  21,  1942,  reporting  to  Fort  Devens,  Massachusetts.  Transferred  a  few  days
later  to  Fort  Bragg,  North  Carolina,  where  he  received  basic  training  in  the  field  artillery.
Attended  Clerk’s  School  and  upon  completion  promoted  to  Corporal  and  assigned  to
the  Headquarters  Battery,  as  clerk.  Transferred  in  fall  of  1943  to  Camp  Blanding,  Flori¬
da,  with  several  others,  to  establish  the  office  for  the  Infantry  Replacement  Training
Center,  to  be  started  at  that  point.  Here  received  additional  training  in  infantry  tactics.
Now  chief  clerk  of  the  Headquarters  Detachment,  but  standing  by  under  alert  orders  for
probable  shipment  to  combat  zone.  Training  received  at  Nichols  has  been  useful  in  his
work  of  office  administrator.

WILLIAM  HOWARD  COHEN

William  was  born  on  July  6,  1923.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address
is  15  Rockland  Road,  Nantasket  Beach,  Massachu¬
setts.  His  temporary  address  is  MOMM  LCI  (L)
1010,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Bill  enlisted  in  the  Navy  in  December,  1942,  and  he  received  his  training  at  Great
Lakes  and  at  the  University  of  Illinois.  At  present  he  is  somewhere  in  the  Pacific.

I EDGEL

JAMES  EDWARD  CUSHING,  JR.

James  was  born  on  July  1,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Avon  Farms,  Avon,  Connecticut.  He
attended  Nichols  from  1939  to  1942.  His  permanent
address  is  1839  Union  Street,  Schenectady,  New  York.
His  temporary  address  is  Co.  C,  1285th  Engr.  (C)
Bn.,  Camp  Howze,  Texas.

Since  his  college  days:

Left  Schenectady  for  Camp  Upton  on  September  24,  1942.  From  there  was  sent  to
Camp  Fort  Ontario  at  Oswego,  New  York,  and  trained  in  an  M.P.  division.  Later
transferred  to  guard  duty  at  the  New  York  and  Jersey  City  docks,  and  in  June  of  1943
went  out  to  Camp  Custer,  Michigan.  After  this  stationed  as  guard  at  a  Prisoner  of
War  Camp  in  Roswell,  New  Mexico.  From  Roswell  was  sent  to  present  address  at
Camp  Howe,  Texas,  and  received  transfer  into  the  Engineer  Corps.  Now  out  on  ex¬
tensive  maneuvers  and  building  Bailey  bridges  that  should  rate  another  page  in  Life
Magazine.

DANIEL  RALPH  DEMSEY

Daniel  was  born  on  February  11,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  East  Haven,  Connecticut  High  School.
He  attended  Nichols  from  September,  1940  to  June,
1941.  His  permanent  address  is  165  Fountain  Street,
New  Haven,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is
V.M.F.  123,  MBDG-42,  MCAS,  Santa  Barbara
(Goleta),  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  in  the  Accounting  Department  of  the  New  York,  New  Haven  and  Hartford
Railroad  Company  at  New  Haven,  Connecticut.  Enlisted  in  the  U.  S.  Marine  Corps
in  January,  1942,  and  after  the  usual  preliminary  training  at  Parris  Island  was  transferred
to  Quantico,  Virginia,  and  then  to  the  Ordnance  School  at  the  Naval  Air  Station  at
Jacksonville,  Florida,  from  where  he  graduated  July  25,  1942.  Upon  graduation  he  was  WAK
transferred  to  San  Diego,  California,  and  attached  to  a  Marine  fighter  squadron  and  i  |  |  <  j  §
holds  the  rank  of  Master  Technical  Sergeant.  This  squadron  was  based  at  various
South  Pacific  islands  during  the  entire  year  of  1943  and  was  returned  to  the  United
States  during  December  and  has  been  stationed  at  Santa  Barbara  continuously  since
returning.

HENRY  PARKER  DRISCOLL

Henry  was  born  on  September  9,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Moses  Brown.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  60  Con¬
verse  Street,  Wakefield,  Massachusetts.  His  tempo¬
rary  address  is  Sgt.  Henry  P.  Driscoll,  A.S.N.
31139001,  Hdqs.,  67th  Fighter  Wing,  Eighth  Air

Since  his  college  days:

Graduated  June,  1942,  from  Nichols  Junior  College.  Entered  U.  S.  Army,  July,  1942,
at  Fort  Devens,  Massachusetts.  Basic  Training  at  Fort  Bragg,  North  Carolina.  As¬
signed  to  1st  Service  Command,  Boston,  Massachusetts,  September,  1942,  rank  of
Private  First  Class.  Transferred  to  Army  Air  Force,  Bedford  Air  Field,  June,  1943,
rank  of  Corporal.  Shipped  overseas,  August,  1943.  Promoted  to  Sergeant.  Awarded
Bronze  Star,  June,  1944.  Awarded  1st  prize  in  high  jump  at  Eighth  Fighter  Command
Track  Championship,  August,  1944.  Placed  second  in  broad  jump  and  220-yard  dash.
Pays  glowing  tribute  to  British  hospitality.  Unmarried.

GEORGE  THOMAS  FISCHER

for  college  at  Perkiomen  School.  He  attended

HAC

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

After  leaving  Nichols  he  joined  the  Navy  Air  Corps.  Took  his  C.P.T.  course  at  St.
Bonaventure  College,  Oleon,  New  York.  His  pre-flight  training  he  received  at  Chapel
Hill,  (University  of  North  Carolina);  primary  flight  training  at  Squantum,  Massachu¬
setts.  At  Pensacola  he  received  his  advanced  flying  training  and  was  commissioned  an
Ensign  there  on  September  24,  1943.  He  then  was  sent  to  the  Central  Pacific  as  a  pilot
on  a  PB2Y,  a  Coronado  Bomber.  He  has  seen  action  in  the  Marshalls,  Gilbert  and
Mariana  Campaigns.  He  returned  home  for  a  thirty-day  leave  on  August  9th,  after
participating  in  the  battle  of  Saipan.  He  has  now  returned  to  active  duty  in  the  Pacific.
He  is  not  married.

Editor’s  note:  Has  been  given  citations  by  Admiral  Nimitz.

GEORGE  G.  FORESMAN

George  was  born  on  February  7,  1922  and  prepared
for  college  at  Prospect  Park  High  School.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  September,  1940  to  June,  1941.
His  permanent  address  is  846  13th  Avenue,  Prospect
Park,  Pennsylvania.  His  temporary  address  is  805th
Base  Unit  Sect.  B,  George  Field,  Box  173,  Lawrence-

Since  his  college  days:

He  was  employed  by  Sears,  Roebuck  &  Company  as  an  adjuster  of  complaints  for  about
one  year,  and  then  went  into  defense  work  at  the  Lester  plant  of  the  Westinghouse
Electric  &  Manufacturing  Co.  until  October,  1942,  when  he  was  inducted  into  the
Army.  Spent  about  fifteen  months  at  Gulfport,  Mississippi,  being  trained  and  instruct¬
ing  in  Airplane  Mechanics.  Transferred  to  Alliances,  Nebraska,  and  then  to  Lawrence-
ville,  Illinois,  where  he  is  located  now.  He  is  not  married.

CHARLES  WOLCOTT  GOODALE

Charles  was  born  on  November  15,  1919  and  prepared
for  college  at  Pawling  School,  Pawling,  New  York  and
Westminster  School,  Simsbury,  Connecticut.  He
attended  Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1942.
His  parents’  permanent  address  is  335  Wolcott  Hill
Road,  Wethersfield,  Connecticut.

Since  his  college  days:

Following  graduation  from  Nichols  in  June,  1942,  he  was  immediately  inducted  into  the
Army.  He  received  his  basic  training  at  Fort  Eustice,  Virginia,  in  the  Anti-Aircraft
Division  of  the  Coast  Artillery.  He  also  was  stationed  at  Camp  Edwards  on  Cape  Cod
and  at  Camp  Myles  Standish  in  Taunton,  Massachusetts.  He  was  sent  overseas  late
in  January  or  early  in  February,  1943.  According  to  the  records  of  the  War  Department,
he  was  reported  missing  in  action  in  February,  1943.  Later  this  was  changed  to  killed
in  action  February  7,  1943,  as  the  result  of  a  submarine  attack  in  the  North  Atlantic
while  his  ship  was  en  route  to  the  European  war  theater.  He  was  awarded  the  Purple
Heart  posthumously.  He  leaves  his  parents,  three  brothers,  and  two  sisters.

PHILIP  CLARK  GOLL1)

Philip  was  born  on  July  21,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Cheshire  Academy,  Cheshire,  Connecticut.
He  attended  Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  perma¬

WAR

■JCDGCC

Since  kis  college  days:

After  graduating  from  Nichols  College  in  June,  1942,  Phil  worked  at  The  Tubular  Products  Co.  in  South¬
ington,  Connecticut,  and  was  employed  there  until  he  was  sworn  in  on  October  19,  1942,  as  an  Army  Air
Cadet.  He  then  worked  at  the  Riverside  Dairy  in  Milldale,  Connecticut,  until  he  was  called  to  active
service  on  January  30,  1943.  He  reported  to  Atlantic  City,  New  Jersey,  there  received  his  elementary
training;  his  college  training  at  the  University  of  Pittsburgh  and  while  there  married  Miss  Gloria  Pierce
of  Meriden,  Connecticut,  on  April  17,  1943,  in  the  Presbyterian  Church;  at  Classification  Center,  at  Max¬
well  Field,  Montgomery,  Alabama,  he  was  classified  as  a  Pilot  and  transferred  to  Arcadia  Air  Field,  Florida,
for  primary  training;  received  his  basic  training  at  Gunter  Field,  Montgomery,  Alabama,  advanced  train¬
ing  at  Blytheville  Field,  Blytheville,  Arkansas,  and  there  in  March,  1944,  received  his  silver  wings  and
commission  as  a  Pilot.  He  next  reported  to  Symrna  Army  Air  Base,  Symrna,  Tennessee,  for  pilot  training
on  a  B-24  Bomber,  and  having  completed  this  course  got  his  crew  at  Westover  Field,  Chicopee,  Massa¬
chusetts,  and  was  transferred  to  Charleston  Army  Air  Base,  Charleston,  South  Carolina,  where  he  is  now
in  training.

FREDER1CH  LOYD  HARRISON

Frederich  was  born  on  April  22,  1929  and  prepared
for  college  at  Brighton  High  School,  Rochester,  New
York.  He  attended  Nichols  from  September,  1940
to  June,  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  Apt.  3,
1095  Park  Avenue,  Rochester,  New  York.  His
temporary  address  is  Lt.  F.  L.  Harrison,  01946980,
AGD.  Hq.  C.R.S.,  Wakeman  General  Hospital,  Bldg.
405,  Room  222,  Camp  Atterbury,  Indiana.

Since  his  college  days:

He  signed  up  before  Pearl  Harbor  as  a  reserve.  Because  of  an  eye  defect  he  was  discharged  from  the
Marine  Reserves  in  June,  1942,  and  enlisted  in  the  Army  the  same  day.  He  received  his  basic  training  in
infantry  at  Fort  McClellan,  Alabama.  While  there  he  worked  in  the  newspaper  office  and  later  as  an
instructor  of  limited  service  men.  In  November,  1942,  he  was  sent  to  the  Adjutant  General  School  at
Fort  Washington,  Maryland.  On  completion  of  this  course  he  was  assigned  to  the  Classification  Branch,
Headquarters  of  Port  of  Embarkation,  Charleston,  South  Carolina.  In  December,  1943,  he  graduated
from  Officers  Candidate  School  of  the  Transportation  Corps,  New  Orleans,  Louisiana,  and  was  commissioned
a  Second  Lieutenant.  From  January  to  May,  1944,  he  was  Assistant  Classification  Officer  then  Assistant
Director  of  Personnel  of  Jackson  Barracks  area  of  P.O.E.,  New  Orleans.  He  also  was  a  Courier  Officer.
In  July,  1944,  he  graduated  from  the  Officers  Branch  of  the  Adjutant  General  School  in  Advance  Adminis¬
trative  at  Fort  Washington.  He  returned  to  New  Orleans  as  an  Adjutant  of  Hqs.  J.  B.  A.  In  September,
1944,  he  is  now  attending  the  Adjutant  General  School  at  Fort  Sam  Houston  in  San  Antonio,  Texas,  for
advanced  classification.

STANLEY  HICKS,  JR.

Stanley  was  born  on  November  20,  1922  and  prepared
for  college  at  Brimfield  Massachusetts  High  School.
He  attended  Nichols  from  September,  1940  to  June,
1942.

Since  his  college  days:

(The  following  is  taken  from  a  letter  his  mother  wrote  for  the  War  Ledger ) :

“The  enclosed  clipping  will  speak  for  itself,  I  think.  I  do  not  know  whether  you  ever  knew  the  very  sad
news.  The  accident  happened  Saturday,  June  12,  1943.  He  died  the  next  day,  Sunday,  at  noon.  He
enlisted  in  the  Air  Corps  about  the  middle  of  December,  1942,  but  he  was  not  called  until  February,  1943.
He  left  Springfield  the  morning  of  February  25  for  Devens,  was  there  only  a  few  hours  when  the  contingent
he  was  in  left  for  Atlantic  City,  New  Jersey.  He  was  there  until  he  went  to  State  College,  Pennsylvania,
the  first  of  May.  He  enjoyed  the  work  there  immensely.  Believe  it  or  not,  he  told  me  he  helped  cadets
with  his  Algebra  in  return  for  some  favor.  It  was  a  source  of  great  satisfaction  to  him  that  he  did  so  well
in  all  his  work.  His  average  in  the  Air  Corps  examination  was  96.”

Editor’s  note:  The  clipping  which  Mrs.  Hicks  enclosed  states  that  “Stan”  died  from  injuries  received  in
an  automobile  accident  in  Altoona,  Pennsylvania.

ROBERT  P.  M.  INGOUF

Robert  was  born  on  March  15,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Mercersburg  Academy,  Mercersburg,
Pennsylvania  and  Roosevelt  High  School,  Yonkers,
New  York.  He  attended  Nichols  from  September,
1940  to  May,  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  333
East  41st  Street,  Apartment  5B,  New  York  17,  New
York.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduating  from  Nichols  in  May,  1942,  Bob  was  called  for  induction  in  the  U.  S.

Army  on  July  1st  at  Fort  Oglethorpe,  Georgia,  but  was  rejected  for  military  service

due  to  a  physical  disability.  In  August,  1942,  he  secured  a  position  with  The  Mathieson

Alkali  Works,  Inc.,  New  York,  New  York  (manufacturers  of  heavy  chemicals),  and  after

having  been  connected  with  their  sales  organization  for  a  period  of  approximately  a  year

and  a  half,  he  is  now  in  charge  of  the  “Ammonia-Chlorine  Allocations  Division”  of  the

same  firm  operating  in  direct  conjunction  with  the  War  Production  Board.  Bob  and  LCDGEC

the  former  Miss  Kathleen  Myers  of  Knoxville,  Tennessee,  were  married  at  “The  Little

Church  Around  the  Corner”  in  New  York,  on  December  24,  1942.

WILLIAM  E.  KELSEY,  JR.

William  was  born  on  February  21,  1923  and  prepared
for  college  at  New  York  Military  Academy,  Cornwall
on  the  Hudson  and  at  Taft,  Watertown,  Connecticut.
He  attended  Nichols  from  September  to  November,
1940.  His  permanent  address  is  70  Wood  Pond  Road,
West  Hartford,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address
is  Sgt.  W.  E.  Kelsey,  Jr.,  11103466,  Det.  Sec.  Signal
Ser.  Bn.,  APO  246,  c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,
California.

Since  his  college  days:

He  has  been  associated  with  his  father,  W.  E.  Kelsey,  Sr.,  in  the  conduct  of  an  Office
Equipment  Business  in  Hartford,  Connecticut.  He  enlisted  on  December  7,  1942,  and
was  sent  first  to  Camp  Edison,  Fort  Monmouth,  New  Jersey,  and  thence  to  Vint  Hill
Farm,  Warrenton,  Virginia.  Here  he  was  associated  with  a  former  Nichols  College
student,  John  Mead.  Later  he  was  transferred  to  Arlington,  Virginia,  where  he  remained
until  last  Friday,  September  1st,  when  he  left  for  the  West  Coast  on  his  way  to  the  Pacific
Warfare.  On  March  4,  1941,  he  married  Janet  White  of  West  Hartford,  Connecticut,
and  they  have  a  son,  W.  E.  Kelsey,  3d,  who  is  two  years  and  six  months  old.

P.S. — Have  just  received  a  ’phone  call  from  Bill  saying  he  is  at  Two  Rock  Ranch,  Peta¬
luma,  California,  and  will  ship  out  from  there  shortly.

Editor’s  note:  Bill  did  ship  out  for  the  Pacific.

LEDGER

Robert  was  born  on  December  17,  1923  and  prepared
for  college  at  Bulkeley  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address

Island,  South  Carolina;  Cherry  Point,  North  Carolina;  Norman,  Oklahoma;  El  Centro,
California;  and  last  Oceanside,  California,  where  he  is  now.  Bob  has  advanced  rapidly
in  the  Marines  and  on  his  first  anniversary  he  received  his  Sergeant’s  stripes.  Since
then  he  received  another  promotion  to  that  of  Staff  Sergeant  in  the  United  States
Marines.

DOUGLAS  B.  KTTTERMAN

Douglas  was  born  on  October  12,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Sharon,  Massachusetts  High  School.
He  attended  Nichols  from  September,  1940  to  June,
1942.  His  permanent  address  is  138  East  Street,
Sharon,  Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is
Lt.  D.  G.  Kitterman,  VMB-443,  USMCR,  1st  MAW,
FMF,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Entered  the  Naval  Reserves  immediately  following  graduation.  Trained  for  a  few
months  at  Squantum,  Massachusetts.  Transferred  to  Cherry  Point,  North  Carolina,
for  another  training  period  following  which  he  transferred  to  Pensacola,  Florida.  At
this  camp  he  entered  the  Marine  Reserve  Corps  and  began  training  as  a  Marine  Bomber
Pilot.  When  he  finished  at  Pensacola  he  was  at  two  or  three  other  camps  in  Florida
after  which  he  was  moved  to  the  West  Coast  for  final  training  preliminary  to  operations
in  the  South  Pacific  where  he  is  now  stationed.  He  was  married  June  11,  1943,  to  Doris
Dunster,  Upper  Montclair,  New  Jersey.  When  last  heard  from  he  was  operating  as  a
Marine  Bomber  Pilot,  relatively  close  to  Japanese  bases,  was  in  good  health  and  appar¬
ently  being  successful  in  his  efforts  to  help  win  the  war.

Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Enlisted  January  12,  1942,  United  States  Naval  Reserves.  Reported  for  active  duty
February  25.  1942,  Philadelphia  Navy  Yard.  March  8,  1942,  transferred  to  Reedy  Is¬
land,  Port  Penn,  Delaware.  July  14,  1942,  transferred  to  Philadelphia  Navy  Yard.
December  18,  1942,  to  U.  S.  Navy  Department,  Washington,  D.  C.  January  30,  1943,
dectached  from  Washington,  D.  C.  February  2,  1943,  married  Miss  Jean  Sparks  of
Penn’s  Grove,  New  Jersey.  February  12,  1943,  transferred  to  and  reported  in  at  Receiv¬
ing  Ship  at  Destroyer  Base,  San  Diego,  California.  Further  transferred  to  U.  S.  Naval
Radio  Station,  Imperial  Beach,  California.  July  18,  1944,  transferred  to  Bremerton
Navy  Yard,  Seattle,  Washington,  for  overseas  duty.  Born  September  4,  1944,  a  daughter.
Marilyn  Jean.

LEDGER

WALTER  L.  LASBURY

Walter  was  born  on  April  28,  1918  and  prepared  for
college  at  Ellsworth  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is
South  Windsor,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address
is  421st  M.A.A.F.  Base  Unit,  Muroc  Army  Air  Field,
Sq.  D.,  Muroc,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Walter  Lasbury  enlisted  in  the  Army  Air  Force  December,  1941.  He  hoped  to  be  a  flyer
but  was  unable  to  because  of  his  eyesight.  His  first  camp  was  in  St.  Louis,  Missouri,  from
there  he  went  to  Sherman,  Texas,  he  was  there  almost  a  year  when  he  received  his  first
rating  and  studied  to  be  a  mechanic.  He  has  been  at  Independence,  Kansas;  Amarillo,
Texas;  and  Sheppard  Field,  Texas.  While  he  was  in  Texas  he  received  his  Seragent’s
rating.  He  liked  the  state  of  Texas  very  much  and  said,  he  would  like  to  make  his  home
there  some  day.  After  his  father’s  death  in  February,  1944,  he  was  sent  to  California
where  he  got  the  chance  to  work  on  some  of  the  big  motors.  He  liked  this  very  much
and  in  August  was  sent  to  Detroit,  Michigan,  for  advance  training  on  these  motors.  He
expects  to  go  back  to  California  shortly.

HARRY  JAMES  LEHMAN,  JR.

Harry  was  born  on  October  12,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Cheshire  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  660
Lafayette  Avenue,  Buffalo,  New  York.  His  temporary
address  is  Ensign  HarryJ.  Lehman,  Jr.,  USS  Algorctb,
c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

WAC

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

Entered  Merchant  Marine  Cadet  Corps  as  Deck  Cadet,  May  1,  1942,  at  Kingspoint,
Long  Island.  Graduated  October  30,  1943.  Granted  commission  of  Third  Mate  in  the
Merchant  Marine.  Was  made  Ensign  in  the  U.  S.  Naval  Reserve,  November  30,  1943.
Left  San  Francisco  port  January,  1944.  Is  now  serving  in  the  Southwest  Pacific.
Editor's  note:  We  have  since  learned  that  he  has  been  promoted  to  Lieutenant  Junior
Grade.

GORDON  R.  LEWIS

Gordon  was  born  on  November  16,  1921  and  prepared
at  Wilby  High  School.  He  attended  Nichols  from
1940  to  1942.  His  parents’  permanent  address  is
529  Highland  Avenue,  Waterbury,  Connecticut.

Since  his  college  days:

In  June,  1942,  Gordon  enlisted  in  the  Naval  Reserve  Air  Corps,  and  in  August  began  preliminary  train¬
ing  at  Squantum,  Massachusetts.  In  November  he  was  sent  to  Pensacola,  where  he  completed  his  flight
training  course.  He  was  selected  for  the  Marine  Corps  and  received  specialized  training  as  a  dive  bomber
pilot.  In  March,  1943,  he  received  his  Navy  “Wings  of  Gold”  and  was  commissioned  a  Second  Lieutenant.
He  left  for  the  South  Pacific  in  August,  1943.  In  September,  1943,  he  was  made  a  First  Lieutenant.  He
spent  more  than  six  months  on  an  atoll  where  he  was  third  in  command.

Editor’s  note:  Gordon  was  killed  in  action  on  Luzon  on  January  28,  1945,  while  attacking  an  objective,  hav¬
ing  delivered  his  bomb.  His  plane  was  seen  to  be  on  fire  at  about  one  thousand  feet.  He  got  the  plane  to
about  one  hundred  feet  when  it  went  out  of  control  behind  the  enemy  lines,  five  miles  west  of  Clark  Field.
He  was  a  member  of  the  “Flying  Eggbeaters”  Squadron  and  was  a  Section  Leader.  He  had  picked  out
some  Jap  rolling  target  as  his  target  and  had  gone  after  it  in  a  dive.  A  20mm.  shell  hit  his  plane,  which
crashed,  exploded  immediately,  and  burst  into  flames.  Six  days  after  the  crash,  Col.  Lyle  H.  Meyer,
Commanding  Officer  of  the  “Flying  Eggbeaters”  issued  special  order:  “Effective  immediately,  the  area
occupied  by  this  group  will  be  known  as  Camp  Lewis,  in  honor  of  1st  Lt.  Gordon  Rhys  Lewis,  killed  in
Action,  January  28,  1945.”

R.  W.  MANHEIM

Manheim  was  born  on  June  10,  1922  and  prepared
for  college  at  Shaker  Heights  High  School.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent
address  is  13309  South  Woodland,  Shaker  Heights,
Ohio.  His  temporary  address  is  Lt.  (jg)  R.  W.  Man¬
heim,  Floyd  Bennett  Field,  Naval  Air  Station,  New
York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Attended  Princeton  University.  Joined  Naval  Air  Corps.  Called  to  active  duty,  August
13,  at  Squantum,  as  AV  Cadet,  U-5.  Graduated  from  Pensacola  and  designated  as  a
Naval  Aviator,  April  13,  1943.  Assigned  temporary  duty  as  an  instructor  to  Medical
Corps  at  Pensacola.  On  June  11,  1943,  he  was  assigned  to  N.A.S.,  St.  Louis,  as  primary
Flight  Instructor  to  Royal  Navy  Cadets.  On  October  6,  1944,  he  was  assigned  to  the
Ferry  Command,  N.A.S.,  New  York.

JOSEPH  AVERY  MANNING,  II

Joseph  was  born  on  May  9,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Wassookeag  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1939  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  71
Berwick  Street,  Worcester,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  15  Chapman  Street,  East
Hartford,  Connecticut.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduation  from  Nichols,  Joe  spent  fifteen  months  at  the  New  England  Aircraft
School,  East  Boston.  Here  he  studied  airplane  construction  and  maintenance.  In
December,  1943,  Joe  started  work  with  Pratt  &  Whitney,  Hartford,  Connecticut,  and
is  employed  in  the  experimental  laboratory.  On  September  24,  1944,  he  was  married
to  Martha  C.  Edgecomb  of  Great  Barrington,  Massachusetts.

from  1940  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is  10

14th  Photo  Lab.,  468th  Bomb.  Group,  A.P.O.  493,
c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

WAR

LEDGER

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  by  Reading  Railroad  in  Philadelphia  from  September  1,  1941  to  August  4,
1942,  when  he  entered  the  Army  in  the  Air  Corps.  Was  sent  to  St.  Petersburg  ,  Florida,
and  then  had  the  chance  for  the  Photography  Course  at  Denver,  Colorado,  then  sent  to
Salina,  Kansas,  then  to  Victoria,  Kansas,  then  back  to  Salina,  Kansas,  and  from  there
went  overseas  in  March  of  1944,  arriving  in  India  in  May  by  way  of  Australia  and  in
August  he  flew  over  the  Hump  to  China  as  his  next  Post.  His  capacity  in  Photography
is  a  Laboratory  Technician.

RICHARD  A.  MARSHALL

Richard  was  born  on  September  15,  1922  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  Lexington  High  School.  He
attended  Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent
address  is  7  Patriots  Drive,  Lexington,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  Lt.  (jg)  R.  A.  Marshall,
USNR,  VPB-2,  OTU-4,  Naval  Air  Station,  Corpus

Since  his  college  days:

Richard  enlisted  as  a  Naval  Aviation  Cadet — graduated  from  U.  S.  Navy  Pre-Flight
School  at  Chapel  Hill,  North  Carolina.  He  received  primary  flight  training  at  U.  S.
Naval  Air  Station,  Memphis,  Tennessee,  and  advanced  training  at  Corpus  Christi,
Texas,  where  he  received  his  wings  and  commission  in  August,  1943,  and  was  assigned
to  Atlantic  Fleet  duty.  He  is  now  Plane  Commander  of  a  PBM  Martin  Patrol  Bomber
flying  from  South  American  bases.  He  is  engaged  to  Miss  Shirley  Webster  of  Rockville,
Connecticut.

Editor's  note:  Richard  was  married  to  Miss  Webster  in  January  1,  1945,  and  is  now  an
Instrument  Flight  Instructor  at  the  Naval  Air  Station,  Corpus  Christi,  Texas.

the  “Air  Medal”.  He  has  a  daughter,  Jeanne  Elsie,  born  in  December,  1944.

Since  his  college  days:

On  September  23,  1941,  enlisted  in  the  United  States  Air  Corps  and  received  his  training
at  Jefferson  Barracks,  Missouri.  On  January  7,  1942,  left  this  country  for  foreign  service.

he  received  a  citation  for  his  efforts  which  contributed  greatly  to  the  successes  attained
by  this  Group  in  combat.”  A  face  injury  was  received  at  this  time.

FRANK  STANLEY  MONTUORT,  JR.

Frank  was  born  on  January  3,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Lawrence  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address
is  11  Weymouth  Street,  Fitchburg,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  902nd  AAF  Base  Unit,
Squadron  H,  Flight  Operation,  AAFTAC  Air  Base,
Orlando,  Florida.

Since  his  college  days:

Immediately  after  graduation,  Frank  was  inducted  into  the  Army.  He  attended  the
Army  Air  Corps  Mechanics’  School  at  Goldsboro,  North  Carolina.  He  was  then  sent
to  the  Vultee  Aircraft  Factory  in  Nashville,  Tennessee,  for  further  training.  After  a
few  months  he  was  then  sent  to  the  Orlando  Air  Base  in  Orlando,  Florida.  From  Or¬
lando  he  was  sent  to  The  Citadel,  Charleston,  South  Carolina,  and  after  a  month  re¬
turned  to  the  Orlando  Air  Base,  Orlando,  Florida,  where  he  is  now  stationed.  For  several
months  he  took  personal  care  mechanically  of  the  plane  of  Colonel  Robert  Scott  who
wrote  “God  is  my  Co-Pilot.”  and  the  plane  of  Captain  Donaldson  who  is  an  RAF  pilot
who  is  now  at  AAFTAC  assisting  in  the  teaching  of  attack.  At  the  present  moment  he
is  working  in  the  Flight  Operation  Squadron  which  is  in  charge  of  all  planes  coming  in
and  off  of  the  field.

to  Fort  Miles,  Lewes,  Delaware.  Promoted  to  Corporal  in  July,  1942.  Chosen  for

now  stationed  in  the  Aleutian  Isles.  On  October  24,  1942,  Lt.  George  E.  Munce  and

Elizabeth  Ann  Flemming  were  united  in  marriage  at  St.  Joseph’s  Cathedral,  Hartford,  LEDGER

WILLIAM  RAMSAY  NEEDHAM

William  was  born  on  August  4,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Bronxville  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  April,  1940.  His
permanent  address  is  18  Gramaton  Gardens,  Bronx¬
ville,  New  York.  His  temporary  address  is  S/Sgt.
W.  R.  Needham,  Squadron  A-4,  APO  19143-A,
c/o  P.  O.,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

He  had  to  stop  his  college  course  because  of  temporary  ill  health  but  was  given  his  full
year  credits  at  Nichols  and  elected  to  be  a  member  of  the  Justinian  Council.  He  worked
briefly  for  a  subsidiary  of  the  Borden  Co.,  in  New  York  City,  and  then  for  the  Gramaton
National  Bank  at  Bronxville,  New  York.  In  both  situations  he  was  rated  as  a  Junior
Accountant.  He  resigned  in  January,  1942,  to  enter  the  Army  Air  Force,  and  has  now
moved  up  to  the  grade  of  Sergeant,  specializing  in  Armament  work  and  qualifying  as  an
Aerial  Gunner  on  the  B-24  Bombers.  He  was  selected  to  be  part  of  a  group  on  the  giant
new  B-29  Bombers  in  May,  1944,  and  is  in  charge  of  Armament  for  an  element  of  his
squadron.  He  is  not  married.  He  expects  to  go  overseas  in  November,  1944,  when  his
squadron'completes  its  training.

JOHN  FRANKLIN  NOBLE,  JR.

WAR

LEDGER

John  was  born  on  December  22,  1918  and  prepared
for  college  at  The  Hill  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1940  to  June,  1941.  His  permanent
address  is  206  Almur  Lane,  Wynnewood,  Pennsyl¬
vania.  His  temporary  address  is  Capt.  John  F.
Noble,  Jr.,  0-1573476,  2470th  Q.  M.  Trk  Co.  (avn),

Patterson  Field  as  Second  Lieutenant,  April,  1942.  Married  Barbara  Ann  Beem,  Day-
ton,  Ohio,  on  December  26,  1942.  No  children.  Commissioned  First  Lieutenant,
February  22,  1943.  Went  overseas  a  Captain,  January  18,  1944,  while  in  Italy.  Left
Italy  in  summer  of  1944  and  went  to  Corsica  from  there  to  southern  France.  Back  to
Italy,  October,  1944,  and  is  still  there  as  far  as  we  know.  He  is  C.O.  of  a  Truck  Com¬
pany,  attached  to  aviation.

lllLTON  LOCKWOOD  NOYES,  JK.

Hilton  was  born  on  March  3,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Pingry  School.  He  attended  Nichols  from
1940  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is  11  Kempshall

is  309  West  Portland,  Phoenix,  Arizona.

Eustis,  Virginia.  After  nearly  four  months  in  the  hospital  there,  he  received  an  Hon¬
orable  Discharge  in  February,  1943.  After  a  six  months  rest,  he  returned  to  the  office
of  Singer’s  where  he  stayed  until  January,  1944,  when  he  went  to  Phoenix,  Arizona.  He
is  doing  temporary  work  there  and  expects  to  return  to  Elizabeth  next  April.

WAR

LECGEP

JOHN  G.  O’CONNELL

John  was  born  on  January  3,  1922  and  prepared  for
college  at  Deerfield  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  68
Cleveland  Street,  Greenfield,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

Upon  my  graduating  from  Nichols  in  1942,  I  became  associated  with  the  Federal  Bureau
of  Investigation  in  the  Boston  Field  Office.  Contemplating  an  appointment  as  a  Special
Agent,  I  enrolled  in  Northeastern  University  School  of  Law.  However,  because  of  a
nervous  breakdown  suffered  in  August,  1943,  I  was  advised  by  my  physician  to  resign
my  position  in  the  F.B.I.  and  return  to  my  home  in  Greenfield.  After  a  month’s  rest,
I  entered  the  employ  of  the  Greenfield  Tap  &  Die  Corporation  in  the  Production  Engi¬
neering  Department.  It  is  with  this  firm  that  I  have  been  with  since  September  1,  1943,
and  serving  as  Administrative  Assistant  to  Mr.  Erwin  A.  Enderele,  Production  Engineer
and  Manager.  Other  than  remaining  thus  far  a  single  man,  and  resolved  to  do  my  part
in  the  winning  of  the  war,  I  look  forward  with  great  anticipation  to  an  all-out  Nichols
Alumnus  party  when  the  war  is  over.

BERTRAND  GAINES  PECK,  JR.

Bertrand  was  born  on  April  4,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Wilbraham  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1939  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  17
Wolcott  Avenue,  Andover,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  A.S.N.,  31158925,  APO  986,
c/o  Postmaster,  Seattle,  Washington.

Since  his  college  days:

Entered  the  service,  August  19,  1942.  Trained  at  Camp  Lee,  Virginia,  in  Quartermaster
Corps.  December,  1942,  Alaska  and  the  Aleutian  Islands,  Transportation.  September,
1944  made  a  Corporal  T/5.

LEDGER

DAVID  PRITCHARD,  JR.

David  was  born  on  December  29,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Cheshire  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address
is  Penwood  Farm,  McClain  Street,  Mt.  Kisco,  New
York.  His  temporary  address  is  David  Pritchard,  Jr.,
SK  3/c,  U.S.C.G.R.,  Coast  Guard  Unit  339,  c/o  Fleet
Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Enlisted  in  U.  S.  Coast  Guard,  July,  1942.  Attached  to  District  Coast  Guard  Office,
New  York  City.  Aboard  C.  H.  C.  Igarus  and  USS  Cepheus,  Army  Transport  Service.
Stationed  at  Elizabeth  City  Air  Base,  Elizabeth  City,  North  Carolina.  Applied  for
service  school  and  sent  to  St.  Augustine,  Flordia,  New  London,  Connecticut,  and  now
temporarily  attached  to  O.C.G.O.  4th  N.D.

Editor's  note:  Latest  information  reports  that  he  was  in  a  hospital  in  Guam.

WILLIAM  JOHN  PROVOOST,  JR.

William  was  born  on  August  6,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Mount  Hermon  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1940  to  June,  1941.  His
permanent  address  is  29  Lincoln  Avenue,  Old  Green¬
wich,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is  USS
Piedmont,  Detail  6A,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  San  Fran¬
cisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

He  was  employed  at  the  Chance  Vought  Aircraft  Division  in  Stratford,  Connecticut,
from  July,  1941  to  July,  1942.  In  August,  1942,  he  enlisted  in  the  U.  S.  Naval  Reserve
and  received  his  boot  training  at  Newport,  Rhode  Island.  He  was  then  assigned  to
sea  duty  with  the  Atlantic  fleet  until  November,  1943.  At  that  time  he  was  reassigned
to  sea  duty  with  the  Pacific  fleet.  He  is  now  on  the  Pacific  and  has  a  rating  of  Petty
Officer  third  class.

STANLEY  H.  REESE,  JR.

Stanley  was  born  on  February  24,  1922  and  prepared
for  college  at  Westfield  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address
is  621  Hanford  Place,  Westfield,  New  Jersey.  His
temporary  address  is  S/Sgt.  S.  H.  Reese,  Jr.,  12137347,
330th  Transport  Squadron,  APO  845,  c/o  Postmaster,
Miami,  Florida.

Since  his  college  days:

Enlisted  in  A.A.F.,  September  21,  1942,  and  obtained  basic  training  in  Atlantic  City,
New  Jersey.  Training  relating  to  the  operation  and  maintenance  of  Airplanes  received
at  Casey  Jones  School  of  Aeronautics,  Newark,  New  Jersey,  Roosevelt  Air  Field,  Long
Island,  and  Bell  Aircraft,  Niagara  Falls,  New  York.  Transferred  July  10,  1943,  to
Florida,  and  attached  to  the  Ground  Crews  at  Fort  Meyers  and  Venice  Air  Fields  for  a
period  of  six  months.  Since  January,  1944,  stationed  at  Dover  Air  Base,  Dover,  Dela¬
ware,  with  the  rank  of  Sergeant,  and  in  charge  of  one  of  the  Ground  Crews.
