LEDGER

WILLIAM  LESLIE  ROGERS

William  was  born  on  April  8,  1923  and  prepared
for  college  at  Scarsdale  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address
is  18  Forest  Lane,  Scarsdale,  New  York.  His  tem¬
porary  address  is  Lt.  William  L.  Rogers,  0-828534,
306th  Bomb.  Group,  368th  Squad,  APO  557,  c/o
Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

WAR

I.ED6ER

Since  his  college  days:

With  American  Can  Company,  New  York  City,  doing  junior  clerical  and  sales  work  for  period  between
Nichols  graduation  until  December,  1942,  resigning  to  enlist  in  U.  S.  Army  Air  Forces.  Enlisted  in  Air
Corps,  January  3,  1943,  and  was  accepted  to  start  training  January  10.  At  initial  base  Atlantic  City,  was
assigned  to  First  Training  Group  at  Colby  College,  Maine,  completing  the  course  prescribed  in  the  21st
College  Training  Detachment,  July  1,  1943,  when  he  was  assigned  to  Classification  at  Montgomery,
Alabama,  being  designated  an  Air  Cadet  at  Maxwell  Field,  and  progressing  to  single-engine  trainers  at
Lafayette,  Louisiana,  and  Walnut  Ridge,  Arkansas.  In  March,  1944,  he  was  assigned  to  Blytheville,
Arkansas,  making  his  solo  hop  and  advancing  to  instrument  and  night  flying,  getting  his  commission
and  Pilot’s  Wings,  April  15.  He  was  assigned  Co-Pilot  on  a  B-17  Flying  Fortress,  and  started  combat
training.  On  completion  of  active  unit  teamwork,  Lt.  Rogers  and  his  crew  were  ordered  to  be  ready  for
overseas  duty.  He  is  now  in  active  duty  with  a  number  of  missions  to  his  credit,  having  earned  the  Air
Medal  with  two  Oak  Leaf  Clusters  during  five  months  work  over  the  Eastern  Front.

JULIAN  RICE,  JR.

Julian  was  born  on  August  24,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Gunnery  School.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  308
Pondfield  Road,  Bronxville,  New  York.  His  tempo¬
rary  address  is  Lt.  Julian  Rice,  Jr.,  0-746940,  746
Bomb.  Sq.,  456  Bomb.  Gp.,  APO  520,  c/o  Postmaster,
New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Enlisted  day  of  graduation,  May  29,  1942,  at  Providence.  Counselor  at  Camp  Winder-
mere,  Lak  Como,  Pennsylvania,  until  induction  in  A.A.F.  at  Binghampton,  New  York,
July  30,  1942.  Air  Cadet  at  Santa  Ana,  California,  and  Deming,  New  Mexico,  where  he
received  wings  as  Bombardier  and  Second  Lieutenant  Bars,  May  29,  1943.  Gunnery
wings  at  Las  Vegas,  Nevada,  August,  1943.  Final  advance  training  at  Charleston,  South
Carolina  and  Mitchell  Field,  New  York.  Overseas,  February,  1944,  with  M. A.A.F,
To  date,  thirty-nine  missions.  Made  first  Lieutenant  July,  1944.

FRANK  W.  SARGEANT,  11

Frank  was  born  on  October  23,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Proctor  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1940  to  1941.  His  permanent  address  is  100
Bellevue  Avenue,  Upper  Montclair,  New  Jersey.

Since  his  college  days:

He  left  Ithaca  School  of  Music  to  enlist  in  the  U.  S.  Merchant  Marine.  In  March,  1944,
he  received  a  commission  as  an  Ensign  USMS,  graduating  from  the  Merchant  Marine
Academy  at  Kings  Point,  Long  Island,  New  York.  As  part  of  his  training,  he  spent
eight  and  one-half  months  in  the  South  Pacific  as  a  Cadet  Officer  on  a  Merchant  ship.
He  is  now  in  San  Francisco,  just  having  returned  from  New  Guinea.  His  ship  is  in  dry
dock  so  I  do  not  know  what  his  next  A.P.O.  will  be.

LEDGER

CHARLES  TAYLOR  SMITH

Charles  was  born  on  April  2,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Kimball  Union  Academy.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1941  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is
65  Eliot  Avenue,  West  Newton,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  Bergstrom  Field,  Austin,  Texas.

Since  his  college  days:

Enlisted  in  the  Army  in  July,  1942,  and  after  a  short  period  of  schooling  in  Denver,
Colorado,  was  sent  to  England  as  an  armourer  in  what  used  to  be  the  Eagle  Squadron
of  the  R.A.F.  Returned  to  United  States  in  June,  1943,  for  Aviation  Cadet  training.
Married  Miss  Phyllis  A.  Petrie  while  on  furlough  and  was  then  sent  to  California.
Spent  this  past  summer  in  Pecos,  Texas,  and  graduated  from  two  engine  pilot  school  in
September.

to  May,  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  89  Mont¬

attended  University  of  Pennsylvania  and  Northwestern  University  in  Chicago,  Illinois,
receiving  his  commission  as  an  Ensign  from  the  latter  school  on  March  17.  Is  not  mar-
WAR  ried.  Is  at  present  on  duty  on  an  L.S.T.  somewhere  in  the  Pacific.

for  college  at  Hope  High  School.  His  permanent

GARDNER  NORTHUP  SOULE

Gardner  was  born  on  February  11,  1921  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  Loomis  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1939  to  June,  1941.  His
permanent  address  is  Victor  Road,  Pittsford,  New
York.  His  temporary  address  is  1st  Lt.  G.  N.  Soule,
U.S.M.C.,  Headquarters  Bn.  TQM,  6th  Marine  Div.,
FMF,  c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

He  was  graduated  from  Syracuse  University,  School  of  Business  Administration,  with
the  degree  of  B.S.  cum  laude  in  May,  1942.  As  an  officer  candidate  in  the  U.  S.  Marine
Corps  he  was  trained  at  Parris  Island  and  Quantico  and  was  commissioned  as  a  Second
Lieutenant,  September  18,  1942.  He  has  had  further  training  in  camouflage  and  trans¬
port  quartermaster  work.  He  is  now  somewhere  in  the  South  Pacific  Area.  He  married
Theodora  (Teddy)  Wendt  in  Chicago  after  finishing  his  training.  Their  son,  Junior,
was  born  September  3,  1944.

WAR

LEDGER

PAUL  HAMILTON  S  WETLAND

Paul  was  born  on  June  5,  1920  and  prepared  for  col¬
lege  at  Kentucky  Military  Institute,  Lyndon,  Ken¬
tucky;  Venice,  Floiida;  and  Proctor  Academy,  An¬
dover,  New  Hampshire.  He  attended  Nichols  from
September,  1940  to  January,  1942.  His  permanent
address  is  Long  Meadow  Farm,  Richmond  Heights
Village,  P.  O.  South  Euclid,  Ohio.  His  temporary
address  is  Lt.  P.  H.  Swetland,  530th  Fighter  Sq.,
311th  Fighter  Bomber  Group,  APO  210,  c/o  Post¬
master,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

He  was  granted  a  commission  as  Second  Lieutenant  of  Infantry  on  reaching  his  twenty-first  birthday.
He  was  called  into  active  service  with  that  rank  in  January  of  1942.  He  was  assigned  to  duty  in  Camp
Wolters,  Texas,  then  transferred  to  Camp  Barkeley,  Texas.  He  was  promoted  to  First  Lieutenant  and
was  Supply  Officer  for  his  Battalion  when  in  January,  1943,  he  applied  for  and  was  granted  transfer  to  the
Army  Air  Forces.  He  got  his  training  as  a  pilot  in  various  flying  fields  in  Texas  and  was  graduated  as  a
combat  pilot  from  Victoria  Field,  Texas,  in  October  of  1943.  He  then  received  combat  training  at  Sarasota
Field,  Florida.  He  was  sent  from  the  United  States  in  February  of  1944,  first  landing  in  India,  then  being
transferred  to  North  Burma.  At  this  date,  October  1,  1944,  he  is  stationed  somewhere  in  China.  He  is
flying  a  P-51  “Mustang”  Fighter  Plane.  He  has  been  promoted  to  his  own  individual  plane  with  a  wing
flier  and  has  been  on  a  number  of  missions  but  will  not  say  where,  how  many  or  what.  He  has  been  awarded
the  Air  Medal.

WILLIAM  WHITING  THOMPSON

William  was  born  on  January  1,  1922  and  prepared
for  college  at  North  Attleboro  High.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is
29  Grant  Street,  North  Attleboro,  Massachusetts.
His  temporary  address  is  SS  John  Lykes,  c/o  Post¬
master,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduating  from  Nichols,  Bill  worked  in  the  office  of  Union  Plate  and  Wire  Com¬
pany  in  Attleboro,  Massachusetts.  In  the  fall  of  1943  he  enlisted  as  a  Midshipman  Cadet
in  the  Merchant  Marine  Cadet  Corps.  He  received  his  basic  training  at  San  Mateo,
California,  and  was  assigned  to  the  SS  John  Lykes.  Since  March  he  has  made  two  trips
to  the  South  Pacific,  and  as  far  as  we  know,  he  is  still  there.

CHARLES  CORTELYON  TOMLINSON,  3D

Charles  was  born  on  March  10,  1922  and  prepared
for  college  at  Wm.  H.  Hall  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1940  to  May,  1942.  His
permanent  address  is  49  Montclair  Drive,  West
Hartford,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is
Seaman  1st  C.,  595-482,  U.S.C.G.  “30119  F.’  Coastal
Lookout  Station,  Perth  Amboy,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Employed  by  Arrow-Hart  and  Hegeman  Electric  Co.,  June-December,  1942.  Enlisted
U.  S.  Coast  Guard,  October  1,  1942.  Called  to  active  service,  December  7,  1942.  Boot
training  at  Curtis  Bay,  Maryland.  Transferred  to  Fort  McHenry,  Baltimore,  Maryland.
Transferred  to  Jersey  City  Encampment.  Transferred  to  Coastal  Lookout  Station,
Perth  Amboy,  New  Jersey.  Became  engaged  to  Doris  L.  Clark,  Wethersfield,  Connecti¬
cut,  August,  1942.  Married  at  Wethersfield  Congregational  Church,  September  25,  1943.

EDWIN  I).  URQIJITART

Edwin  was  born  on  August  23,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Proctor  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1940  to  June,  1941.  His  permanent
address  is  76  Glen  Avenue,  Providence,  Rhode  Island.
His  temporary  address  is  Lt.  E.  D.  Urquhart,
0912510,  c/o  General  Delivery,  Yuma  Army  Air  Field,
Yuma,  Arizona.

Since  his  college  days:

He  enlisted  in  the  United  States  Army  Air  Forces  in  May,  1942,  and  left  for  Nashville,  Tennessee,  on  No¬
vember  1,  1942.  After  completion  of  his  basic  training  at  Nashville,  he  went  to  Maxwell  Field,  Alabama,
for  pre-flight  training  and  had  his  flying  training  at  Bennetsville,  South  Carolina,  Shaw  Field,  Sumter,
South  Carolina,  and  Spence  Field,  Moultrie,  Georgia.  Upon  receiving  his  wings  as  a  pilot  and  a  Second
Lieutenant’s  commission  at  Spence  Field,  he  received  transition  training  in  the  P-51  Mustang  fighter  and
went  overseas  early  in  January,  1944.  After  further  training  in  England,  in  March  he  was  assigned  to  the
Pioneer  Mustang  Group  of  the  Ninth  Air  Force.  This  group  has  recently  received  a  Presidential  citation
and  in  seven  months  of  combat  has  accounted  for  380  enemy  planes.  He  went  to  France  shortly  after  D-
day  and  in  July  was  promoted  to  First  Lieutenant  and  was  awarded  the  Air  Medal  with  first  and  second
oak  leaf  clusters  for  meritorious  achievement  in  combat  flights.

Editor’s  note:  He  now  has  the  DFC,  Presidential  Unit  Citation,  with  one  Oak  Leaf  Cluster  and  the  Air
Medal  with  eleven  Oak  Leaf  Clusters.  He  has  returned  to  this  country  as  an  Instructor.

LEDGER

NORMAN  B.  WENK,  JR.

Norman  was  born  on  November  27,  1922  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  Franklin  K.  Lane  High  School.
He  attended  Nichols  from  September,  1940  to  June,
1942.  His  permanent  address  is  8533  Forest  Park¬
way,  Woodhaven,  New  York.  His  temporary  ad¬
dress  is  U.S.N.T.C.,  Miami,  Florida.

Since  his  college  days:

He  enlisted  as  an  apprentice  seaman  in  the  U.  S.  Coast  Guard  June  15,  1942,  and  was
made  a  Yeoman,  second  class,  April,  1943.  In  June,  1943,  he  was  sent  to  Tufts  College
where  he  took  a  V-12  course.  He  graduated  from  this  course  at  Tufts  in  May,  1944.
He  was  advised  to  get  a  discharge  from  the  Coast  Guard  and  enlist  in  the  Navy.  He
did  this  right  after  graduating  from  Tufts  College.  After  spending  about  a  month  at
Asbury  Park  U.S.N.T.  school,  he  was  sent  to  Northwestern  University  at  Chicago  for
LEDGER  an  indoctrination  course.  He  was  graduated  from  Northwestern  University  as  an  Ensign

in  the  U.S.N.,  September  14,  1944.  He  was  married  September  16,  1944.  He  expects
to  be  placed  on  a  ship  after  two  months  further  training  at  U.S.N.T.C.,  Miami,  Florida,
where  he  now  is,  September  27,  1944.

HARVEY  R.  WOOLF

Harvey  was  born  on  December  26,  1921  and  pre¬
pared  for  college  at  Southside  High,  Elmira,  New
York.  He  attended  Nichols  from  January,  1941  to
March,  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  814  Maple
Avenue,  Elmira,  New  York.  His  temporary  address
is  Harvey  R.  Woolf,  S.O.M.  2/c,  USS  Beale,  c/o
F.P.O.,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Harvey  Woolf  left  school  in  his  Sophomore  year  to  join  the  Navy.  After  his  boot  train¬
ing  at  Newport,  Rhode  Island,  he  studied  Radar  at  Key  West.  He  was  then  assigned  to
a  destroyer  and  after  three  months  Atlantic  duty,  went  to  the  Pacific  where  he  has  been
for  the  last  sixteen  months.  He  married  his  college  and  high  school  chum,  Betty  Smith,
who  now  resides  in  San  Francisco,  waiting  like  so  many  other  wives,  for  his  ship  to  come
in.  He  plans,  upon  his  discharge  from  the  Navy  to  join  the  selling  force  of  Harris,  Mc¬
Henry  &  Baker,  a  lumber  concern  in  Elmira,  where  he  served  a  prewar  apprenticeship.

DOUGLAS  WOODRUFF,  JR.

Douglas  was  born  on  June  22,  1922  and  prepared  for
college  at  Proctor  Academy.  He  attended  Nichols
from  September,  1940  to  August,  1942.  His  perma¬
nent  address  is  4  Fitch  Avenue,  Auburn,  New  York.
His  temporary  address  is  1216  East  Central  Avenue,
Balboa,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

Immediately  after  graduating,  Doug  enlisted  in  the  United  States  Maritime  Service
and  was  sent  to  Gallups  Island,  Massachusetts,  for  training  as  a  radio  operator.  Upon
completion  of  the  course,  he  was  ordered  to  the  port  of  Los  Angeles,  from  which  he
shipped  on  a  tanker  carrying  high-test  gasoline.  He  transferred  this  last  summer  to  one
of  the  largest  tankers  launched  on  the  West  Coast  and  is  now  somewhere  in  the  Pacific.
On  July  10,  1943,  Doug  was  married  to  Vivienne  Verdery,  of  Warrington,  Rhode  Island.

WAR

LEDGER

FREDERICK  PARKER  YOUNG

Frederick  was  born  on  January  21,  1923  and  prepared
for  college  at  Brookline  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1940  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is
6  Emerson  Street,  Brookline,  Massachusetts.  His
temporary  address  is  Pvt.  Frederick  P.  Young,
31469250,  106th  MP  Platoon,  APO  443,  c/o  Post¬
master,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

From  June,  1942,  for  two  years,  Fred  was  employed  by  M.  I.  T.  through  the  Division
of  Industrial  Co-operation  as  assistant  in  charge  of  a  section  of  their  accounting  depart¬
ment.  Completed  second-year  course  at  The  Bentley  School  of  Accounting  and  Finance.
Served  for  six  months  in  the  U.  S.  Coast  Guard  Temporary  Reserve.  Fred  went  into
service  June  6,  1944,  and  was  sent  to  Fort  Mead  in  Virginia.  In  November,  he  went
overseas  to  Italy,  where  he  did  Personnel  work.  He  then  went  to  Germany,  Belgium,
and  France,  and  is  now  back  in  Germany.

Class  of  1943

WARD  TIFFANY  ALLING,  II

WAR

LEDGER

Ward  was  born  on  May  8,  1923  and  prepared  for
college  at  Bulkeley  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1941  to  November,  1942.
His  permanent  address  is  523  Ocean  Avenue,  New
London,  Connecticut.  His  temporary  address  is  3658
Warder  Street,  Washington  10,  D.  C.

Since  his  college  days:

Ward  entered  the  temporary  reserve  of  the  Coast  Guard  on  November  6,  1942,  and  the
Coast  Guard  Reserve  on  December  14,  1943.  For  two  years  he  was  stationed  in  New
London,  Connecticut,  with  the  Captain  of  the  Port  Detail  except  for  the  interval  he
spent  at  the  Northport  District  Training  School  in  Northport,  Long  Island.  In  Septem¬
ber,  1944,  he  was  transferred  to  Headquarters,  Washington,  D.  C.  On  October  22,  1944,
he  was  joined  in  matrimony  to  Miss  Barbara  L.  Jones  of  his  home  town,  New  London.
Mrs.  Ailing  graduated  from  Connecticut  College  for  Women.

RICHARD  WARREN  AVERY

Richard  was  born  on  March  15,  1923  and  prepared
for  college  at  Framingham  High  School.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  1941  to  1943.  His  permanent
address  is  81  Beech  Street,  Framingham,  Massa¬
chusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  384th  Fighter
Squadron,  364th  Fighter  Group,  S.P.O.  557,  c/o
Postmaster,  New  York,  New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Dick  graduated  from  Nichols  on  March  1,  1943,  and  immediately  left  for  Fort  Devens,
having  enlisted  in  the  Army  Reserve  in  November,  1942.  After  being  accepted  in  the
Army  Air  Corps,  he  spent  five  weeks  at  Keesler  Field  before  going  to  Administration
School  at  Sam  Houston  College  in  Texas.  Upon  graduation  Dick  was  sent  to  Cali¬
fornia  for  seven  months,  stationed  at  various  bases  before  returning  East  and  going
overseas  in  January,  1944.  At  this  writing  he  is  a  Corporal  with  a  P-38  Squadron  in
the  8th  Air  Force  at  a  base  in  England.  After  the  war  is  over,  Dick  hopes  to  continue
his  education.

r

JOHN  W.  BARTEMUS

John  was  born  on  August  5,  1922  and  prepared  for
college  at  Concord  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1942  to  1943.  His  permanent  address
is  5  Pine  Street,  Concord,  New  Hampshire.  His
temporary  address  is  2nd  Lt.  John  W.  Bartemus,
United  States  POW,  No.  5080,  Stalag  Luft  1,  Ger¬
many.

Since  his  college  days:

John  entered  U.  S.  Army  Air  Corps,  September,  1942,  and  was  classified  as  an  navigator.
He  trained  at  Selman  Field,  Monroe,  Louisiana,  and  graduated  April  10,  1943.  He
received  his  final  training  at  Dalhart,  Texas.  At  Scott  Field,  Illinois,  he  and  his  crew
picked  up  their  new  bomber,  B17-G,  flying  east  toward  their  hopping  off  place  in  New¬
foundland.  After  spending  a  week  there,  on  across  the  North  Atlantic  to  Britain.  I
received  a  telegram  from  the  War  Department,  January  13th,  that  John  was  reported
missing  in  raid  over  Germany,  December  30,  1943.  Nothing  more  was  heard  of  John
until  October  10.  I  was  notified  by  the  War  Department  that  John  was  a  prisoner  of  the
German  government.  Received  a  card  from  John  November  2nd,  saying  he  was  in  the
best  of  health,  treated  very  well,  and  not  to  worry  any  more  and  to  “keep  the  home  fires
burning.”

HAC

LEDGER

GEORGE  WARREN  BELL

George  was  born  on  August  30,  1920  and  prepared
for  college  at  Newton  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  September,  1941  to  January,  1943.
His  permanent  address  is  218  Mill  Street,  Newtonville,
Massachusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  Pfc
George  W.  Bell,  ASN  11067437,  27th  Ord.  Co.  M.M.,
APO  201,  c/o  Postmaster,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

He  enlisted  in  the  Army  Reserve,  July,  1942,  immediately  after  the  opening  semester
of  his  senior  year  at  Nichols  and  was  deferred  until  he  was  graduated  in  January,  1943.
He  was  inducted  into  the  army  at  Fort  Devens  on  February  5th,  1943,  later  proceeded
to  Camp  Wolters,  Texas,  where  he  received  basic  training  in  infantry  tactics,  remaining
there  until  October  when  he  proceeded  to  the  Pacific  Coast  for  transfer  to  the  southwest
Pacific,  where  he  served  in  Australia,  New  Guinea,  and  presently  with  a  top  division
in  the  Admiralty  Islands,  where  he  has  been  since  their  invasion  and  capture  from  the
Japanese  in  March  of  1944.  He  is  with  an  Ordnance  outfit  and  probably  doing  detail
work,  for  which  Nichols  helped  him  qualify.

IJED6EL

Since  his  college  days:

While  at  college  he  enlisted  in  the  Army  Air  Corps,  but  graduated,  and  after  graduation
he  worked  at  Ruthraff  &  Ryan,  Advertising  Agency,  until  he  was  called  up  in  March,
1943.  Received  his  basic  training  as  an  Air  Cadet  at  Atlantic  City,  from  there  to  Uni¬
versity  of  Vermont,  to  Maxwell  Field,  Montgomery,  Alabama,  and  has  been  stationed
at  various  fields  in  the  South.  He  has  just  received  reassignment  to  Lowry  Field,
Denver,  Colorado.

WILLIAM  STORY  BONSTEDT

William  was  born  on  October  5,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Cranbrook.  He  attended  Nichols
from  1941  to  1942.  His  permanent  address  is  111
East  80th  Street,  New  York,  New  York.  His  tem¬
porary  address  is  Lt.  Wm.  S.  Bonstedt,  8th  Photo
Tech.  Sqdn.,  APO  634,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,
New  York.

Since  his  college  days:

Graduated  from  School  of  Photography,  New  York.  Enlisted  in  Army  Air  Corps,  Octo¬
ber,  1942.  Worked  for  PIX,  Inc.,  while  waiting  call  to  service.  Trained  three  months
at  Boca  Raton,  Florida,  and  sent  to  New  Haven,  where  he  was  commissioned  as  2nd
Lieutenant  in  the  Air  Corps.  Then  assigned  to  Peterson  Field  at  Colorado  Springs,  Colo¬
rado.  From  there  to  an  assignment  at  Will  Rogers  Field  at  Oklahoma  City,  Oklahoma.
From  there  to  Air  Intelligence  School  at  Harrisburg,  Pennsylvania,  and  Camouflage
School  at  Walterboro,  South  Carolina,  then  overseas  to  England.  Is  now  1st  Lieutenant
in  the  8th  Air  Force.

ALBERT  EDWARD  BOUVIER

Albert  was  born  on  February  12,  1921  and  prepared
for  college  at  Mary  E.  Wells  High  School.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  1941  to  1943.  His  permanent
address  is  277  South  Street,  Southbridge,  Massa¬
chusetts.  His  temporary  address  is  L.S.T.  625,
c/o  Fleet  Post  Office,  San  Francisco,  California.

Since  his  college  days:

A1  joined  the  V-12  program  of  the  Navy  in  May  of  1942  and  was  allowed  to  continue
his  studies  at  Nichols  until  graduation  in  1943.  He  was  then  sent  to  Tufts  College  in
Medford,  Massachusetts,  to  continue  in  the  V-12  program,  where  he  stayed  until  Febru¬
ary,  1944,  and  was  then  sent  to  Midshipman  School  at  Plattsburg,  New  York,  from
which  he  was  commissioned  as  Ensign  in  the  U.S.N.R.  on  June  27,  1944.  He  was  mar¬
ried  at  Plattsburg,  New  York,  on  the  same  day  that  he  was  commissioned,  to  Evelyn
Kollette,  of  Uxbridge,  Massachusetts.  He  received  orders  to  report  aboard  ship  on
July  7,  1944,  at  New  Orleans,  and  is  now  serving  as  a  deck  officer  on  LST  No.  625.

JOSEPH  C.  BRADY

Joseph  was  born  on  July  25,  1921  and  prepared  for
college  at  Governor  Dummer  Academy.  He  at¬
tended  Nichols  from  September,  1941  to  January,
1943.  His  permanent  address  is  300  Lydecker  Street,
Englewood,  New  Jersey.

Since  his  college  days:

He  signed  up  with  the  Enlisted  Reserve  in  August,  1942,  and  entered  the  Army  in  Febru¬
ary,  1943,  after  graduating  from  Nichols  College.  He  trained  in  the  infantry  at  Camp
Wheeler,  Georgia,  and  went  overseas  as  a  private  in  June,  1943.  He  was  through  North
Africa  and  in  the  campaign  in  Sicily.  He  was  killed  in  Salerno  on  September  15,  1943.
The  War  Department  awarded  him  the  Purple  Heart.

THOMAS  MELVIN  COOKE,  2ND

Thomas  was  born  on  June  4,  1920  and  prepared  for
college  at  Hebron  Academy,  Hebron,  Maine.  He
attended  Nichols  from  September,  1941  to  May,
1943.  His  permanent  address  is  552  Main  Street,
Haverhill,  Massachusetts.

Since  his  college  days:

After  graduation  I  spent  the  summer  in  Maine.  In  the  fall  I  started  working  for  a  local
civil  engineer,  as  rod  man.  I  liked  the  outdoor  work  and  thought  I  would  make  engi¬
neering  my  life’s  work.  About  as  soon  as  I  made  this  decision  I  nearly  crippled  myself
for  life.  The  axe  slipped  and  I  chopped  my  ankle  and  was  laid  up  for  weeks.  Then  I
took  civil  service  and  got  an  appointment  as  a  military  substitute  in  the  Haverhill  HAI

post-office.  This  changed  my  draft  status  from  4-F  to  2 -A.  I  am  doing  my  father’s  |  |  |  ^  |  |

advertising  in  my  spare  time.  No  doubt  this  will  be  my  full  time  job  after  the  war.  I
am  not  married.  Nothing  exciting  has  happened  since  I  left  Nichols,  I  am  just  the  same
Tom  Cooke.

FRANK  BARTON  COOPER

Frank  was  born  on  November  15,  1922  and  prepared
for  college  at  Montclair  High  School.  He  attended
Nichols  from  1941  to  1943.  His  permanent  address
is  69  Brunswick  Road,  Cedar  Grove,  New  Jersey.
His  temporary  address  is  Sgt.  Frank  B.  Cooper,
11067520,  451st  Bomb  Gioup,  726th  Bomb  Squadron
(H),  APO  520,  c/o  Postmaster,  New  York,  New
York.

Since  his  college  days:

Sgt.  Frank  Barton  Cooper,  son  of  Mr.  Walter  W.  Cooper,  68  Brunswick  Road,  Cedar
Grove,  New  Jersey.  After  graduation  from  Nichols  College  he  enlisted  in  the  Army  on
February  3,  1943.  He  was  assigned  to  the  Ordinance  Department  of  the  Air  Force  and
attended  Ordinance  Supply  School  at  Los  Angeles,  California.  He  is  now  stationed  with
the  15th  Air  Force  based  in  Italy.  Last  December  Sgt.  Cooper  applied  for  Aerial  Gun¬
nery  and  was  assigned  to  the  position  of  Tail  Gunner  on  a  B-24  Liberator.  He  has  made
more  than  thirty-seven  Combat  Missions.
